b'Doncaster Belles used to be women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer royalty, champions of England and a fixture in the F.A. Cup final. Now, as investment floods into the women\xe2\x80\x99s game, a new history is being written without them. '
b'CreditCreditAndrew Testa for The New York Times'
b'Supported by'
b'By Rory Smith'
b'ROSSINGTON, England \xe2\x80\x94 Over the years, Sheila Edmunds has done pretty much everything for the Doncaster Belles. Half a century ago, she was among the group of friends who founded the club. For 25 years, she wore the team\xe2\x80\x99s No. 8 jersey and, for a while, its captain\xe2\x80\x99s armband.'
b'When she retired, she filled in wherever required: welfare officer, first-aid practitioner, physiotherapist. Now her official title is president and general manager. If that sounds like an executive role, an honorary sinecure, it is not.'
b'An hour or so before a game at the windswept stadium that the Belles now call home, Edmunds can be found in the simple wooden cabin that passes for a ticket office. At her back is an electric heater, on futile full blast to stave off the bitter cold. She welcomes fans handing over the \xc2\xa35 entrance fee warmly, as if each one is an old friend.'
b'In quiet moments, she might help out at the trestle table that serves as the Belles\xe2\x80\x99 merchandising arm. After kickoff, she keeps one eye on the game as she totals up the day\xe2\x80\x99s takings; it is easier this way, she says. She is the one, after all, who will have to enter it all into the club\xe2\x80\x99s accounts later.'
b'There is more money in women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer in England than there has ever been. Last summer, the country\xe2\x80\x99s highest tier \xe2\x80\x94 the Women\xe2\x80\x99s Super League (W.S.L.) \xe2\x80\x94 became, for the first time, fully professional, with a broadcasting arrangement with the BBC. England\xe2\x80\x99s biggest clubs, including Manchester City, Chelsea and Arsenal, all have invested heavily in their women\xe2\x80\x99s teams in recent years, spending not just on homegrown players but for high-profile imports, too. Manchester United, even, has finally joined the fray: It launched its women\xe2\x80\x99s team, in the second-tier Championship, last year, and immediately set about recruiting an all-star roster.'
b'The effect has been seismic, not just in terms of results \xe2\x80\x94 Manchester City reached the Champions League semifinals the last two seasons and England\xe2\x80\x99s national team finished third in the 2015 Women\xe2\x80\x99s World Cup \xe2\x80\x94 but in terms of interest, too. More than 45,000 people attended last season\xe2\x80\x99s women\xe2\x80\x99s F.A. Cup final, and two million more watched it live on television.'
b'Little or none of that growth, though, has found its way to Doncaster; or, more accurately, Rossington, a small village on the outskirts of the town, where Doncaster Rovers Belles play their home games in the third tier of English women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer.'
b'Crowds rarely number much more than a hundred here. There are no television cameras. Last summer, the club\xe2\x80\x99s biggest sponsor walked away; its income now does not stretch far beyond the cash Edmunds sifts through in front of that electric heater.'
b'And yet this is the team that has, arguably, done more for women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer in England than any other, a club that was synonymous with the sport for decades. In the 1980s and early 1990s, long before the professional clubs showed any interest in women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer, the Belles were its pre-eminent force.'
b'Between 1983 and 1994, the Belles reached 11 of 12 women\xe2\x80\x99s F.A. Cup finals, and won the trophy six times. The team won the first ever women\xe2\x80\x99s national league title, in 1992, and regained the crown in 1994; it would finish as runners-up seven times in the following years.'
b'Back then, its players formed the backbone of the English national team. \xe2\x80\x9cAt one point, we had seven or eight players in the squad,\xe2\x80\x9d said Gillian Coultard, who spent 21 years playing for the Belles in the team\xe2\x80\x99s heyday, and picked up 119 appearances for England. For a long time, she was one of five players to have made a century of appearances for her country. The others were Bobby Moore, Bobby Charlton, Peter Shilton and Billy Wright. \xe2\x80\x9cIt was a good quiz question,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'Doncaster, of course, was proud of the Belles: A small, tight-knit town on the edge of the South Yorkshire coalfield, it is not a place that attracts much national attention, or frequently enjoys much sporting success. The Belles changed that. \xe2\x80\x9cWe won so much,\xe2\x80\x9d Coultard said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe cup finals were on television. We felt like we represented Doncaster, and South Yorkshire. We kept the town at the pinnacle.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Edmunds remembers the club being asked to send representatives to have \xe2\x80\x9cafternoon tea with the Queen and Prince Philip\xe2\x80\x9d when they visited Doncaster. The players were guests of honor at the town\xe2\x80\x99s Mansion House, the ornate Georgian home of the local authorities, on several occasions.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe never had any sexist stuff,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cSouth Yorkshire people aren\xe2\x80\x99t like that. It\xe2\x80\x99s the sort of place where they acknowledge what people can do. They get behind you. There was a real pride at what we achieved.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'There was broader, cultural recognition, too. The writer Pete Davies spent a year with the team in the early 1990s; his subsequent book, \xe2\x80\x9cI Lost My Heart to the Belles,\xe2\x80\x9d coupled with the club\xe2\x80\x99s success, made the name famous. The playwright Kay Mellor used the book as source material for \xe2\x80\x9cPlaying the Field,\xe2\x80\x9d a BBC drama that ran for five seasons in the 1990s.'
b'To many, at a time when women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer received scant investment and commanded little attention, the Belles were the sport\xe2\x80\x99s most prominent face. \xe2\x80\x9cThey were the epitome of women\xe2\x80\x99s football,\xe2\x80\x9d said Mike Blackham. Like most of the people who go to watch the Belles now, Blackham and his wife, Jane, have a personal connection to the club: A friend plays for the first team.'
b'That is testament to how the club\xe2\x80\x99s horizons have retracted in recent years. As the fortunes of women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer have risen, those of the Belles have ebbed. \xe2\x80\x9cThe women\xe2\x80\x99s game has changed,\xe2\x80\x9d Edmunds said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is more financially driven. We have been left behind a little bit.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In 2013, when the Football Association, the sport\xe2\x80\x99s governing body in Britain, expanded the Women\xe2\x80\x99s Super League to two divisions, Doncaster Belles were demoted to the second tier and Manchester City\xe2\x80\x99s women\xe2\x80\x99s team \xe2\x80\x94 far younger but, crucially, aligned with a Premier League behemoth \xe2\x80\x94 were promoted in their stead. Vic Akers, then the manager of Arsenal Ladies, described the decision as \xe2\x80\x9cmorally scandalous.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Doncaster was promoted back to the top flight in 2015, but lasted only a season before being relegated again. It won the second division last year, its first trophy since 1994, but did not take up its place in the top tier: The F.A. had changed the licensing criteria, and the Belles \xe2\x80\x94 lacking a headline sponsor and a major men\xe2\x80\x99s team to bankroll the club \xe2\x80\x94 could not meet the new requirements. \xe2\x80\x9cFinancially, we could not do it,\xe2\x80\x9d Edmunds said.'
b'All but two members of the championship-winning side departed, many for Manchester United\xe2\x80\x99s new women\xe2\x80\x99s team. Neil Redfearn, the manager, left for Liverpool. The Belles decided against using the Keepmoat Stadium, the neat, modern venue that is home to Doncaster Rovers, the men\xe2\x80\x99s team with which they have a mostly symbolic alliance, and set up instead in Rossington, where the two stands are little more than a few steps covered by a roof. Smaller surroundings, Edmunds said, would not be as \xe2\x80\x9cdaunting\xe2\x80\x9d for the young players that now comprised the team.'
b'In Doncaster, the Belles\xe2\x80\x99 fame endures, and so does the affection and esteem in which they are held. Edmunds, for example, is well-known enough in the town that, a few years ago, when she was awarded an honor in London for her contribution to sport, the local paper afforded her the ultimate accolade: It referred to her by only her first name.'
b'Blackham, who coaches a local junior team, finds that while young boys dream of Premier League stardom, the girls tend to have a different ambition. \xe2\x80\x9cThey don\xe2\x80\x99t talk about playing for Manchester City or Chelsea or Arsenal,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cThey want to play for the Belles.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'There is some regret at the club\xe2\x80\x99s diminished status \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cthe demise of it is very sad, because it was so unique,\xe2\x80\x9d said Coultard \xe2\x80\x94 but there is no resentment of the game\xe2\x80\x99s authorities, no lingering anger at the Football Association for failing to curate the most famous women\xe2\x80\x99s team of all. \xe2\x80\x9cThat era has gone,\xe2\x80\x9d Edmunds said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe do not want people to forget that history, because so many people put so much into it, but we do not dwell on it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Instead, she said, she takes satisfaction in seeing all of the players who came through the club\xe2\x80\x99s ranks who have gone on to play professionally, to play in Europe, to play for their country.'
b'The golden age of the Belles may have come and gone, Edmunds said, but the club still has a role to play. \xe2\x80\x9cYou look at those players and think we must be doing something right,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe still contribute. There is real pride in that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Those Belles may be wearing different jerseys now, playing for different clubs, but they still bear the stamp of the club she helped to create. They all add a little more sheen to the legacy. In Edmunds\xe2\x80\x99s eyes, they are still Belles. \xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s what we have always said,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, turning back to the day\xe2\x80\x99s takings. \xe2\x80\x9cOnce a Belle, always a Belle.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'LONDON \xe2\x80\x94 The wreckage of the small plane carrying the Argentine soccer striker Emiliano Sala and his pilot, David Ibbotson, has been found on the seabed in the English Channel, a shipwreck hunter said on Sunday, days after parts of the aircraft\xe2\x80\x99s seat cushions were discovered on a French beach.'
b'The plane was found using an underwater drone that recorded video of the wreckage, including the body of one of the victims, the British government said on Monday. The video showed the aircraft registration number on the fuselage, confirming that it was the missing plane.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe families of Emiliano Sala and David Ibbotson have been notified by police,\xe2\x80\x9d David Mearns, the shipwreck hunter whose team had been searching for the Piper Malibu plane, said on Twitter.'
b'The families of Emiliano Sala and David Ibbotson have been notified by Police. The AAIB will be making a statement tomorrow. Tonight our sole thoughts are with the families and friends of Emiliano and David. #EmilianoSalas #NoDejenDeBuscarAEmilianoSala'
b'The single-engine, propeller-driven aircraft  disappeared over the English Channel after departing Nantes, a city in western France, at 8:15 p.m. local time on Jan. 21, headed for Cardiff, the capital of Wales.'
b'Mr. Mearns, a maritime scientist, told the British broadcaster Sky News on Sunday evening that the vessel \xe2\x80\x9cwas located earlier this morning by my crew onboard the Morven,\xe2\x80\x9d referring to the search ship FPV Morven. Mr. Mearns\xe2\x80\x99s company, Blue Water Recoveries, had been collaborating with the British Air Accidents Investigation Branch, or A.A.I.B., scanning the sea floor using sonar.'
b'A ship commissioned by the air accidents agency, the Geo Ocean III, launched a remotely operated vehicle, or R.O.V., to view the discovery at close range, the agency said in a statement on Monday.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cBased on analysis of R.O.V. video footage, the A.A.I.B. investigators on board the vessel concluded that the object is wreckage from the missing Piper Malibu aircraft, registration N264DB,\xe2\x80\x9d it said. The underwater drone \xe2\x80\x9ccarried out a further search of the area overnight, but did not identify any additional pieces of wreckage.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTragically, in video footage from the R.O.V., one occupant is visible amidst the wreckage,\xe2\x80\x9d the agency added, but it did not specify whether the body was Mr. Sala\xe2\x80\x99s or Mr. Ibbotson\xe2\x80\x99s. \xe2\x80\x9cThe A.A.I.B. is now considering the next steps, in consultation with the families of the pilot and passenger, and the police.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mr. Sala\xe2\x80\x99s family had commissioned a private search after the authorities ended their search of the Channel\xe2\x80\x99s surface and small islands on Jan. 24. David Barker, the harbormaster of the island of Guernsey, a self-governing British dependency off the coast of France, said in a statement at the time, \xe2\x80\x9cThe chances of survival at this stage are extremely remote.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mr. Sala, 28, a prolific goal scorer for Nantes in the French league, had recently been transferred to the Premier League club Cardiff City and was scheduled to practice with the Welsh team for the first time the next day.'
b'The flight went through rough, wintry weather over the Channel, and Mr. Sala left a voice message for friends and relatives saying that he was afraid that the plane would break apart.'
b'After the authorities ended their search, Romina Sala, Mr. Sala\xe2\x80\x99s sister, pleaded with the authorities not to call it off.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cPlease, please, please don\xe2\x80\x99t stop the search,\xe2\x80\x9d Ms. Sala said at a news conference in Cardiff, fighting back tears.'
b'She said she knew in her heart that Mr. Sala was still alive somewhere in the Channel.'
b'A Facebook message to Mr. Sala\xe2\x80\x99s sister seeking comment was not immediately answered on Sunday night.'
b'People from all over the world \xe2\x80\x94 including soccer stars like Kylian Mbapp\xc3\xa9, a member of the French national team that won the World Cup last year \xe2\x80\x94 chipped in to help the family\xe2\x80\x99s search.'
b'Sport Cover, a Paris-based soccer agency, started a GoFundMe page on Jan. 25 that by Sunday evening had raised more than 371,000 euros, about $424,000.'
b'Geo Ocean III departed Ostend, a coastal city in Belgium, on Sunday morning to begin a three-day underwater search, the A.A.I.B. tweeted. The search area was to cover about four square miles, according to the BBC.'

b'By Hannah Beech'
b'BANGKOK \xe2\x80\x94 The global sports market is worth hundreds of billions of dollars a year. Now, this powerful industry is coming together to promote an unlikely cause: human rights.'
b'Since late November, a Bahrain-born soccer player for a minor team in Australia has been held in detention in Thailand. The player, Hakeem al-Araibi, 24, is not a famous athlete. He has no lucrative sponsors.'
b'But he has spoken out against one of the most powerful men in international soccer, who is also a member of the ruling family of Bahrain. His testimony of torture at the hands of Bahrain\xe2\x80\x99s repressive government earned him refugee status in Australia, which determined that he faced credible threats of persecution should he return to the Gulf state.'
b'Still, over the past week, Mr. Araibi has collected an impressive list of supporters in the world of international sports.'
b'Fatma Samoura, the secretary general of FIFA, the international body governing global soccer, has called for Thailand to return him to Australia \xe2\x80\x9cas a matter of urgency.\xe2\x80\x9d So has Thomas Bach, the head of the International Olympic Committee, who raised the issue with the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees.'
b'On Tuesday, Praful Patel, a vice president of the Asian Football Confederation, issued a statement asking Prime Minister Prayuth Chan-ocha of Thailand to ensure Mr. Araibi\xe2\x80\x99s return to his adopted home.'
b'The head of the Asian Football Confederation is Sheikh Salman bin Ebrahim al-Khalifa, the Bahraini official whom Mr. Araibi accused of not stopping the persecution of athletes in his charge. Sheikh Salman also serves as a FIFA vice president.'
b'Such a collection of statements of support is rare, said Mary Harvey, the chief executive of the Center for Sports and Human Rights, which assembles governments, sports bodies, corporate sponsors and nongovernmental groups to ensure the role of human rights in sports.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHakeem is a historic test case, because it\xe2\x80\x99s the first time that we\xe2\x80\x99ve seen these big, powerful sports bodies all come together publicly to address the fate of a single person,\xe2\x80\x9d said Ms. Harvey, who was a member of the United States national soccer team and a FIFA executive.'
b'Sports has been buffeted by growing concerns about the hidden human costs of mega-events, like the Olympics and the World Cup, that have been used to bring international glory to authoritarian governments. Hundreds of foreign laborers, mainly from South Asia, have died in the building of stadiums and other infrastructure for the 2022 men\xe2\x80\x99s soccer World Cup in Qatar, according to the International Trade Union Confederation.'
b'Although the Qatari government has pledged to improve the rights of its migrant work force, some construction workers and foreign athletes continue to work in what is essentially indentured servitude, human-rights monitors say.'
b'Last year\xe2\x80\x99s hosting of the men\xe2\x80\x99s soccer World Cup by Russia was marred by racism and homophobia controversies. Both bids for the World Cup by Qatar and Russia were tarnished by a series of corruption scandals that cleared out a significant portion of FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s leadership ranks. With corporate sponsors nervous about a backlash from sports fans, FIFA unveiled a series of reforms aimed at bettering its human rights.'
b'In January, Brendan Schwab, the executive director of the World Players Association, which represents 85,000 professional athletes worldwide, wrote an urgent legal request on the \xe2\x80\x9csevere violation of the human rights\xe2\x80\x9d of Mr. Araibi, which was submitted to FIFA. The brief was also signed by unions representing professional soccer players.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHakeem\xe2\x80\x99s case is about a football player, it\xe2\x80\x99s about a human-rights defender, it\xe2\x80\x99s about a refugee and it\xe2\x80\x99s about global sport\xe2\x80\x99s ability to uphold its stated commitment to human rights,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Schwab said.'
b'Although FIFA now has binding human-rights policies, they are largely untested. Even though FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s human rights advisory board was formed two years ago, the request on Mr. Araibi\xe2\x80\x99s behalf was the first time such a formal submission had been made.'
b'When Mr. Araibi traveled to Bangkok on Nov. 27 with his wife for a belated honeymoon, the Thai authorities were waiting for him at the airport.'
b'Initially, Thai officials said Mr. Araibi had been detained based on an Interpol request alerting the immigration authorities to fugitives of justice. But Interpol quickly lifted that request because such alerts, called red notices, are not supposed to apply to refugees.'
b'Nevertheless, Bahrain has formally asked Thailand for Mr. Araibi\xe2\x80\x99s extradition so he can return to face a 10-year prison sentence for a conviction in absentia on charges that he burned a police station, among other convictions.'
b'Last week, the extradition request was passed on to the Thai attorney general\xe2\x80\x99s office, said Busadee Santipitaks, a spokeswoman for the Thai Ministry of Foreign Affairs, meaning that Mr. Araibi\xe2\x80\x99s fate could be decided in a matter of days.'
b'Mr. Araibi was playing in a televised football match when the police station he was supposed to have attacked was burned. Bahrain has racked up thousands of questionable convictions related to its crushing of its Arab Spring movement in 2011, when hundreds of thousands of Bahrainis joined street protests, human rights groups say.'
b'Thailand, which has not signed an international convention on refugees, has a history of extraditing human rights defenders to countries they have fled, like China or Bahrain, where they are likely to face imprisonment or torture.'
b'In early January, however, a Saudi teenager who had flown to Bangkok and feared death from her family, avoided deportation and was eventually allowed to travel on to Canada, where she was granted asylum. Her release followed an outcry on social media.'
b'In 2016, Sheikh Salman, who has refused to answer questions about Mr. Araibi\xe2\x80\x99s detention in Thailand, ran for the FIFA presidency. But his front-runner status diminished in part because of questions raised about Bahrain\xe2\x80\x99s record of imprisoning protesters, including members of the national soccer team.'
b'Instead, Gianni Infantino, who was born in Switzerland, won the top job. Both Mr. Infantino and Sheikh Salman are up for re-election to their respective posts this year.'
b'Running for the first time for a vice-presidential post in the Asian Football Confederation is Somyot Poompanmoung, the leader of the Football Association of Thailand. A former national police chief, Mr. Somyot faced a scandal last year after it emerged that he had received large loans from a fugitive brothel owner implicated in human trafficking.'
b'Thailand has mulled the possibility of jointly bidding for the World Cup in 2034 with another Southeast Asian nation. After the tainted bids by Russia and Qatar, updated FIFA guidelines now require that human rights be considered as a factor in deciding which country wins the right to host the prestigious tournament.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSports, like the Olympics and football, should and can bring social change,\xe2\x80\x9d said Craig Foster, a former captain of the Australian national soccer team who has lobbied on Mr. Araibi\xe2\x80\x99s behalf.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99ve got to hold governments accountable and say, \xe2\x80\x98If you want the great honor of hosting these major sports tournaments, then you have to accept global human rights standards,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'

b'By Victor Mather'
b'For the most part, Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s results from Serie C, the third level of Italian soccer, look like those of any other league around the world: Albissola 1, Arezzo 2. Alessandria 0, Arzachena 1. Cuneo 20, Pro Piacenza 0.'
b'Wait, what?'
b'That eye-popping score, and it\xe2\x80\x99s not a typo, is part of a larger tale. Pro Piacenza 1919 is a venerable team from the Emilia-Romagna region of Italy. But the team has run into financial troubles, and most of its players and staff members, sick of not getting paid, walked out weeks ago.'
b'The team was penalized 8 points by the federation, dropping it to the rock bottom of the standings, and forfeited three straight matches.'
b'One more forfeit and the team could be disqualified from the league.'
b'So for Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s visit to Cuneo, it was imperative that some kind of team be produced. Pro Piacenza, known as the Rossoneri, or Redblacks, scrambled. It mustered up some teenagers from the youth team, and a team masseur, for a total of eight players. The masseur\xe2\x80\x99s number was hastily added to his uniform with tape. One of the youngsters, Nicola Cirigliano, was appointed the player-manager.'
b'Unfortunately one of the players, identified by the Italian press as Isufi, had forgotten his ID card and could not suit up, leaving the team with just seven players, the minimum allowed before an automatic forfeit.'
b'The game progressed as you would expect with seven inexperienced players going against 11. Cuneo passed at will, dribbled at will, and more or less scored at will. A highlight video is great viewing if you enjoy discouraged players trudging back to the center circle after yet another goal. Cuneo went into the break up by 16-0.'
b'Good news for Pro Piacenza: Isufi\xe2\x80\x99s father retrieved his identifying documents, allowing him to join the game. Bad news for Pro Piacenza: the masseur had to leave the game with a cramp.'
b'In the end, Cuneo let up a bit, leading to the 20-0 final score.'
b'Hicham Kanis wound up with six goals, Edoardo Defendi had five, and hat tricks by Francesco De Stefano and Michele Emmausso were almost unnoticed.'
b'To be clear, although Serie C is a far cry from Juventus, the Milan giants and the high-quality play of Serie A, it is still a fully organized soccer league.'
b'Pisa, in the same division as Pro Piacenza, draws an average of 5,000 fans a game. The winner of the division will head up to Serie B, only a level below the likes of Ronaldo, Paulo Dybala and Ciro Immobile.'
b'But several teams at this level have struggled financially, among them Cuneo, the winning team Sunday. Matera has missed four matches and been disqualified.'
b'The Italian press did not like what it saw.'
b'La Gazzetta dello Sport called the match grotesque, \xe2\x80\x9cone of the saddest and surreal pages of Italian professional football.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Even a player on the winning side was embarrassed. \xe2\x80\x9cI feel only shame for those who made all this possible,\xe2\x80\x9d Fabiano Santacroce said.'
b'Francesco Ghirelli, the Serie C president, told Radio Rai that a game like that \xe2\x80\x9cmust never happen again.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'And on Monday he made sure it wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t: Lega Pro, the governing body for Serie C, announced on Monday that Pro Piacenza had been kicked out of the league.'

b'Supported by'
b'On Soccer'
b'By Rory Smith'
b'The trick, with Aurelio De Laurentiis, is to sit and to wait. He tends to take the scenic route through a conversation; his answers come wrapped in anecdotes and parables, laced with riddles and rhetorical questions.'
b'There are times when you wonder if he has taken one detour too many, become so distracted by his own tangents that he has lost his thread. Listening back, it is hard to pinpoint how, exactly, a question about the Champions League\xe2\x80\x99s revenue distribution leads to a brief but powerful homily about the dangers of the \xe2\x80\x98Ndrangheta, the Calabrian mafia, but it does.'
b'It is, though, no great ordeal. De Laurentiis might be most famous now as owner of S.S.C. Napoli, the Italian soccer team he rescued from oblivion and painstakingly restored to Europe\xe2\x80\x99s head table, but he is still, at heart, a film producer, a showman. He knows how to weave together a story, how to craft a compelling pitch. And when he gets to his destination, as he always does, it is invariably worth it.'
b'De Laurentiis is, after all, never knowingly short of ideas on how to revolutionize soccer, never without a sacred cow to slaughter, never without a tradition to overhaul. He has, at various times in the recent past, suggested cutting games from 90 minutes to 60 and advocated the effective abolition of UEFA, European soccer\xe2\x80\x99s governing body, instead handing power directly to Europe\xe2\x80\x99s biggest clubs.'
b'He is also never lacking an adversary, some villain standing in the way of progress, holding the game back through lack of imagination. His list has previously included not only UEFA but FIFA, Adidas, Nike, collective television deals and the Italian political establishment, among others. Many others.'
b'He does all this with a relish and a frequency befitting the scion of one of Italy\xe2\x80\x99s great cinematic dynasties. In his eyes, soccer (and life, most likely) is entertainment. Creating a stir comes naturally. It is all part of the show.'
b'Sitting in a hotel in Liverpool, England, in December, on the eve of what would turn out to be Napoli\xe2\x80\x99s final Champions League game this season, he did not require a vast amount of assistance, then, to land upon his current b\xc3\xaate noire.'
b'He would like, he said, to change the way prize money is handed out by the major leagues. He thinks underperformance should not be rewarded. Rather, he thinks it should be punished. \xe2\x80\x9cYou finish first, you get \xe2\x82\xac100 million, for example,\xe2\x80\x9d he says. \xe2\x80\x9cYou finish second, you earn \xe2\x82\xac50 million, and so on. But if you finish last, you pay a fine.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'This has been a recurrent theme for De Laurentiis this season. He has singled out Frosinone \xe2\x80\x94 a minor team from a town between Rome and Naples, promoted to Italy\xe2\x80\x99s top league, Serie A, for only the second time in its history last year \xe2\x80\x94 as an example of a club that arrives in the top flight \xe2\x80\x9calready relegated.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Clubs like Frosinone do not draw fans, or interest, or broadcasters to the league, De Laurentiis says. They come up, they do not try to compete, and they go back down, except with their coffers stuffed by what he sees as an unwarranted share of the division\xe2\x80\x99s television revenue.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe problem is the small teams have the same rights as the big ones,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, adding, with a reference to a type of bread: \xe2\x80\x9cWhy should Frosinone have a season in Serie A, be given a slice of the pagnotta and then be relegated back to the third division? If they cannot compete, if they finish last, they should have to pay a fine. They shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be given money for failing.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After yet another tangent in which he dismisses an overmatched club in a major league as a mere \xe2\x80\x9csparring partner,\xe2\x80\x9d he quickly builds up a head of steam. \xe2\x80\x9cPromotion and relegation is the biggest idiocy in soccer,\xe2\x80\x9d De Laurentiis says. \xe2\x80\x9cEspecially when you also have UEFA trying to force clubs to comply with financial fair play rules. Clubs should be structured geographically, so they can all be self-sufficient. If they cannot survive financially, if they cannot be self-sufficient, they should be booted out.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It would be easy to listen to De Laurentiis\xe2\x80\x99s words, to hear the many and varied ways in which he feels soccer has gotten things wrong, and to assume that he holds it in contempt, that he has wearied of the sport in the 15 years or so since he bought up what remained of Napoli \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cjust the name,\xe2\x80\x9d he has said previously \xe2\x80\x94 and set about reinvigorating it.'
b'His actions, though, are rather different. De Laurentiis is not distancing himself from soccer; rather, he is embedding himself more deeply in it. He has, for several years, been seeking to add another club to his portfolio; ideally, he would have liked one in London. \xe2\x80\x9cWe never found the occasion,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'He switched his attentions to the United States, investigating an offer to buy an expansion franchise in Major League Soccer. He spent months examining proposals in Baltimore, Detroit and Las Vegas, he said, but was put off by the cost of a team \xe2\x80\x94 more than $150 million, plus the cost of a new stadium, in the last expansion round.'
b'Then, in August, De Laurentiis received a phone call from the mayor of Bari, a port city in Apulia, down near Italy\xe2\x80\x99s boot heel. The local club, which played in Serie A as recently as 2011, had been declared bankrupt and had been relegated to the fourth tier of Italian soccer. The mayor offered De Laurentiis the chance to buy it.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI was surprised,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t know anyone in Bari. I have barely ever been there.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'More surprising still, however, is that De Laurentiis eventually said yes. Napoli and Bari are, strictly speaking, rivals, but suddenly the same family owned them: the older De Laurentiis in charge of the former, and his son, Luigi, given control of the latter.'
b'It was not, needless to say, a universally popular move. Though Bari\xe2\x80\x99s fans were broadly welcoming \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cThey saw we were serious people,\xe2\x80\x9d Aurelio De Laurentiis said \xe2\x80\x94 there was dissent in Naples. \xe2\x80\x9cGet out of our city,\xe2\x80\x9d read one banner, slung from railings in the city the night the Bari purchase was announced.'
b'De Laurentiis insists that owning another team will not draw his focus from his first love. \xe2\x80\x9cNapoli is Napoli, Bari is Bari,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. His son, meanwhile, is adamant that the expertise he and his father have gleaned on the Tyrrhenian coast now can be applied on the Adriatic.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe started from zero,\xe2\x80\x9d Luigi said of Bari. \xe2\x80\x9cWe had to create the brand, starting with a new crest, and then do all of the things necessary for a team: a season-ticket campaign, a website, the marketing, the social media, the jerseys, finding sponsors.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The rationale, the younger De Laurentiis said, is obvious. \xe2\x80\x9cBari has a national appeal; we are the only team in our division being broadcast nationally,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, the result of a partnership with the streaming service DAZN. Apulia itself has seen a boom in tourism in recent years; the opportunity, the younger De Laurentiis said, was too good to ignore.'
b'The plan, needless to say, is to restore Bari to the top flight, even if that would create a battle with the game\xe2\x80\x99s authorities over whether two teams in the same competition can have the same ownership.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cBari is a recognizable brand,\xe2\x80\x9d Luigi said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is not Frosinone. It has played in Serie A. It has a long list of famous former players.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It is not the sort of team, in other words, that Aurelio De Laurentiis would denounce as a sparring partner, a club whose only purpose is to pad out the standings and to pick up a paycheck. De Laurentiis might compulsively court controversy. He might prod and poke and provoke his rivals, and soccer\xe2\x80\x99s authorities. He might do it all in the name of entertainment. He is, though, as good as his word. Bari is putting his money where his mouth is. He thinks soccer needs to change. So he is trying to change it.'
b'Follow Rory Smith on Twitter: @RorySmith.'

b'By Reuters'
b"(Reuters) - Jose Maria Marin, the former president of Brazil Football Confederation (CBF), has been banned for life and fined 1 million Swiss francs ($997,000) for taking bribes, the sport's governing body FIFA said on Monday."
b'Marin is currently serving a four-year sentence in prison a the United States after being convicted on corruption charges related to a bribery scandal at FIFA. He was also fined $1.2 million and ordered to forfeit $3.34 million.'
b"FIFA's investigation into Marin was linked with the awarding of contracts for the media and marketing rights to The South American Football Confederation (CONMEBOL), CBF and CONCACAF competitions in 2012-2015."
b'"In its decision, the adjudicatory chamber found that Mr Marin had breached art. 27 (Bribery) of the FIFA Code of Ethics and, as a result, banned him for life from all football-related activities (administrative, sports or any other) at both national and international level," FIFA said in a statement.'
b'Marin was among the first to stand trial over what U.S. prosecutors called a sprawling scheme involving payments of more than $200 million of bribes and kickbacks in exchange for marketing and broadcast rights for soccer matches.'

b'By David W. Chen and Marc Tracy'
b'As Rudy Meredith was inducted into the Connecticut Soccer Hall of Fame in January to honor his 24-year run as Yale women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer coach, he sprinkled his hallmark humor and humility throughout his remarks.'
b'He recounted how his wife was on the opposite sideline for the University of Hartford when they met in the early 2000s. And he saluted several people in the audience while repeatedly expressing \xe2\x80\x9cthankfulness,\xe2\x80\x9d recalled Bill Duffy, a middle school principal and soccer lifer who served as master of ceremonies.'
b'There was nothing in Mr. Meredith\xe2\x80\x99s words, Mr. Duffy said, \xe2\x80\x9cthat would refer to anything that was going on.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Despite Mr. Meredith\xe2\x80\x99s placid demeanor, people who knew him best had recently begun to detect changes in his behavior. He seemed to be more anxious. He appeared less enthusiastic about soccer, even before he resigned as Yale\xe2\x80\x99s coach in November. He paid little attention to recruiting. He played poorly in pickleball, a paddle sport he usually excelled at.'
b'In hindsight, those hints of stress and fatigue coincided with revelations that Mr. Meredith, 51, had been the linchpin of a sprawling federal investigation into corrupt college admissions schemes that exploded into public view this week.'
b'At the heart of the scandal was a consultant, William Singer, who took $25 million to help fix exam scores or fraudulently misclassify prospective students as recruited athletes to boost their chances of being admitted to elite colleges. But the person who led federal authorities to Mr. Singer, according to court papers filed on Tuesday, was Mr. Meredith.'
b'In a Boston hotel on April 12, 2018, Mr. Meredith solicited a $450,000 bribe from the parent of a prospective college student in exchange for saving a Yale soccer recruitment spot for his daughter. Mr. Meredith took $2,000 from the parent, and directed the parent to wire future payments to a bank account in Connecticut. But the F.B.I. was secretly recording the conversation, the charging documents said. Then six days later, the parent, who was working with the authorities, wired $4,000 to Mr. Meredith from a bank account in Boston that the F.B.I. controlled, giving the government evidence of wire fraud.'
b'With the authorities on to Mr. Meredith, he told them about a deal he had struck in November 2017, when Mr. Singer had introduced him to a man who wanted his daughter to attend Yale. Mr. Singer helped doctor the application to make it seem as though she was the co-captain of a prominent club soccer team in Southern California, even though she did not play at that level, according to the government documents. But Mr. Meredith told the admissions office he wanted to recruit her, and after she was admitted, Mr. Singer paid the coach $400,000.'
b'Late Friday, Yale released a statement in which it said one student involved in the scheme was admitted and is attending now, while the other was denied admission. In the statement, Peter Salovey, the university president, called the criminal actions \xe2\x80\x9can affront to our community\xe2\x80\x99s deeply held values of fairness, inclusion and honesty.\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Salovey said the university was starting an internal investigation into its admissions process.'
b'Prosecutors said on Tuesday that Mr. Meredith had agreed to plead guilty to wire fraud, honest services wire fraud and conspiracy to commit honest services wire fraud.'
b'Mr. Meredith did not respond to a request for comment. Paul Thomas, Mr. Meredith\xe2\x80\x99s lawyer, who works at a New Haven firm founded by Felice Duffy, a former Yale soccer coach who later became a federal prosecutor and lawyer, declined to comment.'
b'It was a dramatic fall for a man considered to be a Yale institution. Mr. Meredith started as an assistant coach in 1992, rose to head coach in 1995 and led the team to its first unshared Ivy League title in 2005.'
b'The charges blindsided virtually everyone who knew Mr. Meredith, according to interviews with more than a dozen former players and others connected to Yale or soccer. Mr. Meredith was generous and well liked, and did not appear to have any health, financial or personal problems.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m both appalled and sympathetic \xe2\x80\x94 I would never have thought that he was capable of doing this,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sharon Eisen, a veterinarian who became friendly with the Merediths in recent years through pickleball, in which Mr. Meredith is a national-level player and coach. \xe2\x80\x9cOn the one hand, I know them and like them personally. But on the other hand, I\xe2\x80\x99ve lost all respect. So greedy. So immoral.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mr. Meredith grew up modestly in the Rockville, Md., area, and was an all-state soccer player at Richard Montgomery High School. But he failed classes while at Montgomery College, and almost quit school. After undergoing tests at the urging of his coach and being found to have a learning disability, he turned his life around, and ultimately transferred to Southern Connecticut State. The university\xe2\x80\x99s men\xe2\x80\x99s soccer program was then a Division II powerhouse. Mr. Meredith played on the 1990 N.C.A.A. championship team, then embarked on a career coaching soccer and teaching physical education.'
b'Robert Kehoe, director of college programs for the National Soccer Coaches Association of America, said he first met Mr. Meredith in 1996 and worked closely with the Yale women\xe2\x80\x99s team for the next several years as part of a development workshop he used to conduct.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe had a lot of credibility because he was a very good player in his own right,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Kehoe said.'
b'Mr. Meredith quickly fostered an energetic atmosphere. He required players to wear costumes for Halloween practice. He bought bagels and extra food on his own dime for long bus rides to away games, while good-naturedly enduring the film \xe2\x80\x9cDirty Dancing\xe2\x80\x9d at his players\xe2\x80\x99 behest.'
b"Yale enjoyed success in the mid-2000s, with the 2005 team reaching the third round of the N.C.A.A. tournament, knocking out third-seeded Duke in the process. Mr. Meredith coached several Ivy League players of the year and an all-American second-teamer who was profiled by ESPN. Meredith Speck, class of 2015, was the first Yale player in the National Women\xe2\x80\x99s Soccer League, according to Yale's alumni magazine."
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe thing I remember is how professionally he treated us,\xe2\x80\x9d said Theryn Gibbons, who was a member of Meredith\xe2\x80\x99s first recruiting class in 1996 and now ranks third on Yale\xe2\x80\x99s scoring list. \xe2\x80\x9cRefs were calling me Babe, and Rudy was never like that \xe2\x80\x94 we were athletes. He was very respectful, very sensitive.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'If anything, Ms. Gibbons said, Mr. Meredith sometimes seemed intimidated by the aura of Yale, and tried hard to be liked.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s not sophisticated by any means, and I know he would defer to people who he thought were smarter,\xe2\x80\x9d said Ms. Gibbons, who later became a federal prosecutor. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s very trusting, and gullible for sure.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'She added, \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m not condoning what is alleged, but he\xe2\x80\x99s family, and you stand by family.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mr. Meredith\xe2\x80\x99s wife, Eva Bergsten Meredith, was also a familiar presence at Yale soccer events. A former national team player for Sweden, she is the longtime women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer coach at Wesleyan, and has also run, with her husband, Bulldog Cardinal soccer camp for many years.'
b'In 2013, in what former players said was an unusual move, the Yale women\xe2\x80\x99s coaching position itself was endowed in Mr. Meredith\xe2\x80\x99s name, thanks to an anonymous donation: For a time, Rudy Meredith was the Rudolph L. Meredith Head Coach of Women\xe2\x80\x99s Soccer. Even after Mr. Meredith\xe2\x80\x99s resignation in November, the name stuck: When Brendan Flaherty was hired as Mr. Meredith\xe2\x80\x99s replacement the next month, it was as the Loring Family and Rudolph L. Meredith Head Coach of Women\xe2\x80\x99s Soccer.'
b'Now, Mr. Flaherty is listed on Yale\xe2\x80\x99s website as simply the Loring Family coach. It was not immediately clear when or why Yale made the change. A university spokesman said Mr. Meredith was not involved in funding and naming the position.'
b'In recent years, Yale\xe2\x80\x99s teams did not perform as well as they had in the 2000s, and players and friends began to suspect that Mr. Meredith was no longer as gung-ho about soccer.'
b'Adele Jackson-Gibson, a Yale goalkeeper who graduated in 2013 and is now a freelance writer in Brooklyn, said she \xe2\x80\x9ccould feel people become more defeated over time.\xe2\x80\x9d She added, \xe2\x80\x9cPeople seem tired and a little bit checked out.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Some players, speaking on condition of anonymity so as not to be ensnared in the investigation, also began to notice a player or two, every couple of years, who did not belong on a Division I team, based on their skill level. Some of those players came from wealthy families, prompting speculation that their parents had donated money in exchange for coveted recruiting spots.'
b'In August 2017, the Merediths purchased a vacation home in Fernandina Beach, Fla., for $125,000, and took out a construction loan for $359,250, records show. The next month, Mr. Meredith was badly shaken, friends say, by the unexpected death of Fritz Rodriguez, a longtime assistant coach who had been Mr. Meredith\xe2\x80\x99s roommate and teammate in college. So his resignation in November 2018 did not come as a complete surprise to some.'
b'What few knew, of course, was that he had been cooperating with federal authorities for roughly half a year.'
b'A Yale spokesman said the university learned about the scheme and the federal investigation only after the announcement that he was leaving.'
b'Mr. Duffy, the M.C. at the Hall of Fame ceremony, summed up the feelings of many people close to Mr. Meredith when he said that he was still processing the gravity of the scandal.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIn the soccer community, we\xe2\x80\x99re saddened by Rudy\xe2\x80\x99s personal involvement, whatever that may be,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI think more people are angry that more deserving players were overlooked.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Katie Benner contributed reporting, and Susan C. Beachy contributed research.'

b'By Tariq Panja'
b'Over the past four years, some of the most damning secrets of the professional soccer industry have been exposed by a deluge of leaks that have shined an unflattering light on some of the sport\xe2\x80\x99s most popular clubs, players and coaches.'
b'Last week the man behind the leaks, a 30-year-old Portuguese citizen named Rui Pinto, was arrested in Budapest, Hungary. He faces extradition to his home country on the charges, which include an extortion attempt in 2015 on a secretive investment fund that had bet millions of dollars in the player transfer market.'
b'For the moment, though, Pinto\xe2\x80\x99s fate depends on a far narrower matter: whether his team of lawyers can successfully argue that he is a whistle-blower under Hungarian law \xe2\x80\x94 a defendant whose actions to expose malpractice and, potentially, a raft of financial and other crimes in soccer outweigh any offenses he might have committed.'
b'In the view of the Portuguese authorities, Pinto is guilty of extortion and violation of secrecy in relation to his contact with the investment fund, Doyen Sports. They and Doyen have accused him of threatening to publish internal company documents \xe2\x80\x94 revealing transfer fees and secret payments \xe2\x80\x94 unless the fund paid him to keep the documents private.'
b'Those documents, which offered a window into both Doyen\xe2\x80\x99s business model and its bank accounts, were later published on the website known as Football Leaks. The revelations, along with a number of player contracts posted on the site, exposed a murky world of soccer finance that was at best unsavory and at worst in violation of national and international soccer regulations.'
b'Ultimately, Pinto turned over about 70 million documents and 3.4 terabytes of information to a German newsmagazine, Der Spiegel, which shared documents with a select group of news media outlets who published reports on their contents.'
b'Now that Pinto has been arrested on a Portuguese warrant, his case represents a high-profile test of a Hungarian law passed in 2014 that affords special protection to whistle-blowers. His lawyers plan to argue that the leads his leaked documents provided to a variety of European law enforcement organizations outweigh Pinto\xe2\x80\x99s actions.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cBased on the leaks, there have been some extremely important criminal investigations opened with prosecutions in various countries,\xe2\x80\x9d said William Bourdon, Pinto\xe2\x80\x99s lawyer, who previously has represented the national-security whistle-blower Edward Snowden. \xe2\x80\x9cWithout Pinto, this wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have been possible.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Those investigations include several tax cases in Spain, where top soccer stars, including Cristiano Ronaldo, have been prosecuted for tax evasion after Football Leaks revealed details of the complicated structures through which they received millions of dollars in salaries and image rights. (Pinto\xe2\x80\x99s lawyers said that he also has been in contact with French financial crimes prosecutors since late 2016.)'
b'More recently, Football Leaks disclosures have targeted the FIFA president, Gianni Infantino, and the ways some top clubs might have circumvented the sport\xe2\x80\x99s financial regulations. The revelations also led to the reopening of a sexual assault case against Ronaldo.'
b'Unlike in most whistle-blower cases, however, Pinto has no official connection with the soccer industry \xe2\x80\x94 no access to clubs\xe2\x80\x99 books or a players\xe2\x80\x99 contracts \xe2\x80\x94 beyond being a fan of the game.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cFor me, it doesn\xe2\x80\x99t make a difference considering what is the basis of whistle-blower protection: the intensity of the contribution to the public interest,\xe2\x80\x9d Bourdon said. \xe2\x80\x9cThis is the key point.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Bourdon said Pinto already had agreed to assist the authorities in Switzerland, and that Germany\xe2\x80\x99s tax agency was seeking access to his information, too. But it is the decision of a Hungarian judge that matters most to him at the moment, since that will determine whether or not he avoids extradition to Portugal.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe expect the Hungarian judge to be sensitive to the paradoxical situation,\xe2\x80\x9d Bourdon said, \xe2\x80\x9cthat on one hand he\xe2\x80\x99s being prosecuted in Portugal, while on the other he has been providing assistance to prosecutors in other countries.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Bourdon said that he sees little difference between Pinto and one of his former clients, Herv\xc3\xa9 Falciani, who leaked account details of clients of the British bank HSBC while he worked in Geneva. Falciani\xe2\x80\x99s disclosures, which shook the secretive world of Swiss banking, revealed accounts containing more than $100 billion, and led to the bank\xe2\x80\x99s agreeing to pay 300 million euros (about $340 million) to French authorities to settle a tax-evasion investigation.'
b'Spain\xe2\x80\x99s high court last September rejected an extradition request for Falciani \xe2\x80\x94 once labeled the Edward Snowden of banking \xe2\x80\x94 from Switzerland.'
b'In addition to Pinto\xe2\x80\x99s extradition, the Portuguese police have demanded the entirety of the computer equipment seized from him in Hungary. Bourdon called that an overreach because their case is limited to the suspected 2015 extortion attempt.'
b'Bourdon acknowledged that Pinto had attempted to make contact with Doyen once he had the company\xe2\x80\x99s documents, but he said the extortion charges were not valid because Pinto ultimately \xe2\x80\x9cdidn\xe2\x80\x99t follow through\xe2\x80\x9d with an operation to secure a payment.'
b'Bourdon described the charges as \xe2\x80\x9ca tool to criminalize him, to target him as an offender and not a whistle-blower.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Little is known about Pinto. A Der Spiegel reporter, Rafael Buschman, is the only journalist known to have contact with an individual connected with Football Leaks. Buschman has written a series of breathless accounts and a book detailing his relationship with a man he referred to as \xe2\x80\x9cJohn.\xe2\x80\x9d Der Spiegel has not confirmed Pinto is its source.'
b'But a September report by the Portuguese magazine Sabado reported Pinto was the \xe2\x80\x9ccomputer genius\xe2\x80\x9d behind Football Leaks. Shortly after its article was published, a message was posted on Football Leaks\xe2\x80\x99 Facebook page that appeared to taunt Portuguese authorities, signing off with \xe2\x80\x9c#catchmeifyoucan.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In a video posted to websites including YouTube after a court appearance in Budapest last week, Pinto, dressed in a brown leather jacket and jeans, appeared relaxed as he sat on a wooden bench outside the courtroom with his hands cuffed in front of him. Pinto\xe2\x80\x99s lawyers managed to secure house arrest for him until the judge delivers a verdict.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cJurisprudence and regulations say there is a question of proportionality between the seriousness of the offense and the importance to public interest,\xe2\x80\x9d Bourdon said. \xe2\x80\x9cYou could violate the law, could be hacking, or stealing, and if the contribution is tremendous then it\xe2\x80\x99s not a crime.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt will be a historic decision for a Hungarian judge to make.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'Young players with dreams of glory think elite training programs lead to riches. They do. Just rarely for them.'
b'A training session at a semi-professional program in Rio de Janeiro in February.CreditCreditDado Galdieri for The New York Times'
b'Supported by'
b'By Tariq Panja and Manuela Andreoni'
b'RIO DE JANEIRO \xe2\x80\x94 Even in death the haggling went on.'
b'Christian Esm\xc3\xa9rio was going to be the one \xe2\x80\x94 his family had been sure of it.'
b'He was 15 and towering, a soccer player with an easy smile that belied his prowess between the goal posts. Already there was talk of contracts, and of buying a home for his parents, who had poured all their savings into the dream that their son might be the next great Brazilian soccer export \xe2\x80\x94 the next Ronaldo, Ronaldinho or Neymar.'
b'Now, his father stood in a daze of grief outside a Rio office building, surrounded by lawyers. Just days earlier, Christian had burned to death in a fire at the youth academy of one of South America\xe2\x80\x99s most famous soccer clubs, Flamengo. He was one of 10 players killed.'
b'The deaths lifted the veil over international soccer\xe2\x80\x99s biggest production line, and raised sweeping questions about a brutal apparatus that chews up untold numbers of young Brazilian boys for every star it mints.'
b'But for the moment, as lawyers sparred over how much money families of the players killed in the blaze should get, there was just one simple question: What was Christian worth?'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cDreams.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The word hung in the air as Rafael Stival let out a sigh.'
b'Mr. Stival\xe2\x80\x99s for-profit talent scouting operation had posted a note on Facebook mourning three of its graduates who had died in the fire at Flamengo. Since then, the messages had been pouring in.'
b'They were not condolences. The Facebook post had inadvertently acted as an advertisement \xe2\x80\x94 a signal to ambitious parents that Mr. Stival\xe2\x80\x99s organization could get their boys into not just any club, but the great Flamengo. They wanted Mr. Stival to give their boys a chance.'
b'The soccer world in Brazil is populated by a variety of actors, some drawn by glory, but almost all attracted by the chance of breaking out of poverty, maybe even striking it rich.'
b'There are the boys, of course, and their families. There are the investors and the middlemen like Mr. Stival, who trawl the continent-size country in search of prospects as young as 9. And there are the teams, many in a state of such financial disarray that only the sale of the latest star keeps them afloat.'
b'The profits from investing wisely, and early, in even a single player can run into the tens of millions of dollars.'
b'To many in the game, the industry has grown out of control. It has morphed from a system intended to develop promising players into an international market whose value is $7 billion a year, according to soccer\xe2\x80\x99s global governing body, FIFA. In this speculative environment, talented young athletes \xe2\x80\x94 some of them children \xe2\x80\x94 are bought and sold like any other raw material. In Brazil, the best ones are even referred to that way: as \xe2\x80\x9cgems.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'No one knows for sure how many boys are in Brazil\xe2\x80\x99s youth soccer system.'
b'There are no official figures. Estimates range from 12,000 to 15,000, but that is hard to corroborate. The Brazilian soccer federation makes no effort to track players until they turn 16 and become professionals.'
b'But one thing is known: On the night of the Flamengo fire, Feb. 8, more than two dozen boys \xe2\x80\x94 most from poor families, and all hoping to achieve a dream \xe2\x80\x94 were asleep in a club dormitory.'
b'In a country obsessed with soccer, Flamengo prides itself on being the most popular team, with wealth that is the envy of rivals across South America. But that adoration and power, it appears, may have allowed Flamengo to escape for years any real censure for the treatment of boys in its care.'
b'In 2015, Rio state prosecutors sued Flamengo over the conditions at its training center. The prosecutors cited child-protection failures, declaring the conditions to be \xe2\x80\x9ceven worse than those currently offered to juvenile delinquents.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'City officials issued an order closing the facility in 2017, but never carried it out, limiting their sanctions to dozens of fines.'
b'In recent years, Flamengo spent millions to upgrade its youth academy. Last year, club officials boasted that the new facilities would be the best in Brazil.'
b'But the dormitory holding 26 sleeping boys on the night of the fire was a makeshift structure, consisting of six steel containers fused together. It had never been inspected, according to local authorities.'
b'Interviews with survivors of the fire and officials who investigated it suggest that a series of failures may have contributed to the boys\xe2\x80\x99 deaths:'
b'\xe2\x80\x94 Federal regulations require at least one caretaker for every 10 boys, but there was no adult present at the time of the fire.'
b'\xe2\x80\x94 Survivors said the only exit from the dorm was at its far end. Some of the boys may have been in beds farther away from the exit than the 33-feet limit required by the regulations.'
b'\xe2\x80\x94 The rooms had sliding doors, another violation because they can jam.'
b'\xe2\x80\x94 And while each room had a window, the openings were covered with grates.'
b'One boy who was in Christian\xe2\x80\x99s room told investigators their door had stuck when he tried to get out. The boy managed to slide through the window grates. But Christian, a strapping 6-foot-3 goalkeeper, could not. When rescuers got to him, his body was so badly charred he could be identified only through dental records.'
b'Flamengo officials did not respond to interview requests. But in February, its president, Rodolfo Landim, denied knowing about any irregularities when he spoke at a news conference after the fire.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cOur goal is to solve this problem as quickly as possible,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'Soccer is hardly the only industry to attract Brazil\xe2\x80\x99s desperate.'
b'Sergio Rangel, a journalist who has covered the sport for three decades, says the youth-training system reminds him of the giant gold mine in Serra Pelada. The horrific conditions there were immortalized by the photographer Sebasti\xc3\xa3o Salgado in the 1980s.'
b'Desperately poor men from all over the country swarmed the mine\xe2\x80\x99s open pit, turning over rocks in the hope of finding the nugget that would change their lives.'
b'Soccer has also been a fool\xe2\x80\x99s gold of sorts for many families. Some of them move hundreds, even thousands of miles to enroll their sons in training programs that will sort, scrutinize and, more often than not, reject their child as worthless.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cPick one up, turn it over, and throw it away if it\xe2\x80\x99s no good,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Rangel said.'
b'The young men are not just disposable. To those who run the industry, they are often indistinguishable.'
b'That much was clear at a memorial for the 10 players who died at Flamengo. Midway through the service, a team official rushed to cover a large montage of photos of the boys: someone had realized that a player who survived had been mistakenly included.'
b'The streets of Xer\xc3\xa9m, about 50 kilometers outside Rio, teem with boys of various ages in red, green and white jerseys \xe2\x80\x94 the colors of the Fluminense soccer club.'
b'Until the team built its training complex there, Xer\xc3\xa9m was little more than a swamp, locals say. But now, despite the humid heat that tops 100 degrees Fahrenheit, it is home to players and families whose lives revolve around the club.'
b'Among them earlier this year was an 11-year-old nicknamed Maradoninha, for his resemblance to the former Argentine great Diego Maradona. Even in this hotly competitive town, Maradoninha was attracting attention.'
b'Two years ago, a talent scout from Fluminense saw the boy, whose real name is Leandro Gomes Feitosa, play in a local tournament and approached his family. The boy was only 9, and Brazilian law does not allow soccer clubs to house children under 14. But if the family could get to Rio, the scout said, Fluminense would train him.'
b' A group of local businessmen put up the money \xe2\x80\x94 for a cut of future proceeds \xe2\x80\x94 and the family moved more than 1,200 miles, from the town of Palmas to Xer\xc3\xa9m, to pursue the dream.'
b'Almost all the families living in their community of 26 rowhouses have a similar story, Maradoninha\xe2\x80\x99s father, Evandro Feitosa, said.'
b'Maradoninha may not be old enough for high school, but he knows his family\xe2\x80\x99s future is tied to his skills with a soccer ball. \xe2\x80\x9cGod willing,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ll become a big player to help my family in Palmas, my family here and those in need.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The chances of making it are slim. Fewer than 5 percent of the soccer prospects in Brazil will ever make it as professionals, by most estimates. Fewer still will earn a decent wage in the game. A study published by the Brazilian soccer federation in 2016 found that 82 percent of soccer players in the country earned less than 1,000 reais ($265) each month.'
b'And for Maradoninha and his family, the odds recently got even slimmer: Fluminense released him.'
b'Whatever the odds, whatever the hardship, there are enough soccer success stories to feed the hopes of young boys and families who have little else to aspire to.'
b'There is Neymar, so successful he is more international brand than player. He is the product of a humble neighborhood on the outskirts of S\xc3\xa3o Paulo. There are Rivaldo, Ronaldo and Rom\xc3\xa1rio, three former Brazilian World Cup winners, all awarded the title of best player in the world in their time by FIFA.'
b'And most recently, there is Vinicius Junior, a flashy forward who rose out of Flamengo\xe2\x80\x99s youth ranks. He once trained on the same fields as the 10 boys killed in the fire, and then he began living the dream: in 2017, when he was 16, Spain\xe2\x80\x99s Real Madrid agreed to pay 45 million euros (just over $50 million) for his rights after he played just 11 minutes in his debut game.'
b'All of those players, and hundreds more, have emerged from the Brazil\xe2\x80\x99s soccer mill to ply their trade on the world\xe2\x80\x99s biggest stages.'
b'In his early days in the sport, Christian\xe2\x80\x99s parents used all they had \xe2\x80\x94 and borrowed from friends and neighbors \xe2\x80\x94 to finance his soccer dream.'
b'He seemed to be getting closer to his own version of the soccer success story. On March 5, the day he turned 16, he was expected to sign his first professional contract at Flamengo. His dream, years in the making, was in reach.'
b'He died four weeks before that birthday.'
b'Days after his death, his father, Cristiano Esm\xc3\xa9rio, was standing outside an office tower in downtown Rio where public defenders were meeting with officials from Flamengo. He was with a group of lawyers. One turned to him.'
b"When it came to compensation, the lawyer said, it would be unfair if Christian's family was treated the same as the others. After all, he said, some of the dead boys had been recent arrivals to the club. But Christian was different: He had been called up to one of Brazil\xe2\x80\x99s youth national teams. Clearly he was worth more than the rest."
b'Esm\xc3\xa9rio nodded silently. He and his son had discussed money, too.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cDad, let\xe2\x80\x99s look for a house,\xe2\x80\x9d he recalls Christian saying when he got word that he was closing in on a professional contract. \xe2\x80\x9cMy first paycheck, I want to pay for a house for my mom, so she doesn\xe2\x80\x99t have to suffer because she doesn\xe2\x80\x99t have water or electricity.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'A week before he died, the boy posted a tribute to his family on Facebook. Above two pictures of father and son taken a decade apart, he made a promise:'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAll the sacrifice will be compensated, my old man.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'For decades, women\xe2\x80\x99s uniforms were just derivations of men\xe2\x80\x99s. Now, taking specific design cues, like ponytail-friendly necklines, comes the good stuff. '
b'By Vanessa Friedman'
b'The United States women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer team has been fighting for gender parity not just in the courts \xe2\x80\x94 suing the United States Soccer Federation last week for discrimination \xe2\x80\x94 but also in their uniforms, known as kits. And at least when it comes to the clothes and the Women\xe2\x80\x99s World Cup, they have won.'
b'On Monday, at a global event in Paris, Nike revealed the new home and away uniforms for 14 out of 24 competing teams, and for the first time since the brand began working with the WWC tournament in 1995, each one of them was made specifically for the women\xe2\x80\x99s teams, not as derivations or extensions of kits made for men. Three days before, to coincide with International Women\xe2\x80\x99s Day, Adidas released its new designs for four WWC teams.'
b'In the larger picture of gender issues and sports, this may not seem like a big deal. But the clothes athletes wear speak loudly about identity and allegiance, and have the power to help instill confidence. Clothes are also the easiest way for fans to assert their own allegiance, aspiration and personal connection. They are, above all, symbols. And now they are finally symbols of parity.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe are shifting more resources to women,\xe2\x80\x9d said Amy Montagne, the vice president for global categories at Nike \xe2\x80\x94 and not just because this is the largest number of teams the company has worked with. (It outfitted 11 clubs for the 2015 Women\xe2\x80\x99s World Cup.) But because, Mark Parker, the chief executive, said, \xe2\x80\x9cWe believe this summer can be another turning point for the growth of women\xe2\x80\x99s football.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Certainly, given Nike\xe2\x80\x99s current emphasis on women\xe2\x80\x99s sports \xe2\x80\x94 the Dream Crazier campaign, a series of new initiatives designed to support women\xe2\x80\x99s coaching and engage more girls \xe2\x80\x94 as well as its own experience with Serena Williams and the current focus on female dress in the competitive arena, it would have been fairly hypocritical for the company to treat its women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer kit as in any way secondary to men\xe2\x80\x99s. (Especially given Nike\xe2\x80\x99s own somewhat uncomfortable internal history with gender issues.)'
b'Yet it wasn\xe2\x80\x99t until 2015 that Nike began making women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer jerseys in men\xe2\x80\x99s sizes so that more male fans could buy them. And it wasn\xe2\x80\x99t until the players really spoke up that things began to change.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThree years ago they said, \xe2\x80\x98We want our own thing,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d Cassie Looker, the senior apparel product manager for global football, said in a call from France. \xe2\x80\x9cTheir own thing\xe2\x80\x9d refers to both fit and to the design of the uniforms, which Nike refers to as the \xe2\x80\x9cstorytelling.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'According to Ms. Looker, the fit took three years and multiple four-dimensional body mapping sessions of professional athletes to adjust. \xe2\x80\x9cThey are shaped differently than the standard body type,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cThey generate most of their power from their lower body.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'While male soccer players like a slimmer fit \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cIt makes them feel more powerful, like superheroes,\xe2\x80\x9d Ms. Looker said \xe2\x80\x94 women are more interested in comfort and \xe2\x80\x9clooking professional.\xe2\x80\x9d This meant a lot of focus on the length of the sleeve (the athletes did not want to expose too much of their upper arms) and the neckline, which ended up halfway between a V-neck and a crew neck, with enough give to be easily pulled over a ponytail. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey want zero distractions,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'Most of this may be lost on the armchair soccer fan, though the storytelling implicit in the design will not. (In any case, the kits are available in two fits: athlete and \xe2\x80\x9cstadium,\xe2\x80\x9d or looser, for the weekend fan.) Though the kits rely on the color palettes of national flags, the difference is often in the pixelated details. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cChile, France, U.S.A. \xe2\x80\x94 they are all red, white and blue,\xe2\x80\x9d Ms. Looker said, which can make them hard to distinguish. \xe2\x80\x9cWe bring it up all the time internally.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'What to expect? The United States jerseys have a throwback patriotism with (in the home kit) direct references to the jerseys worn by the 1999 team that transformed the profile of women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer in America: white, with red and blue stripes on the sleeves. '
b'The names of the 50 states are printed in gray on the back, and three stars over the crest nod to the three championships the United States has won. The away kit has tonal abstractions of stars and stripes on red (though they read a little blotchy from afar).'
b'Also tonal are the roses and assorted other florals on the four burgundy-red quadrants of the England jerseys, which is why France\xe2\x80\x99s hexagonal blue polka dots on white stand out, as does the Norwegian snowflake pattern that fades from red to blue, giving their home jersey an Empire-waist effect and uniting the shorts and top.'
b'By athlete request Chile, Nigeria, South Africa and Korea have the same pattern that the men\xe2\x80\x99s teams wore in the 2018 World Cup, though the fit has been customized for the women. (At least in Nigeria\xe2\x80\x99s case, the look was so successful that you can kind of understand why they didn\xe2\x80\x99t want to mess with a good thing.)'
b'And then there\xe2\x80\x99s Australia. Of all 14 Nike team looks, this will likely be the most controversial; a canvas of forest green, mustardy gold and white slashes and splotches that looks sort of like animal print meets modern art landscape painting. '
b'Together with the Sweden kit, by Adidas, which features the faces of female role models chosen by the players embedded in the numbers on the back of each jersey, it makes a statement that, on the pitch or the street, will be impossible to miss. '

b'By Tariq Panja'
b'A toxic political dispute is threatening to sink the Persian Gulf\xe2\x80\x99s biggest sports television contract, a development that could have repercussions for other broadcast rights agreements worth billions of dollars.'
b'The Asian Football Confederation, the governing body for soccer in the region, on Tuesday unilaterally broke its exclusive contract with its Middle Eastern broadcast partner, the Qatar-based beIN Media Group, so that it could broadcast matches in Saudi Arabia, a country where beIN has been banned amid a bitter diplomatic and economic crisis between Gulf neighbors that is now in its second year.'
b'The A.F.C\xe2\x80\x99s decision to nullify its contract for the broadcast rights to games in Saudi Arabia comes even after rulers there have allowed a major piracy operation, perhaps the most sophisticated in television history, to steal billions of dollars of sports content owned by beIN since 2017.'
b'BeIN\xe2\x80\x99s rights deals with the A.F.C., which run through 2020, are worth $300 million. The broadcaster immediately announced its intention to file a lawsuit to counter the decision to strip it of the rights to games broadcast in Saudi Arabia, which comes weeks before the A.F.C.\xe2\x80\x99s president, Sheikh Salman Bin Ibrahim al-Khalifa of Bahrain, stands for re-election. His opposition in that vote consists of a candidate from the United Arab Emirates, a Saudi ally, and another from Qatar.'
b'Yousef Al-Obaidly, beIN\xe2\x80\x99s chief executive, said Tuesday\xe2\x80\x99s decision was not a coincidence; he accused the A.F.C. of colluding with Saudi Arabia ahead of April\xe2\x80\x99s election.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt is remarkable to see the governing body of football across Asia \xe2\x80\x94 which should, by definition, be apolitical \xe2\x80\x94 putting politics ahead of its long-term commercial interests and established legitimate relationships,\xe2\x80\x9d Al-Obaidly told The New York Times in an emailed statement. \xe2\x80\x9cWe will use the full force of international law to claim every dollar of damages we have and will incur as a result of the A.F.C.\xe2\x80\x99s unilateral breach of our agreement.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Previously, the A.F.C. had issued strongly worded condemnations of the theft of beIN\xe2\x80\x99s programming and threats of legal action against the Saudi-based piracy operation, dubbed BeoutQ.'
b'The dispute comes at a delicate time, with beIN Media and the A.F.C locked in negotiations over a new regional contract. The A.F.C. had tried to persuade beIN to agree to purchase future rights but without access to Saudi Arabia, the Gulf\xe2\x80\x99s biggest market.'
b'News of a separate deal with the A.F.C. for the Saudi rights was first announced by the Saudi soccer federation, well before the A.F.C.\xe2\x80\x99s released its own brief statement on the matter almost 24 hours later.'
b'Salman, who is also a FIFA vice president, has made no comment. The A.F.C said its decision to stream games in Saudi Arabia on its own channels was an attempt to tackle piracy. But within hours, its content was available on other platforms across Saudi Arabia, including on the free-to-air channel Saudi 24. A promise to geoblock coverage so it could only be viewed inside the Gulf\xe2\x80\x99s most-populous country also failed, with the A.F.C.\xe2\x80\x99s stream of its Champions League games available outside the kingdom.'
b'Rights owners across the spectrum of sports, from FIFA to the governing bodies for tennis and track and field, have lodged complaints over the industrial scale piracy of their broadcast rights by BeoutQ. The latest twist could threaten the billions of dollars in income those organizations are able to extract for their content, according to beIN. The company said broadcasters would be unlikely to pay vast sums for exclusive contracts if those rights could be protected.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere is now no guaranteed protection of intellectual property in the region to due to the A.F.C. in effect endorsing Saudi Arabia\xe2\x80\x99s theft of world sport and wholesale disregard for the international rule of law,\xe2\x80\x9d the network said.'
