b'By Allie Conti'
b'In a dive bar underneath the Williamsburg Bridge in Brooklyn, fans of an obscure soccer team gathered after an entire workday of information blackout. They spent their Tuesday avoiding calls from family members and social media in its entirety because they didn\xe2\x80\x99t want to spoil the outcome of a match that technically ended long ago, halfway across the world in Germany.'
b'When their team scored what would be their only goal of the game, the supporters chanted raucously for \xe2\x80\x9cthe boys in brown,\xe2\x80\x9d thrusting their pints in the air, none the wiser that it was, as it frequently has been, already a lost cause.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cOne of the biggest crimes you could commit with this group is to mention you know the outcome,\xe2\x80\x9d said Karl Paranya, who lives in the neighborhood and has been watching the matches since he first stumbled into East River Bar about seven years back. \xe2\x80\x9cIt can be a bit awkward because our cries don\xe2\x80\x99t do anything for a team that finished eight hours ago, but it feels the same for us.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The team they follow is F.C. St. Pauli, a tiny club whose games no cable soccer package broadcasts live; it would be like expecting to find an Orlando Solar Bears hockey game on ESPN.'
b'But what draws Mr. Paranya and the rest of the supporters here is the team\xe2\x80\x99s unusual politics: F.C. St. Pauli is an avowed anti-fascist soccer team based in Hamburg that plays in Germany\xe2\x80\x99s second division and hasn\xe2\x80\x99t won the title in more than 40 years, though it runs a kindergarten inside the stadium, which displays signs proclaiming \xe2\x80\x9cno person is illegal.\xe2\x80\x9d The club has a worldwide, international fandom that defines itself in opposition to the racism and violence that characterizes European football hooliganism.'
b'The East River Pirates, as they\xe2\x80\x99re known, are still only maybe one of 10 supporters\xe2\x80\x99 groups in North America, and the only official one in the city. As such, East River Bar has become an unlikely spiritual home for German tourists, as well as a set of extremely devoted American fans who are far more interested in the team for their politics than whether or not they\xe2\x80\x99re in possession of the ball at any given time.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s not like we\xe2\x80\x99re that invested in the game play or the results,\xe2\x80\x9d said Shawn Roggenkamp, age 32, who helps coordinate the loose gathering of fans. \xe2\x80\x9cBut it is a reason for us to get together every week and bring this group of people together who maybe wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have found each other any other way.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'East River Bar, which began as paint factory and was also a biker hangout in a previous life, was purchased about 15 years ago by Marek Gregorski, a Polish expatriate. His intention was originally to serve food, though he said the money for that part of the business fell through. The cheap drinks, cavernous space, and location next to the Williamsburg Bridge soon attracted a specific clientele, which Mr. Gregorski happily catered to. \xe2\x80\x9cAt some point we started to get some bike messengers, more and more of them, and we became a staple for hosting messengers and their parties,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Gregorski said. \xe2\x80\x9cThey get off work, and this is their first stop to get a beer and relax a little bit.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Pirates, who celebrated their 10th anniversary this past November, were initially regarded as oddballs at East River, which is decidedly not a sports bar, unless you count billiards or biking. Out front, there\xe2\x80\x99s a sign featuring an enormous gear and a vending machine selling spare inner tubes. The backyard has communal grills for customer barbecues in warm weather. The inside is sparsely decorated, and being a classic dive, contains only a couple of tiny televisions that are always on but no one pays much attention to. A regular game day will bring a mix of bike punks, New York soccer heads, and Germans on a pilgrimage to watch St. Pauli on a giant projector screen instead.'
b'Ms. Roggenkamp, who works for the auction house Christie\xe2\x80\x99s, was introduced to the cult of St. Pauli about five years ago when she was studying German through a private program. A classmate took her to watch a game at East River. Over the next year and a half, she slowly started to take on a leadership role in the supporters\xe2\x80\x99 club. In keeping with the team\xe2\x80\x99s philosophy, that typically involves passing a collection cup for charity during halftime. The ritual takes on an air of communion \xe2\x80\x94 a characterization that Ms. Roggenkamp agrees with.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI was having a conversation about it with one of my friends the other day,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd he was like, \xe2\x80\x98You talk about this as if it\xe2\x80\x99s your church group.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Jah Jah Brown, half of the Brooklyn-based rap duo known as Ninjasonik, has been coming to watch games at East River Bar for the past six years because he\xe2\x80\x99s enamored with the team\xe2\x80\x99s politics. He said that German tourists regularly walk into the bar, which is typically full of bicycles, and have to ask, \xe2\x80\x9cAre we in the right spot?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In fact, the bar is a bridge between the two nations. Mr. Paranya remembered being with a Turkish friend years ago and lamenting that he didn\xe2\x80\x99t have a geographical allegiance to a soccer team as an American. The friend immediately pegged him as a would-be St. Pauli fan, though the comment was initially forgotten. Years later, he and his wife popped into East River Bar for a beer, where a game happened to be screening. After about five minutes, he realized who was playing. \xe2\x80\x9cI remembered that I was supposed to like these guys,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Paranya said. \xe2\x80\x9cBy the end of the game I was singing all the songs and had purchased a T-shirt.\xe2\x80\x9d A few years later, he took a trip to Germany, which he described as a pretense to visit St. Pauli\xe2\x80\x99s stadium. He wore his supporters shirt and made about \xe2\x80\x9c20 new best friends,\xe2\x80\x9d some of which he now sees occasionally when they come to visit the United States and make their obligatory trip to Williamsburg.'
b'With about 10 minutes left in the game that Tuesday, the other team scored, though not many fans seemed to notice. When they sunk another goal and things seemed good and over, one of the Pirates\xe2\x80\x99 organizers, S\xc3\xb6ren Thode, switched the broadcast to a YouTube video of the German entertainer Hans Albers\xe2\x80\x99s ode about the Reeperbahn \xe2\x80\x94 the red-light district district of working-class Hamburg. People finished their beers and said their goodbyes until the next match on Monday afternoon, though they, of course, wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be watching until nightfall.'

b'Supported by'
b'By Tariq Panja'
b'ABU DHABI, United Arab Emirates \xe2\x80\x94 China\xe2\x80\x99s recent attempts to emerge as a serious soccer nation after decades in the sports wilderness have taken some curious turns. One of the more recent ones is visible \xe2\x80\x94 or, rather, invisible \xe2\x80\x94 at this month\xe2\x80\x99s Asian Cup.'
b'Temperatures in the tournament, which is being played in the United Arab Emirates, can be stifling, making the sight of some Chinese players wearing long-sleeved undershirts beneath their jerseys seem puzzling.'
b'The answer lies in a semiofficial edict from Chinese sports officials issued last year that bans tattoos from being visible during matches. The directive applies to the national team but also to Chinese players in domestic competitions, like the Chinese Super League.'
b'Soccer is now a national priority under President Xi Jinping, and China\xe2\x80\x99s soccer authorities expect the country\xe2\x80\x99s best players to promote positive values to the next generation of athletes and their parents, some of whom remain wary of allowing their children to play a sport they consider to be dangerous or, worse, frivolous. In many ways, the no-tattoos rule is a microcosm of the never-ending wrestling match that China\xe2\x80\x99s central government conducts with its sometimes-dueling allegiances to modernity and control.'
b'The rule can be more onerous for some players than for others. Take the heavily inked central defender Zhang Linpeng. Most of his body, including the entirety of both arms, is heavily tattooed. He has been playing with a compression shirt underneath his national team jersey at the Asian Cup, though he has avoided covering the markings on his right leg and his neck.'
b'Other players have less work to do; a tattooed back or calf is often covered by a player\xe2\x80\x99s uniform, while a smaller bit of artwork can be hidden under athletic tape. (Zhang and others have managed to get some respite: Covering tattoos isn\xe2\x80\x99t mandatory for training sessions.)'
b'The Chinese soccer federation and tournament organizers clearly do not want to talk about the issue, however. At a news conference before a game with South Korea this week that will decide top spot in Group C, a tournament official tried to shut down a question about the tattoos before the Chinese national team coach, Marcello Lippi of Italy, could answer it.'
b'After it was rephrased, Lippi gave a short, diplomatic response, saying he was not unduly concerned by the edict. The team\xe2\x80\x99s captain, Zheng Zhi, sitting to Lippi\xe2\x80\x99s right, stifled a laugh but declined to comment on the issue.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThis is only a detail; I don\xe2\x80\x99t really want to talk about this,\xe2\x80\x9d Lippi said through a translator.'
b'A few months before the ink ban was imposed on Chinese soccer players, television stars faced similar restrictions as part of government efforts to control what viewers were being exposed to in the media. The soccer rules were brought in so quickly, though, that some clubs simply chose to heavily bandage their players before they took the field.'
b'The tattoo ban has become a lively topic on Chinese social media. Many people in China appear to support the official view that the players are public figures and should act accordingly. Others have ridiculed the move, which is at odds with a current trend in Western sports, where elaborate tattoos are now as commonplace as cleats and jerseys. Zlatan Ibrahimovic of the Los Angeles Galaxy is covered by them; Barcelona\xe2\x80\x99s Lionel Messi now has a long sleeve of art on his right arm and another on his left leg.'
b'Zhang, a defender considered one of China\xe2\x80\x99s best players, did not play in two national-team matches after the tattoo ban was established in March. The official reason was injury, but angry fans speculated on social media that China had been thrashed in matches against Wales and the Czech Republic because it was forced to play without Zhang, who they suspected had been benched because of his body art.'
b'China has been pumping millions of dollars into soccer since 2015. A sleepy national league is now backed by some of the country\xe2\x80\x99s biggest companies, whose lavish spending quickly attracted world-class coaches and players in search of some of the biggest paydays in the sport. A more intense focus is on creating a national team capable of transforming itself from a punch line into a force that can compete with the best in Asia and, eventually, against the best in the world.'
b'The road to get there has been bumpy, though, with soccer officials, typically political figures, chopping and changing policy, or introducing rules that some have found hard to follow.'
b'Last year, for example, top clubs were taken by surprise when the Chinese Football Association suddenly announced the best young players would be pulled from their club teams midseason and sent for military training, a practice that China has used with top athletes in other sports. Images of players with freshly shaved heads being put through drills by specialty trainers were beamed around the country.'
b'The effects on some teams were significant. Dalian Yifang F.C. lost four straight games and was pulled toward relegation after three of its young starters were called up.'
b'It is unlikely the best young players will be going back to their clubs anytime soon. Plans have been announced to create a team composed of young Chinese to play in the second division for a team recently created by a university in Beijing. The team could function as a kind of second national team.'
b'China\xe2\x80\x99s men\xe2\x80\x99s national team has not played in a World Cup since its first appearance in 2002, when it lost all three of its games. Its leaders have targeted hosting the event in 2030, and winning it by 2050. To do that, Xi has set a target for 20,000 training centers and 70,000 soccer fields to be established by 2020.'
b'The efforts are immediately visible. Private soccer schools have mushroomed in the major cities, and European coaches of varying abilities are being recruited at staggering rates.'
b'Lippi, who won the World Cup as Italy\xe2\x80\x99s manager in 2006, has seen much of it. He moved to China in 2012 to run the big-spending club Guangzhou Evergrande, and has announced that he will step down as national coach after the Asian Cup. He has stressed a focus on youth development as a path to China\xe2\x80\x99s soccer goals.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSix years ago in China there were not so many young players,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cThis is the only way if you want to become stronger in the future. China has to continue to work in this direction.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Regardless of how fast it improves, however, don\xe2\x80\x99t be surprised to see some players turning up in long sleeves on the way there.'

b'By The Associated Press'
b'FIFA president Gianni Infantino has called for a crackdown on racism at soccer games after several high-profile incidents, and encouraged referees to abandon matches in the worst cases.'
b'"We will not hesitate to do everything in our power to eradicate racism, and any other form of discrimination, from football, at any level and anywhere in the world," the head of world soccer\'s governing body said in a statement on Saturday.'
b'Infantino referred to the "three-step procedure" at tournaments, a measure that was brought in at the 2017 Confederations Cup and which allows a referee to stop a game, suspend a game and ultimately abandon a game if discriminatory behavior persists.'
b'"FIFA urges all member associations, leagues, clubs and disciplinary bodies to adopt the same procedure, as well as a zero-tolerance approach to incidents of racism in football, and to apply harsh sanctions for any such kind of behavior," Infantino said. "Racism has no place in football, just as it has no place in society either."'
b"Infantino's intervention comes one day after Amiens' French league game at Dijon was temporarily halted after the visiting side's captain Prince Gouano was subjected to racist insults."
b'"I heard monkey noises," said Gouano, who asked the referee to stop the game. The French league said the alleged perpetrator was subsequently identified and arrested.'
b'FIFA says it fully supports Gouano, as well as players such as Kalidou Koulibaly, Raheem Sterling and Danny Rose, who were also subjected to racist abuse.'
b'Tottenham defender Rose went so far as to say he was looking forward to retiring from the game in the future because of ongoing racism and a lack of action from authorities.'
b'Rose was among England players targeted with monkey chants in Montenegro last month while playing in a European Championship qualifier.'
b'"In recent days, it has been very sad to see a number of racist incidents in football," Infantino said. "This is really not acceptable."'
b'FIFA disbanded its anti-racism task force early in Infantino\'s presidency in 2016, saying it had "completely fulfilled its temporary mission."'
b"Later Saturday, Premier League club West Ham said it will ban any fans who were filmed chanting anti-Semitic abuse about rival Tottenham ahead of West Ham's game at Manchester United."
b'West Ham said it was "disgusted" by the video circulating on Twitter.'

b'By Manuela Andreoni, Shasta Darlington and Tariq Panja'
b'RIO DE JANEIRO \xe2\x80\x94 Fire consumed a dormitory early Friday at a Brazilian training center for teenage soccer players run by one of South America\xe2\x80\x99s most prominent teams, killing at least 10 in a disaster that reverberated through the soccer world and beyond.'
b'The fire in the dormitory, which may have been constructed improperly on what was intended to be a parking lot, was the latest in a string of seemingly preventable tragedies that have convulsed Brazil over the past two weeks.'
b'It struck the training center of the Flamengo club in Rio de Janeiro, breaking out in the early morning when many youth players, ages 14 to 17, were asleep. Three others were injured, one seriously, and were taken to a hospital.'
b'Officials would not confirm the identities of the dead. But Globoesporte, a Brazilian sports news website, said all were players. The dorm housed 26 players and 13 escaped unharmed, the website said.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe location was completely consumed in flames,\xe2\x80\x9d Douglas Henaut, a lieutenant with firefighters, told journalists at the scene. \xe2\x80\x9cUnfortunately, we weren\xe2\x80\x99t able to rescue anyone inside. As much as we tried to enter and locate the victims, it wasn\xe2\x80\x99t possible. The bodies were found totally charred.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Flamengo is one of Brazil\xe2\x80\x99s most popular soccer clubs and is considered a symbol of the country\xe2\x80\x99s global dominance in the training and development of young athletes who aspire to join professional soccer.'
b'Some of Brazil\xe2\x80\x99s biggest stars have played with Flamengo, among them Rom\xc3\xa1rio, Ronaldinho and Zico, who represented the country in World Cups, and many others who have played for high-profile teams abroad.'
b'The club\xe2\x80\x99s training center, known as Ninho do Urubu, or Vulture\xe2\x80\x99s Nest, in the western part of the city, had recently undergone renovations. Rio officials confirmed local news reports that the dormitory had been erected in what was supposed to be a parking lot, with no permits for construction, and was going to be torn down after the occupants moved into a new dorm.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe fire was in my room,\xe2\x80\x9d Felipe Cardoso, 15, who plays for the Flamengo youth team, wrote on Twitter. \xe2\x80\x9cI have only God to thank for managing to wake up and escape death, may God comfort my brothers.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'For players accepted to the youth team, it was the Brazilian equivalent of joining the Dallas Cowboys. A video posted by a team member who was away when the fire erupted showed their exuberant camaraderie in the dorm.'
b'President Jair Bolsonaro of Brazil, who is hospitalized after intestinal surgery, posted a condolence message on social media: \xe2\x80\x9cThis morning we were made aware of the sad tragedy in the Flamengo training center, taking the young lives of those who were beginning the path toward the realization of their professional dreams.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Firefighters said they were alerted to the blaze at 5:17 a.m. local time, and Rio de Janeiro prosecutors said they had created a task force to investigate the cause.'
b'The fire comes two weeks after a dam broke in the most lethal mining disaster in Brazil\xe2\x80\x99s history, and just two days after a powerful summer storm in Rio de Janeiro set off flooding and mudslides, killing six.'
b'The disasters have shocked and saddened Brazilians and have highlighted the country\xe2\x80\x99s shoddy infrastructure and poor emergency response.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe are seeing a succession of avoidable, preventable facts and disasters, and we must pay attention to them so that the institutions of control, enforcement and punishment really work in Brazil,\xe2\x80\x9d the country\xe2\x80\x99s prosecutor general, Raquel Dodge, said in Bras\xc3\xadlia, the capital, after news of the fire spread.'
b'The blaze also focused attention on living conditions for young Brazilian soccer players, many of whom come from underprivileged backgrounds and live in dormitories like Flamengo\xe2\x80\x99s across the vast country.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s hard to imagine what Flamengo means for these boys,\xe2\x80\x9d said Juca Kfouri, a Brazilian sports columnist and author. \xe2\x80\x9cIn Brazil, there are only two legal paths to social improvement for them: entertainment and soccer. Otherwise it\xe2\x80\x99s a life of crime.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mr. Kfouri said he was not familiar with the dormitory at the Flamengo training ground, but he said that living conditions at soccer clubs in Brazil historically were atrocious \xe2\x80\x94 including a case in which boys were housed in one dormitory built underneath the stands and another infested with rats.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTraining at Flamengo is realizing your life\xe2\x80\x99s goal,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Kfouri said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut now it\xe2\x80\x99s a dream turned into a nightmare.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He added that the death toll in the fire was most likely lower than it could have been because training had been suspended after the widespread flooding in Rio, and some boys had gone home.'
b'Zico, one of Brazil\xe2\x80\x99s soccer legends, sent reporters a video lamenting the tragedy. He said he had met some of the boys who died in the fire. \xe2\x80\x9cWe ended up getting close to them,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cBoys with dreams, goals, a lot of them trying to help their families.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Rival clubs expressed sympathy on social media. The messages included one from Chapecoense, which suffered its own tragedy just over two years ago when a plane carrying team members to an international competition ran out of fuel and crashed, killing nearly all of the 77 people on board.'
b'One of soccer\xe2\x80\x99s most recent breakout stars, the Real Madrid forward Vin\xc3\xadcius J\xc3\xbanior, who was developed in Flamengo\xe2\x80\x99s youth ranks and lived at the academy, took to Twitter to express his horror at the fire. He wrote that he was in shock and called for prayers.'
b'While Brazil, Latin America\xe2\x80\x99s largest economy, is known for its exports of meat, metal and coffee, nothing garners as much attention as the soccer players it dispatches at a rate unmatched anywhere.'
b'Brazilian players form the backbone of soccer\xe2\x80\x99s $7 billion player trading industry. Last year alone 832 players left on overseas adventures, according to data provided by soccer\xe2\x80\x99s global governing body, FIFA.'
b'While a few, like the star forward Neymar, will make it to the biggest stages of the game, most are soccer\xe2\x80\x99s workhorses, providing a Brazilian touch to professional teams from East Timor to the Faroe Islands looking to fill their rosters with reliable, well-coached and relatively inexpensive talent.'
b'Back home in Brazil, rampant inequality and a lack of other opportunities mean, the supply of young, gifted soccer players looking for a way out of grinding poverty is almost limitless.'
b'Flamengo\xe2\x80\x99s newly renovated facility opened late last year, at a cost of about $6 million, and was part of a complete overhaul of the club\xe2\x80\x99s youth development system.'
b'Besides five training fields, a swimming pool and gym facilities, the complex was to contain accommodations for 48 players to live on site: 36 single bedrooms, and six doubles.'
b'Occupants of the dorm that burned had been scheduled to move into a new building next month, according to local news media reports.'
b'Flamengo also had engaged Double Pass, a Belgian consulting firm that specializes in soccer youth development, to modernize the way it trained players.'
b'Alexandre Wrobel, a vice president at the club, has been quoted by Brazilian media as saying the youth training facility it would be among the top five in soccer.'
b'Such modern surroundings remain comparatively rare in South America, where many clubs cannot call on the lucrative television deals and sponsorship arrangements that bankroll teams in Europe.'
b'Manuela Andreoni reported from Rio de Janeiro, Shasta Darlington from S\xc3\xa3o Paulo, Brazil, and Tariq Panja from London. Rory Smith contributed reporting from Manchester, England.'

b'On Soccer'
b'By Rory Smith'
b'DORTMUND, Germany \xe2\x80\x94 There are times these days when Marco Reus finds himself in the middle of the field at Borussia Dortmund\xe2\x80\x99s Signal Iduna Park, watching as Jadon Sancho and Jacob Bruun Larsen and Achraf Hakimi tear around him, a blur of yellow and black, and remembering what it was like to be young.'
b'Not that Reus is what most of us would call old; he is not quite what his peers would call old, either. That is how he feels, though. \xe2\x80\x9cI am old, my friend,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cIn our business, now, when you are 29 or 30, you are old.\xe2\x80\x9d He delivers it with a smile, an acknowledgment that he is hamming it up, just a little, but the sentiment is real.'
b'Reus feels old in the sense that he is starkly aware that he is no longer young. He knows that whenever he sees Sancho, Larsen and the rest of Dortmund\xe2\x80\x99s shooting stars, the way they play with boldness and fearlessness. They look to him like \xe2\x80\x9cyoung horses,\xe2\x80\x9d wild and free.'
b'Reus knows that feeling well, that glorious weightlessness, unencumbered by thoughts of \xe2\x80\x9cwhat will happen later, what happens after you finish,\xe2\x80\x9d the end so distant that you cannot believe it will ever come.'
b'He was like that once, when he was one of the standard-bearers of the new German generation that was going to lift the World Cup in 2014, a winger of pace and cunning and dead-eyed finishing, first with Borussia M\xc3\xb6nchengladbach and then as part \xe2\x80\x94 a key part \xe2\x80\x94 of J\xc3\xbcrgen Klopp\xe2\x80\x99s Dortmund team.'
b'He remembers it well enough to know that he no longer has it, that it has disappeared at some point along the way. And yet it is hard to conceive of Reus as a \xe2\x80\x9cveteran,\xe2\x80\x9d as he puts it. Partly, that is because he does not really look the part. His hair is a little darker than it used to be, no longer colored a bright blond, but his face is still smooth-skinned, and his voice is still soft, boyish. He hardly fits the stereotype of the grizzled, wizened pro.'
b'And partly it is because it feels as if Reus, even on the cusp of his 30th birthday, is still somehow a talent-in-waiting, his potential not yet fully tapped. For a player regarded as one of Europe\xe2\x80\x99s best for much of the last decade, he has an air of one of the sport\xe2\x80\x99s lost boys.'
b'When Dortmund re-signed Reus \xe2\x80\x94 he was released from its youth system as a teenager \xe2\x80\x94 after its last Bundesliga title, in 2012, he was supposed to be the player who lifted the club to the next level.'
b'Klopp believed Reus represented a scarcely believable bargain \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9chis real market value is much higher\xe2\x80\x9d than the nearly $20 million he cost, he said \xe2\x80\x94 while the Dortmund chief executive, Hans-Joachim Watzke, felt Reus might be able to \xe2\x80\x9cdefine an era\xe2\x80\x9d for the club, in the way that \xe2\x80\x9cUwe Seeler did at Hamburg and Steven Gerrard at Liverpool.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Franz Beckenbauer identified him, along with Mario G\xc3\xb6tze, as Germany\xe2\x80\x99s brightest hopes. The two helped Dortmund to the 2013 Champions League final; Reus was penciled in as a starter in Joachim L\xc3\xb6w\xe2\x80\x99s Germany team for the 2014 World Cup.'
b'And then, 10 hours before Germany was scheduled to travel to Brazil, Reus tore his ankle ligaments in his final pretournament friendly. He punched the ground in frustration. Germany\xe2\x80\x99s team flew without him. It came home a month later as the world champion.'
b'Reus did his rehab, returned to fitness, seemed ready to break through into the elite once more. Before the European Championship in 2016, L\xc3\xb6w said that Reus \xe2\x80\x9chugely enriched\xe2\x80\x9d the Germany side. But he missed that tournament through injury, too (Germany reached the semifinals).'
b'Another recovery, another fresh start. In 2017, EA Sports made him the cover star of that year\xe2\x80\x99s edition of its FIFA game, an honor usually afforded to Lionel Messi or Cristiano Ronaldo; that was the sort of company Reus was expected to keep. Dortmund made the German Cup final that year. Reus, after so many delays, had the first silverware of his career in his grasp.'
b'He picked up an injury in the first half. At halftime, Dortmund\xe2\x80\x99s doctors informed him that they believed he had torn his anterior cruciate ligament, and that he would be sidelined for six months, eight months, maybe more. He called his parents, and his girlfriend, Scarlett, and cried. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s bad,\xe2\x80\x9d he told them. Dortmund went on to win.'
b'That evening, Reus stopped to talk to reporters. They asked him if he knew the extent of the injury. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is just a little cruciate,\xe2\x80\x9d he told them. Dortmund\xe2\x80\x99s communications team was baffled. There is, they knew, and Reus knew, no such thing as a little cruciate injury.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNegative experiences teach you what to say,\xe2\x80\x9d Reus said, explaining how he could be so relaxed. It was not, though, an act of bravado. He had suffered injuries before, setbacks bad enough that he had once said he would happily trade all of the money he had made during his career for his fitness.'
b'This injury was the worst of all of them, and yet it had, he said, \xe2\x80\x9ccaused something in my head to accept it.\xe2\x80\x9d That is not to say he did not suffer. In the hospital, a couple of days later, \xe2\x80\x9conce the adrenaline had worn off,\xe2\x80\x9d Reus felt that familiar bleakness setting in. He still had times when he \xe2\x80\x9cgot emotional, angry, screamed, cried,\xe2\x80\x9d but he knew that he had to get it out, get over it, get on with it.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf it stays inside, you get sad, and you never get to the point where you can make the next step,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cYou can be sad for a couple of days, and nobody will be angry with you. But for weeks and months? It does not help.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He did not, though \xe2\x80\x94 not then, not during any of his injuries, not during any of the time that he lost \xe2\x80\x94 start to feel he was cursed. He never asked why this was happening to him, why he had so much snatched away from him, why fate seemed arranged that he would remain a what if, one of those players who never quite becomes \xe2\x80\x94 through no fault of his own \xe2\x80\x94 what he was supposed to be.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt is human to think about what I have missed,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut if I regret too much, think about what I have lost, I lose focus on what I need to do. You cannot rewind. This is not a computer game that you can play again. All I can do is try to be better, to be luckier, next time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That is not the only change in perspective injury has afforded him. \xe2\x80\x9cYou have a lot of time to think about other things, too,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. Over the eight months of his rehabilitation, Reus \xe2\x80\x94 by his own estimation \xe2\x80\x94 grew up. \xe2\x80\x9cYou become aware of what you are doing, and what comes next, and when that will start,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'He turns 30 in May. By that stage, if all goes well, he will have become a father for the first time. He is no longer young, even if he is not quite old. \xe2\x80\x9cI have three or four years left,\xe2\x80\x9d he said of his playing career. \xe2\x80\x9cThat is still quite a period, but football goes fast.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He has made no firm decisions on what he will do when his career ends \xe2\x80\x94 he would prefer not to go into senior management, but coach children, if he stays in soccer, because that is when \xe2\x80\x9cyou should be having the most fun\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 though he has a few ideas. He has not forgotten what it is to be footloose, carefree, but that does not mean he envies Sancho, Larsen and his other young teammates. He does not resent the clock for ticking.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe injuries have taught me to enjoy the time I have on the field, the time I am training with the guys,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cAs you get older, you learn it will end at some point, and so you cherish the moments you are healthy.\xe2\x80\x9d Those young horses are lucky, he knows, to feel it will never end. But he would not trade places with them. When you know that time is limited, and time is precious, you appreciate it all the more.'

b'By Austin Ramzy'
b'A soccer player who was jailed in Thailand and faced being sent back to his native Bahrain, where he said he would be imprisoned and tortured, was released Monday after Thai prosecutors dropped the extradition case against him.'
b'On Tuesday afternoon, the player, Hakeem al-Araibi, arrived back in Australia, where he has refugee status. He was greeted at the airport in Melbourne by a swarm of well-wishers, who started singing, \xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99ll Never Walk Alone,\xe2\x80\x9d a popular soccer anthem.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAmazing to see all the people here,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m going to die in Australia. Australia is my country,\xe2\x80\x9d he added. \xe2\x80\x9cI love Australia.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mr. al-Araibi, 25, who had been a star defender for the Bahrain national soccer team, fled the small Gulf nation in 2011 during a crackdown on Arab Spring protesters. He said he had been tortured by government security forces. He has been playing soccer for a minor team in Melbourne, Australia.'
b'After his arrest in November at an airport in Bangkok, he became the focus of lobbying by diplomats, prominent sports figures and a social media campaign under the hashtag #savehakeem.'
b'Mr. al-Araibi left for Australia as soon as his departure was approved.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThis is the best outcome,\xe2\x80\x9d said his lawyer, Natalie Bergman. \xe2\x80\x9cIt should have happened from the beginning, but later is better than nothing.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After Mr. al-Araibi\xe2\x80\x99s arrival in Australia, Prime Minister Scott Morrison and Foreign Affairs Minister Marise Payne released a joint statement commending the Thai government for its decision and noting the \xe2\x80\x9cconstructive dialogue that we have had with Bahrain in helping to resolve this issue.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The statement added: \xe2\x80\x9cWe know all Australians will deeply appreciate the decision, allowing him to return to his wife, family and friends.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mr. al-Araibi traveled to Thailand last year for a honeymoon and was detained with his wife. She was released, but Mr. al-Araibi remained in detention as Bahrain pursued his extradition.'
b'He had been convicted in absentia and sentenced to 10 years in prison for charges including the burning of a police station, which he said occurred while he was playing in a televised match.'
b'The royal family of Bahrain, which is Sunni Muslim, has pursued an aggressive crackdown against calls for democracy from the kingdom\xe2\x80\x99s Shiite Muslim majority, including a campaign of widespread arrests and many convictions on what human rights groups say are trumped-up charges.'
b'Thailand, which has been run by a military junta since a 2014 coup, has sent people fleeing political oppression back to countries including China, raising fears that Mr. al-Araibi would also be returned.'
b'But the country has also shown signs that it can be moved by international pressure.'
b'Last month, a Saudi woman who said she was fleeing abuse from her family barricaded herself in a Bangkok airport hotel room and rallied support to her cause online. The woman, Rahaf Mohammed Alqunun, 18, was allowed to leave the airport after a two-day standoff and was granted asylum in Canada.'
b'Mr. al-Araibi received widespread support from the international sports world, including FIFA, the international body that oversees global soccer; the International Olympic Committee; and the World Players Association, an umbrella group representing 85,000 professional athletes worldwide.'
b'Jamie Vardy, a striker for the English Premier League club Leicester City, expressed support for Mr. al-Araibi on Twitter, and Craig Foster, a broadcaster and former captain of the Australian national men\xe2\x80\x99s team, was a prominent advocate for his release.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThis is a big victory for that global campaign and marks the fact that football will have to play an important role in human rights going forward,\xe2\x80\x9d said Phil Robertson, deputy Asia director for Human Rights Watch. \xe2\x80\x9cThey call football the beautiful game, and it is a beautiful day for the beautiful game.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mr. Foster, who lobbied FIFA officials and shouted his support to Mr. al-Araibi when he appeared at a hearing last week in leg shackles, expressed his gratitude to the Thai government for dropping the case.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMost important thing now is Hakeem\xe2\x80\x99s immediate well-being,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Foster said on Twitter after the ruling was announced. \xe2\x80\x9cSure embassy staff will take care of him, there\xe2\x80\x99ll be tears there tonight, as there are in our household right now.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'When Mr. al-Araibi arrived in Melbourne, Mr. Foster placed his arms around his shoulders.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTo see him back here on home soil today speaks volumes about the character, the values and the pride that we have as Australians,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Foster said.'
b'The Thai foreign minister, Don Pramudwinai, visited Bahrain and met on Sunday with Salman bin Hamad al-Khalifa, the crown prince, the state-run Bahrain News Agency reported. No details of their discussion were released.'
b'The decision to drop the case came after the government of Bahrain told Thai diplomats that it did not want to pursue it, said Chatchom Akapin, director general for international affairs for the Thai attorney general\xe2\x80\x99s office.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe got information from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs this morning that Bahrain is not interested in extraditing Hakeem anymore,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cTherefore, the attorney general office decided it was no use to pursue the case.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'LONDON \xe2\x80\x94 The diplomatic standoff between Qatar and its Arab neighbors spilled into the sports world once again Thursday as a Qatari vice president of Asia\xe2\x80\x99s soccer confederation was barred from traveling to the United Arab Emirates ahead of the region\xe2\x80\x99s top tournament.'
b'Saoud al-Mohannadi, vice president of the Asian Football Confederation, was denied permission to travel from Oman to the U.A.E. after airport officials said he wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be let into the country. The U.A.E., with Saudi Arabia and a handful of other Mideast countries, broke diplomatic relations and severed all ties with Qatar in 2017.'
b'Mohannadi is the chairman of the A.F.C.\xe2\x80\x99s competitions committee, a group with overall responsibility for the Asian Cup. Prohibiting him from traveling to the U.A.E. is the first sign that long-simmering political tensions in the Gulf are likely to have ramifications for continent\xe2\x80\x99s biggest tournament.'
b'Mohannadi immediately wrote a letter of complaint to Sheikh Salman bin Ibrahim al-Khalifa, the Bahraini royal who is the A.F.C.\xe2\x80\x99s current president. The organization said in a statement that it was aware of reports that Mohannadi was being denied the right to travel and that it would investigate. The A.F.C. said it had been \xe2\x80\x9cassured of visas and entry permits\xe2\x80\x9d for tournament organizing committee members and executives.'
b'The Saudi-led diplomatic dispute with Qatar included the suspension of flights between Qatar and the United Arab Emirates, as well as several other countries. Only recently have Qatari citizens been allowed to apply for permission to travel between the two countries. Such travel typically requires a visa and an approval letter from local authorities.'
b'Mohannadi, who in 2017 successfully managed to overturn a one-year FIFA ethics ban, had applied to enter the U.A.E. Local organizers told him he could travel there even though he had not received official clearance, according to people familiar with the matter. He traveled from Doha to Muscat, Oman\xe2\x80\x99s capital, where he was told his clearance was not registered.'
b'The soccer federation in Qatar, which will host the World Cup in 2022, said in a statement that it had reached out to the A.F.C. about the matter. \xe2\x80\x9cWe will comment further once we have an official response on the incident,\xe2\x80\x9d the federation said.'
b'The diplomatic dispute, which exploded in the spring of 2017, has already impacted regional sports. Players and officials on teams from countries opposed to Qatar initially refused to speak to beIN Sports, the Qatari-owned network that owns the rights to the A.F.C.\xe2\x80\x99s events. For much of the past year, BeoutQ, a bootlegging television network, has been unimpeded in broadcasting pirated beIN Sports events using a satellite operator based in Saudi Arabia.'
b'BeoutQ was launched in response to the governments of Saudi Arabia and the U.A.E. blocking the sale of beIN Sports as part of a blockade that has closed off air and sea access between the countries.'
b'Mohannadi\xe2\x80\x99s travel plans are unlikely to be the last flashpoint in the 24-team tournament that kicks off on Saturday. The draw, made in May, set up a match between foes Qatar and Saudi Arabia on Jan. 17. It\xe2\x80\x99s unlikely many, if any, Qatari supporters will make the trip to Abu Dhabi.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s almost more difficult to imagine than the U.S. national soccer team playing Iran in Tehran,\xe2\x80\x9d said Neil Quilliam, a senior research fellow with the Middle East and North Africa program at London\xe2\x80\x99s Chatham House, a British foreign affairs think tank. \xe2\x80\x9cThere will be some jittery people in Qatar hoping their players make it home.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mohannadi is one of two candidates who will be challenging Sheikh Salman for the A.F.C.\xe2\x80\x99s presidency later this year. The other candidate is Mohammed Khalfan al-Romaithi, a sports official from the U.A.E.'

b'LONDON \xe2\x80\x94 The authorities announced on Thursday that they had ended the search for the Argentine soccer player Emiliano Sala and his pilot after their aircraft vanished over the English Channel on Monday.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe reviewed all the information available to us, as well as knowing what emergency equipment was on board, and have taken the difficult decision to end the search,\xe2\x80\x9d David Barker, the harbormaster captain of the island of Guernsey, a self-governing British dependency off the coast of France, said in a statement posted by the police on Twitter.'
b'The search, which involved three planes, five helicopters, two lifeboats and the assistance of passing ships and fishing boats, covered an approximately 1,700-square-mile area, according to Mr. Barker.'
b'The police examined mobile phone data and satellite imagery, but no trace of the aircraft, Mr. Sala or the pilot, David Ibbotson, could be found.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe chances of survival at this stage are extremely remote,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Barker said in his statement.'

b'(Reuters) - Liverpool have taken a cue from Manchester United and hiked prices for away supporters when they host Barcelona in the Champions League semi-finals to subsidise tickets for own fans travelling to the Nou Camp, the Premier League club have said.'
b'Manchester United had hiked prices for their quarter-final tie with Barcelona when the Spanish club charged 102 pounds ($132.50), which British media reported was the most expensive ticket to a United game outside of a final.'
b'Liverpool have been allocated 4,620 away tickets priced at 119 euros ($133.70) each for the first leg in Spain on May 1.'
b'In response, the Merseyside club raised their ticket prices for Barcelona supporters travelling to Anfield to the same amount and will use the extra revenue to ensure Liverpool fans pay only 88 euros for the first leg.'
b'"All away tickets are priced at 119 euros, which is in line with Barcelona\'s pricing structure for the knockout stages of this season\'s Champions League," Liverpool said in a statement.'
b'"As a result, LFC will charge Barcelona supporters a reciprocal ticket price of 119 euros in the return leg at Anfield on Tuesday, May 7.'
b'"The additional revenue from this higher ticket pricing will be used to subsidise Liverpool supporters for their tickets, reducing the price by 31 euros to 88 euros."'
b"Tottenham Hotspur play Ajax Amsterdam in the other semi-final with the final scheduled at Atletico Madrid's Wanda Metropolitano stadium in the Spanish capital on June 1."

b'By The Associated Press'
b'Major League Soccer\xe2\x80\x99s Board of Governors formally unveiled plans Thursday to expand to 30 teams, and Sacramento and St. Louis have been invited to submit bids for new franchises.'
b'Commissioner Don Garber made the announcement at the board\xe2\x80\x99s meeting in Los Angeles.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cProfessional soccer at all levels is thriving in the United States and Canada and we believe there are many markets that could support a successful M.L.S. club,\xe2\x80\x9d Garber said in a statement. \xe2\x80\x9cExpansion during the last 15 years has been enormously successful and a key driver behind the league\xe2\x80\x99s continued rise, and we are pleased that some of the top business and community leaders representing great markets in North America are aggressively pursuing M.L.S. expansion clubs.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The league is currently at 24 teams, with F.C. Cincinnati joining this season. Nashville and Miami are set to start next year, and Austin will come aboard in 2021.'
b'The board did not identify markets that would receive teams, but groups in Sacramento and St. Louis have been invited to give formal presentations to the league\xe2\x80\x99s expansion committee.'
b'Garber said he hoped to have a decision announced by the M.L.S. All-Star Game in late July.'
b'He said he would like to see detailed bids that include final stadium plans, commitments of corporate support, composition of ownership groups, details about funding, as well as plans for player development, fan engagement and community programs.'
b'It has not been determined when the new teams will join the league. M.L.S. has set an expansion fee of $200 million for the league\xe2\x80\x99s 28th and 29th teams. A fee has not been set for the 30th franchise.'
b'Sacramento\xe2\x80\x99s hopes of landing a team were boosted in January when the billionaire Ron Burkle became the new lead investor in the Sacramento Republic soccer team. The team plays in the second-tier United Soccer League.'
b'The Republic, in a statement, called Thursday\xe2\x80\x99s announcement a \xe2\x80\x9cmonumental step\xe2\x80\x9d in the process.'
b'Burkle is a co-owner of the N.H.L.\xe2\x80\x99s Pittsburgh Penguins with a net worth estimated at $2 billion by Forbes magazine.'
b'The St. Louis group includes the World Wide Technology chief executive Jim Kavanaugh and the Taylor family, owners of the rental car company Enterprise Holdings.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cObviously, this increases the likelihood of fulfilling our dream of securing an M.L.S. team for St. Louis, but there\xe2\x80\x99s still work to be done, and this doesn\xe2\x80\x99t guarantee us an expansion spot,\xe2\x80\x9d said Carolyn Kindle Betz, president of the Enterprise Holdings Foundation President and the leader of the ownership group. \xe2\x80\x9cWe look forward to continue working with M.L.S. and Commissioner Garber toward our goal of bringing M.L.S. to the country\xe2\x80\x99s soccer capital.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'St. Louis supporters had hoped to help fund stadium plans by expanding the port authority, which would have allowed use of a 1 percent sales tax at the Union Station stadium site. But the measure was not brought up for a vote by the city\xe2\x80\x99s board of aldermen at Monday\xe2\x80\x99s final meeting of the 2018-19 session.'
b'M.L.S. has also decided that its clubs will seek training compensation and solidarity payments when academy players are signed by teams outside of the United States and Canada.'
b'Training compensation applies to academy players who have been offered an M.L.S. contract with their club but have chosen to sign their first professional contract with a foreign team, the league said. Such compensation is covered by FIFA regulations for player transfers.'
b'Solidarity payments apply to academy-developed players who are transferred for a fee between two teams from different international federations.'
b'The move toward training compensation and solidarity payments comes as the league\xe2\x80\x99s teams have increased their investment in player development. Last year, clubs collectively spent a record of more than $75 million on their academies, and the additional funds offer the potential to increase that investment.'
b'It also comes as international interest in players from the United States has increased. Training compensation and solidarity payments are common in professional leagues worldwide, but M.L.S. did not adopt a similar policy until Thursday.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe have been making a significant investment in youth development, and that investment has accelerated over the past few years,\xe2\x80\x9d Todd Durbin, M.L.S. executive vice president of competition and player relations, told The Associated Press. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd we believe that by making this change we\xe2\x80\x99ll not only be able to continue that investment, but increase it and provide more opportunities to young players.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The M.L.S. Players Association said the move was an attempt to force young players to sign with M.L.S. by limiting opportunities elsewhere.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt is an effort by the league to inhibit player choice, does nothing to address the development of youth soccer, and makes plain MLS\xe2\x80\x99s selective application of international rules to suit its own agenda,\xe2\x80\x9d the union said in a statement.'

b'By Palko Karasz'
b'A small village in Argentina on Saturday bid farewell to a favorite son, the soccer striker Emiliano Sala, who died along with his pilot last month when his small plane crashed in the English Channel.'
b'Friends, family and supporters gathered early Saturday in the village of Progreso, in the country\xe2\x80\x99s northeast, for a wake at Mr. Sala\xe2\x80\x99s soccer boyhood club, San Mart\xc3\xadn de Progreso, where his body lay in state. A religious ceremony was held in the afternoon, and he was to be cremated, reports said.'
b'Outside the club, a banner read, \xe2\x80\x9cEmi, you will never walk alone.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mr. Sala\xe2\x80\x99s body arrived in the village on Friday, a little more than a week after his remains were found in the wreckage of the plane that went down shortly after takeoff from Nantes, France, for Cardiff, Wales.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe are waiting for you, Emi,\xe2\x80\x9d the San Mart\xc3\xadn club posted on Facebook ahead of the body\xe2\x80\x99s arrival.'
b'The club\xe2\x80\x99s president, Daniel Ribero told Agence France-Presse, \xe2\x80\x9cHe represented a lot for us. We\xe2\x80\x99re a small village and Emi was a celebrity, the only player to turn professional.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mr. Sala, 28, started off as a youth player in his native Argentina and began his international career in France in 2010. He recently transferred to the English Premier League club Cardiff City from Nantes in the French league. The Cardiff club signed him for \xc2\xa315 million ($19 million) to add to its striking power.'
b'Representatives of both clubs attended the funeral service, the BBC reported and FC Nantes and fans paid tribute to Mr. Sala on Twitter.'
b'On Thursday, as two of his former French teams \xe2\x80\x94 SN Caen and FC Nantes \xe2\x80\x94 faced each other at Caen on France\xe2\x80\x99s west coast, signs paying tribute to the striker lined the pitch and players and fans joined in applause before the match began.'
b"Mr. Sala was flying to Cardiff with a pilot, David Ibbotson, on Jan. 21, when their single-engine, propeller-driven Piper Malibu vanished. An initial search for survivors was called off, but after pleas from Mr. Sala's family and a funding drive that raised more than 371,000 euros, about $424,000 in donations, the search resumed."
b'Recovery crews sent by the British Air Accidents Investigation Branch found the wreckage of the plane and recovered Mr. Sala\xe2\x80\x99s body.'
b'An inquest into the crash has been adjourned until November, when police and air investigators will release more details about the accident.'
b'The pilot is still missing, and Mr. Ibbotson\xe2\x80\x99s family were seeking donations to help find and recover his body.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe know that he\xe2\x80\x99s dead; we do know that, but we just want him home,\xe2\x80\x9d Nora Ibbotson, the pilot\xe2\x80\x99s wife, told a morning television show on the British network ITV on Monday. With the help of famous soccer players and fans, the fund-raiser was close to hitting its target of 400,000 pounds, around $515,000, according to its GoFundMe page.'
b'Although the wreckage of the Piper Malibu was not raised from the ocean bed, British investigators said underwater footage of the aircraft would help their work. The British Air Accidents Investigation Branch said it would publish early findings in the coming week.'

b'Screenland'
b'By Jody Rosen'
b'There is no shortage of Lionel Messi content on the World Wide Web. The 31-year-old soccer superstar ranks high in surveys of top Google searches, one of just a few human beings to earn a spot among such keyword perennials as \xe2\x80\x9cFacebook,\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x9cweather\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cfree porn.\xe2\x80\x9d In a 2015 tally of the most Googled person in each nation on earth, Messi tied Kim Kardashian for the most No. 1s, with a global reach that extended from his native Argentina to Haiti, Turkmenistan, Senegal and 22 other countries.'
b'Messi is also one of the world\xe2\x80\x99s pre-eminent viral video stars. Countless clips document \xe2\x80\x9cMessi magic,\xe2\x80\x9d a playing style of almost unseemly brilliance. On social media, users share videos of Messi\xe2\x80\x99s slipping passes through improbably tight spaces, corkscrewing shots past sprawling goalkeepers, darting around defenders like a jack rabbit navigating a gantlet of sloths. Type \xe2\x80\x9cMessi\xe2\x80\x9d into a YouTube search field, and you will find hundreds of highlight compilations with bombastic titles: \xe2\x80\x9cLionel Messi sees things we don\xe2\x80\x99t even consider,\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x9cLionel Messi: \xe2\x80\x94 A God Amongst Men,\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x9cLionel Messi: Extraterrestrial.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'So it was not exactly surprising when, on March 17, the internet was captivated by a Messi goal. It came in the 85th minute of a 4-1 victory for Messi\xe2\x80\x99s club team, FC Barcelona, over the Seville-based Real Betis. Messi gathered the ball about 24 yards from the Betis goal, slid a pass to his teammate Ivan Rakiti\xc4\x87 and then flowed forward to receive a return pass. The goal that followed was so easeful, so understated, that it was momentarily hard to process. Messi struck the ball in full stride but with shocking delicacy, lifting a chip shot that arced gracefully across the penalty area. The ball drifted beyond the reach of the goalie, Pau L\xc3\xb3pez, scraped the underside of the crossbar and dropped into the goal. Messi had taken his shot from a diagonal position more than 20 yards away, but it was not the stinging kick generally required to score from that spot. The ball\xe2\x80\x99s trajectory was languid and dreamy, like a gull gliding on an ocean breeze.'
b'Messi had already scored twice in the game. But the beauty and impudence of this goal \xe2\x80\x94 by some counts, the 656th of Messi\xe2\x80\x99s professional career \xe2\x80\x94 was clear to all. Betis supporters stood to applaud their tormentor. Soccer pundits reached for celestial metaphors. On ESPN.com, the journalist Musa Okwonga wrote that \xe2\x80\x9cthe ball, with the glorious inevitability of our slowly dying sun, rose and fell.\xe2\x80\x9d The wildest exultations came from the operatic English TV commentator Ray Hudson, who unleashed a torrent of mixed metaphors. \xe2\x80\x9cThe staggering genius of Lionel Messi!\xe2\x80\x9d he cried, during a live broadcast on the beIN SPORTS network. \xe2\x80\x9cThis miraculous footballer, this halo of a footballer!\xe2\x80\x89... He\xe2\x80\x99s got an algebraic equation to solve in the blink of a baby\xe2\x80\x99s eye, and he does it in a way that is just so poetic!\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Hudson is onto something with this talk of algebra and poetry. Messi\xe2\x80\x99s greatness lies in his mind as much as his body. Watching replays of the goal, you marvel above all at the audacity of Messi\xe2\x80\x99s idea. A chip? From that distance, at that angle, in that frenzied moment of open-field play? It\xe2\x80\x99s nuts \xe2\x80\x94 a fool\xe2\x80\x99s fantasy that blossoms, with every slow-motion replay, into wondrous fact. Messi saw something we didn\xe2\x80\x99t even consider.'
b'That viral clip is a testament to Messi\xe2\x80\x99s supernatural talent. It\xe2\x80\x99s also a reminder that online video is changing the way we consume and conceptualize sports. Decades ago, the culture of \xe2\x80\x9chighlights\xe2\x80\x9d was already transforming America\xe2\x80\x99s pastimes. The decline of slow-paced baseball, the ascendancy of the razzle-dazzle N.B.A., the rule changes that have brought an offensive explosion in the N.F.L. \xe2\x80\x94 these developments were fueled in no small part by the rise of ESPN\xe2\x80\x99s SportsCenter and the primacy of video clips. But in the old days, those highlight packages were appointment viewing, available only on nightly broadcasts. Today highlights spread across the web in seconds, mutating into memes and turning star athletes into visual brands. You don\xe2\x80\x99t have to be a purist to wonder how this media ecosystem is affecting our tolerance for the natural rhythms and longueurs of sports, those lengthy stretches of \xe2\x80\x9clowlight\xe2\x80\x9d play that are only occasionally punctuated by thrills.'
b'Soccer is a subtle game; in general, goals are hard to come by. It would seem to be the major sport most antithetical to highlight culture. (For all those moments of Messi magic, the essence of his greatness may lie in untelegenic maneuverings off the ball, the cagey movements that put him into positions where he can erupt.) But viral video is altering our view of soccer\xe2\x80\x99s history. Today\xe2\x80\x99s fans compare clips while endlessly debating the \xe2\x80\x9cgreatest of all time\xe2\x80\x9d status of Messi and his chief rival, the Portuguese striker Cristiano Ronaldo. The GOATs of previous eras \xe2\x80\x94 like Pel\xc3\xa9, Johan Cruyff and Diego Maradona \xe2\x80\x94 recede into the background: They had the misfortune to play in a time before a footballer\xe2\x80\x99s every exploit was captured on video. If a player\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9creceipts\xe2\x80\x9d aren\xe2\x80\x99t on YouTube, he\xe2\x80\x99s liable to lose to his toehold in the historiography.'
b'Yet for the 21st-century soccer fan, online video is a godsend \xe2\x80\x94 the only conceivable way to keep up with the ultimate global sport. With a mobile phone and a well-curated social media feed, it is now possible to follow great matches on five different continents, nearly every day, in real time.'
b'As for Messi: I know few more pleasurable ways to kill a couple of hours than by squinting at a liquid-crystal screen, bugging out to the likes of \xe2\x80\x9cLionel Messi Humiliating Players Two or More Times in the Same Play.\xe2\x80\x9d Messi is the quintessential internet-age soccer star \xe2\x80\x94 he scored his first goal for Barcelona in 2005, the year YouTube went online \xe2\x80\x94 but his persona is a throwback to an earlier period. He is a trickster and a funnyman, like an old-time silent-movie star. He\xe2\x80\x99s small and scrappy, standing just 5-foot-7, the Charlie Chaplin to suave Ronaldo\xe2\x80\x99s Rudolph Valentino. Many of his greatest moments play out like slapstick farce, leaving pratfalling defenders littered across the pitch.'
b'At their best, sports like soccer are the digital age\xe2\x80\x99s most reliable suppliers of an old-fashioned brand of entertainment, the special-effects-free kind, in which human beings use only their sinews and synapses to deliver thrills and spills, action and comedy. Messi\xe2\x80\x99s chip in the Betis match was a comedic set piece in its own right. On YouTube, you can find video montages of the play\xe2\x80\x99s aftermath: Messi and his teammates celebrating and cracking up, the goalie L\xc3\xb3pez mugging like an exasperated vaudeville straight man, play-by-play announcers dissolving in peals of laughter. The goal is a cosmic joke if there ever was one. A small man swings his left leg; a ball loops skyward; common sense and natural laws are suspended. You know the punch line: The ball will fall back to earth, landing \xe2\x80\x94 plop \xe2\x80\x94 in the back of the net. But no matter how many times you watch it, the gag still kills.'
b'Jody Rosen is a contributing writer for the magazine and the author of the forthcoming book \xe2\x80\x9cTwo Wheels Good: The Bicycle on Planet Earth and Elsewhere.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'\xe2\x80\x9cSo many of us can relate to playing by rules that were never set up for us to win.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x94 Abby Wambach, two-time Olympic gold medalist and World Cup champion'
b'Abby Wambach has made a career out of pursuing goals. She\xe2\x80\x99s scored 184 of them after all, the most by any soccer player, male or female, in international soccer history. But now, a few years into her retirement, Wambach, who led the United States women\xe2\x80\x99s team to a World Cup championship in 2015, is focused on a new kind of goal: motivating women to become leaders. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere has never been a more important, urgent time than right now for women to begin to fully lead our own lives,\xe2\x80\x9d she told me this week.'
b'In her new book, \xe2\x80\x9cWolfpack,\xe2\x80\x9d Wambach, 38, shares lessons she learned from decades of training, failure and triumph on the field. It is based on the commencement speech she gave at Barnard College in New York last year that quickly went viral. \xe2\x80\x9cIf I could go back and tell my younger self one thing, it would be this: \xe2\x80\x98Abby, you were never Little Red Riding Hood; you were always the wolf,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d she told graduates.'
b'[FROM THE ARCHIVES: Abby Wambach, Retired U.S. Soccer Star, Reflects on Her Addiction]'
b'Her book\xe2\x80\x99s release comes a month after the United States women\xe2\x80\x99s team filed a gender discrimination lawsuit against the United States Soccer Federation. While Wambach is not part of the suit, she\xe2\x80\x99s been outspoken on the subject. \xe2\x80\x9cThis isn\xe2\x80\x99t just a female athlete\xe2\x80\x99s story; this is every single woman\xe2\x80\x99s story on planet Earth,\xe2\x80\x9d she said in September. \xe2\x80\x9cWomen lose our very lives because of this pay gap inequity, and in order to get it back we have to fight.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In \xe2\x80\x9cWolfpack,\xe2\x80\x9d Wambach offers eight new rules to help women succeed professionally and personally. And she hopes her ideas trigger a domino effect. \xe2\x80\x9cWhen one person stands up and demands the ball, the job, the promotion, the paycheck, the microphone, that one gives others permission to do the same,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. '
b'Here are the four of her \xe2\x80\x9cnew rules,\xe2\x80\x9d and the norms she hopes they\xe2\x80\x99ll upend. '
b'______'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cChampion each other.\xe2\x80\x9d '
b'Old Rule: Be against each other. '
b'New Rule: Be FOR each other.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cPower and success and joy are not pies,\xe2\x80\x9d Wambach writes. \xe2\x80\x9cA bigger slice for one woman doesn\xe2\x80\x99t mean a smaller slice for another.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'______'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cBe grateful and ambitious.\xe2\x80\x9d '
b'Old Rule: Be grateful for what you have. '
b'New Rule: Be grateful for what you have AND demand what you deserve.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI was so grateful for a paycheck, so grateful to represent my country, so grateful to be the token woman at the table, so grateful to receive any respect at all that I was afraid to use my voice to demand more,\xe2\x80\x9d Wambach writes. \xe2\x80\x9cOur gratitude is how power uses the tokenism of a few women to keep the rest of us in line.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'______'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMake failure your fuel.\xe2\x80\x9d '
b'Old Rule: Failure means you\xe2\x80\x99re out of the game. '
b'New Rule: Failure means you\xe2\x80\x99re finally IN the game.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cImperfect men have been empowered and permitted to run the world since the beginning of time,\xe2\x80\x9d Wambach writes. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s time for imperfect women to grant themselves permission to join them.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'______'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cLead from the bench.\xe2\x80\x9d '
b'Old Rule: Wait for permission to lead. '
b'New Rule: Lead now \xe2\x80\x94 from wherever you are.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe picture of leadership is not just a man at the head of a table,\xe2\x80\x9d Wambach writes. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s also every woman who is allowing her own voice to guide her life and the lives of those she cares about.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'What would happen if women gained the same physical strength as men? That was the question posed in an 1870 article in The New York Times titled \xe2\x80\x9cMuscular Women\xe2\x80\x9d (!). '
b'The answer, according to the opponents of equal rights at the time, would be a disruption of the natural order of things, meaning women would exert their strength to take down men physically and mentally. '

b'By Tariq Panja'
b'LONDON \xe2\x80\x94 The group entrusted with conducting the surprisingly difficult search for a candidate to run English soccer\xe2\x80\x99s Premier League has received another rejection from an executive for whom the opportunity would appear to have been a step up.'
b'Earlier this year, the league approached Christian Seifert, chief executive of Germany\xe2\x80\x99s Bundesliga, to see if he would like to step into the shoes of Richard Scudamore, the towering figure under whose leadership England\xe2\x80\x99s top flight managed to become by far the world\xe2\x80\x99s most popular soccer league, not to mention its richest.'
b'Seifert briefly thought about the idea before dismissing it, according to people with knowledge of his thinking. He is focused on managing the next set of broadcast rights sales as Germany\xe2\x80\x99s league competes with Spain\xe2\x80\x99s La Liga in the battle for second place behind the Premier League, said the people, who were not authorized to speak about it publicly.'
b'A spokeswoman for the Bundesliga and Seifert declined to comment. A Premier League spokesman said the league did not comment on names linked to the role.'
b'The search for Scudamore\xe2\x80\x99s replacement has shined a harsh light on the search team, led by Chelsea\xe2\x80\x99s chairman, Bruce Buck, entrusted to find the former advertising executive\xe2\x80\x99s replacement. Last year, the group announced the appointment of Susanna Dinnage, a senior executive at Discovery Communications, before she abruptly changed her mind in late December. That left the league scrambling for a second option. A raft of names have since been linked to the post, but the search continues without any sign of an imminent appointment.'
b'At a league board meeting, which was attended by a mix of owners and executives from the Premier League\xe2\x80\x99s 20 teams, those in attendance were told that the search group, which has hired the U.K. headhunting firm Spencer Stuart to help with the process, has interviewed a final group of six candidates who will be shortlisted to three by the end of the month.'
b'Scudamore\xe2\x80\x99s replacement will find an increasingly busy inbox, as well as a challenging media climate, as the league attempts to at least keep pace with the multibillion-dollar deals that have fueled its rise. The Premier League recently joined counterparts across Europe in voicing concerns about plans by some of the continent\xe2\x80\x99s top clubs to restructure the elite Champions League, changes that risk diminishing the value and relevance of domestic soccer.'
b'The new boss must also manage tension between the league\xe2\x80\x99s biggest clubs \xe2\x80\x94 a group of six that includes Manchester United, Arsenal and Liverpool, who have owners from the United States and who are constantly fighting for a larger slice of income at the expense of the rest of the competition. He or she will also be faced with as yet unknown challenges created by the United Kingdom\xe2\x80\x99s decision to leave the European Union.'
b'But even without a leader, the Premier League continues to provide a compelling product for its worldwide fan base, with this season\xe2\x80\x99s title race set to go to the wire as Manchester City and Liverpool match each other point for point into the final games, while the next four teams are involved in an equally tight fight for the final two qualification places for next season\xe2\x80\x99s Champions League.'
b'The delay, though, has been frustrating for some of the league\xe2\x80\x99s staff and companies that do business with it. They had grown used to Scudamore\xe2\x80\x99s decisive management style. For instance, the Premier League recently scrapped a multimillion-dollar agreement with Facebook to broadcast games in four Asian countries after failing to finalize the agreement. An executive involved in the talks, who had completed contracts with Scudamore in the past, said the leadership void did not help the process.'

b'By Tariq Panja'
b'Two days after fans in the United Arab Emirates threw shoes at rival players during a 4-0 loss in the semifinals to Qatar at the Asian Cup, the country\xe2\x80\x99s soccer federation has taken direct aim at the team itself.'
b'Organizers of the Asian Cup said on Thursday that they would respond to an official complaint lodged by Emirates soccer officials, who charged that two members of the Qatari team were ineligible to play in the region\xe2\x80\x99s biggest tournament.'
b'The players \xe2\x80\x94 Almoez Ali, a Sudan-born striker, and Bassam al-Rawi, a defender born in Iraq \xe2\x80\x94 are fixtures in Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s lineup. Ali is the tournament\xe2\x80\x99s top scorer, with eight goals in six games, and al-Rawi scored the goal that sent Qatar to the quarterfinals.'
b'The complaint is the latest salvo in a bitter dispute between the Gulf neighbors that goes far beyond soccer. The Emirates is part of a two-year-old, Saudi-led blockade of Qatar, driven by a belief that its neighbor is financing terrorism and growing too close to Iran, Saudi Arabia\xe2\x80\x99s biggest regional rival; Qatar has denied playing any role in supporting terrorist groups.'
b'The dispute has already manifested itself in ways small and large in the tournament, which now represents Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s biggest success on the soccer field.'
b'One consequence of the dispute is that there are no direct flights from Doha to Abu Dhabi, so Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s team had to fly through Oman on its way to the event, and Qatari fans \xe2\x80\x94 unable to travel to the Emirates without permission \xe2\x80\x94 are largely absent at the team\xe2\x80\x99s matches.'
b'But Qatar, which has never qualified for a World Cup but will host the event in 2022, has been the surprise of the field. It will play Japan in the final on Friday.'
b'But even as Qatar marched through the field, rumors \xe2\x80\x94 fueled by a close reading of FIFA nationality rules \xe2\x80\x94 swirled about the eligibility of Ali and al-Rawi.'
b'The silence of Qatari officials on the issue has only led to more rumors. A spokesman for the team has not responded to repeated requests for comment, while FIFA, the global governing body for soccer, has said the matter falls under the jurisdiction of the tournament organizer, the Asian Football Confederation.'
b'The A.F.C. had said that it would intervene only an official complaint were filed. That complaint arrived in the aftermath of the Emirates\xe2\x80\x99 humiliating defeat in front of its own fans in Abu Dhabi on Tuesday.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe Asian Football Confederation has a received a protest from the United Arab Emirates F.A. regarding the eligibility of two Qatar players,\xe2\x80\x9d the A.F.C. said in a statement on Thursday. \xe2\x80\x9cThis protest will now be reviewed in line with the A.F.C. regulations.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The A.F.C. declined to identify the possible punishment for Qatar. Teams that have previously fielded ineligible players have forfeited games, but the situation has never come up at the final stages of a major international event.'
b'Under soccer\xe2\x80\x99s regulations, players are only eligible for a national team outside of their country of birth if they have lived there for five continuous years after turning 18. Al-Rawi is 21 and Ali is 22. The rules make an exception that permits players to represent a country if a parent or grandparent was born there; many countries, including the United States, regularly take advantage of the exception.'
b'Qatar has been trawling the world for talent for years in preparation for the 2022 World Cup, embarking on perhaps the most extensive talent identification program in history, one that involved the creation of training programs for youngsters from Africa and an academy for the best prospects in Doha.'
b'Officials in the country have said in the past that the program does not require those scouted to pick Qatar over their birth countries. Though born in Sudan, Ali has lived in Qatar since he was a child. Al-Rawi\xe2\x80\x99s father once represented Iraq internationally.'
b'Still, Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s squads at the youth and senior levels have included several expatriate players, and the eligibility was not questioned when Ali and al-Rawi represented the country at previous tournaments sanctioned by FIFA and the A.F.C.'
b'It was not clear why the Emirates, or any of Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s other opponents \xe2\x80\x94 including Saudi Arabia, which lost to Qatar, 2-0 \xe2\x80\x94 did not raise the issue until after the semifinal.'
b'The victories over the Saudis and the Emirates were greeted by scenes of jubilation in Qatar, where fans draped in the country\xe2\x80\x99s flag took to the streets of Doha to celebrate the victories.'
b'For the hosts, the defeat was particularly painful given the efforts it had made to create a partisan atmosphere inside Abu Dhabi\xe2\x80\x99s Zayed Sports City Stadium. Local organizers distributed thousands of free tickets to what it described as \xe2\x80\x9cloyal\xe2\x80\x9d fans before the game.'
b'For the A.F.C., the issue also raises another political issue. Its president, Sheikh Salman bin Ibrahim al-Khalifa of Bahrain, is being challenged for his post by candidates from the Emirates and Qatar.'
b'The organization has opened a separate investigation over the shoe- and bottle-throwing incidents that marred the semifinal. That case could lead to sanctions.'

b'By Andrew Das'
b'Don Garber, who in two decades as commissioner has overseen a wave of expansion that has more than doubled the size of Major League Soccer, has signed a five-year contract extension that will keep him in charge of the league through the 2023 season.'
b'The league announced the new contract on Thursday. Garber\xe2\x80\x99s previous deal expired after last season, but he had widely been expected to remain in his post. Garber, 61, also will continue in his role as the chairman of Soccer United Marketing, the league\xe2\x80\x99s powerful \xe2\x80\x94 and profitable \xe2\x80\x94 marketing arm.'
b'A former N.F.L. executive, Garber was recruited to join M.L.S. by the N.F.L. owners Robert Kraft and Lamar Hunt, who also owned teams in the then-fledgling soccer league.'
b'Garber took over a 12-team M.L.S. in August 1999, and among his first moves was to close the league\xe2\x80\x99s two Florida franchises, in Tampa Bay and Miami. The decision reduced the league\xe2\x80\x99s roster to 10 teams and raised questions about its viability as a national league.'
b'But in the two decades that followed, Garber led the league on a wave of expansion \xe2\x80\x94 first two teams in 2005, and then a steady flow of at least one new team a year from 2007 to 2012. That burst of growth included the additions of three teams in Canada, in Toronto, Vancouver and Montreal.'
b'All the while, he tinkered with the league\xe2\x80\x99s roster and salary rules, recruited global stars like David Beckham and persuaded the owners to invest in player development and new stadiums. M.L.S. had one soccer-specific stadium in 1999; by this summer, 20 of its teams will play in facilities they control.'
b'Garber\xe2\x80\x99s tenure has not been trouble-free. Critics point to the league\xe2\x80\x99s centralized control of player contracts and Soccer United Marketing\xe2\x80\x99s influence with U.S. Soccer as hampering the growth of the domestic game, and Garber once openly feuded with the former United States national team coach Jurgen Klinsmann after the coach criticized the league.'
b'But there is little question that Garber\xe2\x80\x99s tenure has transformed the league. The league now has national sponsors and television contracts that bring its games to 170 countries. Twenty-four teams will play in M.L.S. this year, including a new one in Cincinnati, and three more ownership groups have been approved to enter the league by 2021.'
b'One of them, led by Beckham, will bring the league back to the Miami market it once abandoned.'
