b'Inside the List'
b'By Tina Jordan'
b'Back in 2016, the soccer legend Abby Wambach was honored at the ESPY Awards with two other newly retired athletes, Kobe Bryant and Peyton Manning.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAs I watched those men walk off the stage,\xe2\x80\x9d she writes in \xe2\x80\x9cWolfpack\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 a women\xe2\x80\x99s advice book inspired by her viral 2018 commencement speech at Barnard \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cit dawned on me that while the three of us were stepping away from similar careers, we were facing very different futures\xe2\x80\x9d because of salary disparities. She says now, \xe2\x80\x9cI realized that their hustling days were over but mine were just beginning. And that\xe2\x80\x99s when I finally acknowledged what had been simmering inside me for years: anger.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That was the night Wambach became an activist. \xe2\x80\x9cBecause women are told in a million different ways that the only thing they are allowed to do is be grateful,\xe2\x80\x9d she says. She\xe2\x80\x99s not just talking about sports: \xe2\x80\x9cThe truth is that on average every woman in every industry in every state and every country around the world will earn significantly less than men in equivalent positions throughout her career.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Wambach has never calculated what being a female athlete cost her in actual dollars, \xe2\x80\x9cbut I\xe2\x80\x99ve imagined it in terms of freedom, because dollars represent respect, and deliver freedom,\xe2\x80\x9d she says. \xe2\x80\x9cIf you work the same as a man, but you don\xe2\x80\x99t earn what he earns because of institutionalized discrimination, then \xe2\x80\x94 at the end of a day, and the end of a career \xe2\x80\x94 you have less freedom than he does.\xe2\x80\x9d Though the U.S. Soccer Federation \xe2\x80\x9cinvests more in the men\xe2\x80\x99s program, the women still earn more for the federation, and are paid significantly less,\xe2\x80\x9d she points out, adding that she\xe2\x80\x99s proud of the American women\xe2\x80\x99s team for recently filing a lawsuit over this discrimination.'
b'[ Read about the long history of pay discrimination in sports. ]'
b'For Wambach, being an activist means two things. \xe2\x80\x9cFirst, it\xe2\x80\x99s using my platform and privilege to pursue change that is too risky for others to call for,\xe2\x80\x9d she says. \xe2\x80\x9cSecond, it\xe2\x80\x99s encouraging people to become active in their own lives.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThroughout my 20 years of training and playing professionally, there was a moment in every soccer game when I\xe2\x80\x99d feel the energy shift toward me,\xe2\x80\x9d she explains. \xe2\x80\x9cWhether it was a morale boost, a momentum swing or a goal that we needed \xe2\x80\x94 it was my job to make it happen. When I felt that shift, I\xe2\x80\x99d say silently to myself: Let\xe2\x80\x99s go, Abby. It\xe2\x80\x99s your time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'She wants \xe2\x80\x9cWolfpack,\xe2\x80\x9d which enters the advice and how-to list this week at No. 3, to empower other women to do the same thing \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cto embrace and step into those monumental everyday moments.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'On SOCCER'
b'Tottenham will open its billion-dollar stadium on Wednesday, an arena the club hopes will be a catalyst for the revival of its entire neighborhood. But not everyone is certain they will be included in those plans. '
b'By Rory Smith'
b'LONDON \xe2\x80\x94 Standing outside the Lilywhites Sandwich Bar, Ali Demirci pointed, proudly, to the fresh paint on the window frame. Its color was one of those on-trend grays from an upscale catalog, with a name like Elephant\xe2\x80\x99s Breath or Slipper Satin. \xe2\x80\x9cThe club came and did it,\xe2\x80\x9d Demirci said. He glanced upward to the other minor alteration to the shop he owned until a few weeks ago: a bright white sign. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I installed that myself.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'On the other side of the road, the change has been rather more drastic. The window seats at the Lilywhites Sandwich Bar now offer a view of the gleaming glass frontage of the $1 billion, state-of-the-art stadium that \xe2\x80\x94 starting Wednesday evening, when it hosts its inaugural Premier League game \xe2\x80\x94 Tottenham Hotspur will call home.'
b'The territory is, of course, familiar: The new stadium is on the same patch of land as the atmospheric, historic, old White Hart Lane, where Spurs played for 118 years. The horizon, though, is different: the club hopes the new stadium represents not just a great leap forward for Spurs \xe2\x80\x94 proof, in concrete and steel, that this team belongs among Europe\xe2\x80\x99s pre-eminent powers \xe2\x80\x94 but for English soccer as a whole.'
b'Chris Lee, its chief architect, said he had looked at some 300 stadiums around the world for inspiration and incorporated the best elements he could find into what he labeled the \xe2\x80\x9cbest\xe2\x80\x9d stadium on the planet: an arena supposed to be more modern than Wembley, sleeker than Old Trafford, bigger (crucially) than Arsenal\xe2\x80\x99s home at the Emirates. It is supposed to set what Daniel Levy, the Spurs chairman, described as a \xe2\x80\x9cnew standard\xe2\x80\x9d for sports stadiums.'
b'The arena\xe2\x80\x99s centerpiece is the biggest single-tier stand in England, capable of holding 17,500 fans, modeled on Borussia Dortmund\xe2\x80\x99s S\xc3\xbcdtribune \xe2\x80\x94 known, more commonly, as the Yellow Wall. It claims to be home to the longest bar in Europe. It has a retractable field, allowing it to host not only Premier League matches but N.F.L. games, too. It has its own microbrewery and a restaurant run by a Michelin-starred chef. And, in what is surely a first for a soccer team, Spurs will have its own on-site sommelier.'
b'The appeal for Levy and the club, of course, is the financial boost all of that can bring: more fans, spending more time and more money, all of it flowing straight into the team\xe2\x80\x99s coffers. Levy said Tuesday that, with the extra revenue generated by the stadium, Spurs\xe2\x80\x99 income would be in the world\xe2\x80\x99s top 10.'
b'This is a team that has long had to wheel and deal in the transfer market. On Sunday, the club\xe2\x80\x99s manager, Mauricio Pochettino, admitted he and his staff had laughed at the sight of Naby Keita and Fabinho, \xc2\xa3100 million worth of talent combined, on Liverpool\xe2\x80\x99s bench when the teams met, representing a luxury way beyond Spurs\xe2\x80\x99 means. Tottenham\xe2\x80\x99s new home is, in time, supposed to change that, to turn Spurs into a club that can compete with the elite not just on the field, but off it.'
b'The effects of the stadium, though, will resonate beyond Spurs\xe2\x80\x99 balance sheet. The club has long claimed it can be a \xe2\x80\x9ccatalyst\xe2\x80\x9d for the regeneration of the neighborhood around it. At a news media presentation on Tuesday, the club\xe2\x80\x99s executive director, Donna Cullen, opened with a photograph of a burning car: a reminder of the riots that scarred the area \xe2\x80\x94 before spreading across the capital and the country \xe2\x80\x94 in 2011.'
b'That hot, angry summer, Cullen said, was the \xe2\x80\x9ctrigger\xe2\x80\x9d for Spurs to think about what it could do to improve not only its own horizons, but those of the place it represents. The area around Tottenham, Haringey, is the fifth-most deprived borough in London, she said: The club was taken over by a spirit of \xe2\x80\x9clet\xe2\x80\x99s see what we can do.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The local authority, Haringay Council, does not entirely accept the idea that Tottenham\xe2\x80\x99s rebirth rests on the stadium. Charles Adje, the councilor responsible for regeneration, said he would not use the word \xe2\x80\x9ccatalyst\xe2\x80\x9d himself, but he acknowledged that it \xe2\x80\x9cadds value to the area.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Both the club and the council project that the new stadium could pour around \xc2\xa3293 million a year into the local economy; Spurs estimated that it would be responsible for more than 1,700 jobs. \xe2\x80\x9cThis stadium and this new club is going to make a massive, massive difference to the people of Tottenham,\xe2\x80\x9d David Lammy, Tottenham\xe2\x80\x99s member of Parliament, said this week.'
b'That, too, will take time, of course. So far, the main visible differences to Tottenham High Road are the new facades on the sandwich bar, the convenience store and a handful of other properties across from the stadium. The streets running to and from it are, otherwise, much the same as always: a jumble of jerk chicken places and nail bars, Polish supermarkets and tumbledown mechanics.'
b'Smoking a cigarette outside the barbershop he has run for 25 years, Inan Gulecyuz said he was happy to wait. The stadium opening is, technically, bad news for him: Business drops on game days, he said, and with soccer and the N.F.L. to fit in, he will lose a little trade.'
b'That will, he hopes, be offset by the benefits it will bring. \xe2\x80\x9cThey have changed a lot of the shops just up the road,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cHopefully the same thing will happen down the road, too.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'A little further from the stadium, Irfan Sahin was serving coffee in Fieldseat, his delicatessen, caf\xc3\xa9, bookshop and organic food market. Soft classical music played overhead.'
b'Sahin said that he expected the stadium to alter the character of the area, to encourage more businesses to open \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cThere is no other Michelin-starred restaurant in north London,\xe2\x80\x9d he noted \xe2\x80\x94 but then, he said, Tottenham is changing anyway: In London, gentrification is a constant tide, regardless of where soccer clubs play.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt is very different from when I first came here in 2001,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is slow, of course: We had two gang fights right outside in the last year or so. But there are more places opening all of the time: bars and pubs and caf\xc3\xa9s and restaurants. It is not as expensive as central London, or as expensive as east London, so it is a good place to open. Hopefully it will be better with the stadium.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Academic literature is unclear on whether that will hold true. Writing in the Journal of Economic Perspectives in 2000, John Siegfried and Andrew Zimbalist concluded \xe2\x80\x94 based largely on case studies in the United States \xe2\x80\x94 that while \xe2\x80\x9cteam owners have argued that sports facilities boost local economic activity, economic reasoning and empirical evidence suggest the opposite.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'There are those in Tottenham, certainly, who feel disenfranchised by the speed of change and by redevelopment proposals backed by the council and the club. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere is a real risk of companies going out of business if we cannot find alternative locations in the neighborhood,\xe2\x80\x9d said Feruk Tepeyurt, the owner of a local joinery firm and chairman of the Peacock Industrial Estate, home to more than 50 small businesses but, under both the council\xe2\x80\x99s plans and a separate project proposed by the club, scheduled to become a park. \xe2\x80\x9cDo we need a park, or do we need a community of small businesses, a lot of them run by local, black and minority ethnic people?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That is the tension inherent in any regeneration, of course: the issue of who, precisely, it is supposed to work for, of whose needs it is meeting. \xe2\x80\x9cThere is a thin dividing line between seeing the stadium as a catalyst for regeneration and a Trojan horse for social cleansing,\xe2\x80\x9d said Mark Panton, an academic at Birkbeck College who has written extensively on the dispute.'
b'There is one change left to come: Transport for London, the capital\xe2\x80\x99s transit authority, is expected to accept a proposal to rename White Hart Lane, the nearest train station to the stadium, to Tottenham Hotspur.'
b'It is not unprecedented \xe2\x80\x94 Arsenal has had its own tube stop, dating to the 1930s \xe2\x80\x94 but nor is it universally popular. The objection is based on the idea that erasing the station\xe2\x80\x99s name wipes clean a century or so of history; that it needlessly, ham-fistedly conflates the identities of Tottenham the area and Tottenham the team; that it creates the impression, deep down, below the fresh coats of paint, that the place exists to serve the club, rather than the club existing to reflect the place.'
b'Rory Smith is the chief soccer correspondent, based in Manchester, England. He covers all aspects of European soccer and has reported from three World Cups, the Olympics, and numerous European tournaments.  @RorySmith '
b'Advertisement'
b'Advertisement'
b'Supported by'
b'By Steve Brenner'
b'MIAMI \xe2\x80\x94 When David Beckham, the former captain of England\xe2\x80\x99s national team, announced his intention to bring a Major League Soccer team to South Florida at a rousing event in downtown Miami five years ago, the excitement was palpable.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI remember thinking how amazing it was going to be,\xe2\x80\x9d said Cesar Molero, who runs a fan club named Vice City 1896.'
b'When Beckham returned last year for a similar event, where he and many M.L.S. executives were joined by a group of deep-pocketed local investors, there were new plans, new promises and new colors on the scarves.'
b'By September, Beckham\xe2\x80\x99s expansion team had a new name (Inter Miami) and a new logo (with twin herons). By January, its new team president had put together the core of a technical staff.'
b'And on Wednesday, M.L.S. Commissioner Don Garber confirmed what he had been saying for months: that he has the \xe2\x80\x9cutmost confidence\xe2\x80\x9d that Beckham\xe2\x80\x99s group will produce a team that is a worthy successor to recent M.L.S. start-ups in Atlanta and Los Angeles.'
b'But just over a year before Inter Miami is set to take the field for the first time, its road is not without obstacles. Battles in the courtroom and with powerful residents of South Florida have blocked its progress more than once. The team is working on its fifth potential stadium site, with no assurances that this one will be the last, and is facing multiple lawsuits seeking to block the club\xe2\x80\x99s right to acquire the property.'
b'Even the most passionate followers of the team \xe2\x80\x94 who are united more around an idea than anything tangible \xe2\x80\x94 have been pulled in different directions. The cause of their split is the most basic of disputes: They disagreed over what their group should be called.'
b'The original fan group \xe2\x80\x94 known as the Southern Legion \xe2\x80\x94 was also the largest, with more than 400 dues-paying members. But last year it sought to rename itself The Siege.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe felt a change was appropriate once we saw the crest,\xe2\x80\x9d said Max Ramos, a founding member of the Southern Legion. \xe2\x80\x9cA group of herons is called a siege. It felt right.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Those who felt otherwise split off and kept the original name. Ramos insisted there were no hard feelings. The amicable split, he said, is a sign of the camaraderie that has helped fans remain steadfast in their dedication to Beckham\xe2\x80\x99s grand, but at times excruciatingly fluid, plan.'
b'There is no turning back at this point, anyway. Last year, Beckham and his new group of well-financed, well-connected investors were finally granted the rights to an expansion place in the league. Satisfied that doubts about a stadium plan and the Beckham group\xe2\x80\x99s resources and local commitment had been resolved, the commissioner confirmed that the team would enter M.L.S. in the 2020 season.'
b'The matter of where it will make that debut, however, is a bit more complicated.'
b'Inter Miami has been the focus of a stream of legal action in recent months, with issues including an ethics complaint related to the owners\xe2\x80\x99 political lobbying, disputes about the feasibility of building a stadium on its preferred site and the legality of public votes on the matter.'
b'Thwarted at several downtown locations, the team now has its sights on creating Miami Freedom Park, a $1 billion complex spread over 160 acres at Melreese Country Club, a city-owned golf course near Miami International Airport. Critics have ridiculed the proposal as a real estate deal with a 25,000-seat soccer stadium included, but a larger problem may lurk underneath the golf course: Last July, it was revealed that it sits atop a toxic waste dump.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere are so many holes in their plans \xe2\x80\x94 it\xe2\x80\x99s unreal,\xe2\x80\x9d said David Winker, a Florida-based lawyer who has filed two lawsuits against Beckham\xe2\x80\x99s franchise in the past five months.'
b'Winker described himself as a soccer fan eager to take his family to matches when the team begins play \xe2\x80\x94 Florida International University could serve as a temporary home while the legal fights continue \xe2\x80\x94 but not, he said, at any cost.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI was immediately suspicious of how the deal was being conducted \xe2\x80\x94 behind closed-door negotiations and in a frantic rush,\xe2\x80\x9d Winker added, calling it \xe2\x80\x9cjust a terrible way to introduce a new sports team to Miami.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Still, in November, it appeared that Beckham, his ownership group and M.L.S. had finally cleared the last hurdle. Amid songs, drumbeats and free paella on Election Day, Beckham and his new partners \xe2\x80\x94 including Jose and Jorge Mas, the Miami-based construction magnates; Masayoshi Son, the billionaire Japanese owner of SoftBank; Marcelo Claure, the former chief executive of Sprint telecommunications; and the pop-music mogul Simon Fuller \xe2\x80\x94 celebrated victory in a public referendum that had granted them the right to enter into a noncompete bidding process for the Melreese property.'
b'Just 24 hours later, however, those negotiations were frozen because of an ethics complaint filed by Winker after he noticed that of all the people who spoke on behalf of the project before the city commission that will decide its fate, none had properly registered as a lobbyist. Those speakers included the aunt of the commission\xe2\x80\x99s chairman, Keon Hardemon.'
b'Although the Miami-Dade County ethics commission issued a letter last month advising that the negotiations over a 99-year lease on the golf course site could move forward while an investigation continued, problems persist.'
b'Winker filed a lawsuit in which he argued that city documents provided an unclear land description, and that the city should be prohibited from using the referendum as authorization to negotiate a no-bid lease. Ordinarily, he said, that type of sale would be open to bids.'
b'A separate lawsuit by Bruce C. Matheson, a wealthy landowner in South Florida, also took aim at the referendum. Matheson had previously filed suit to block a stadium planned for the Overtown neighborhood of Miami, near where he owns property.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cEach plan seems more convoluted than the last,\xe2\x80\x9d Matheson said this month.'
b'Victoria Mendez, the city\xe2\x80\x99s lawyer, told The Miami Herald last month that the actions filed by Winker and Matheson did not \xe2\x80\x9cdepict a clear understanding of our codes.\xe2\x80\x9d M.L.S. continues to express its support; in November, Garber hailed the victory in the stadium referendum as \xe2\x80\x9ca historic day for the sport in our country.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Inter Miami, meanwhile, is plowing ahead.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe baseless and frivolous lawsuits/complaints will not deter any of our efforts and focus,\xe2\x80\x9d Jorge Mas wrote in an email. \xe2\x80\x9cThese are sideshows and a nonissue to our plan.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Beckham, who is based in London, has placed confidence in his local partners to navigate the political and legal waters of South Florida.'
b'The team\xe2\x80\x99s fans appear to be doing the same.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cOnce we begin playing next year,\xe2\x80\x9d said Ramos, the Siege leader, \xe2\x80\x9ceverything else will be forgotten.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'By Tariq Panja'
b'LONDON \xe2\x80\x94 Confronted with what they consider a power play by a group of wealthy soccer clubs to promote the Champions League at the expense of national championships, representatives of Europe\xe2\x80\x99s domestic leagues will meet in Lisbon this week to discuss a strategy to protect what they say is decades of tradition, and a basic sense of fairness.'
b'What the leagues fear, several officials said, is what they consider a behind-the-scenes campaign to reshape European soccer for the exclusive benefit of the continent\xe2\x80\x99s biggest clubs. The leagues contend the proposed changes to the Champions League, which include new barriers to entry for nonelite clubs and schedule changes that would push matches onto weekend dates, will diminish the relevance and marketability of domestic leagues, and potentially render many of their matches irrelevant.'
b'At this week\xe2\x80\x99s Lisbon meeting, an annual gathering of the umbrella European Leagues group, members will discuss plans to fight back \xe2\x80\x94 perhaps even in court \xe2\x80\x94 against suggested changes that they argue will adversely affect the competitions that still form the cultural and financial backbone of the global soccer industry. The coalition of leagues is a diverse group \xe2\x80\x94 leagues from Portugal to Ukraine are members \xe2\x80\x94 but a potentially formidable one given the influence and resources of members like England\xe2\x80\x99s Premier League, Germany\xe2\x80\x99s Bundesliga and Spain\xe2\x80\x99s La Liga.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe association of European Leagues is raising its voice and the leagues are cohesive more than ever in the defense and protection of domestic football,\xe2\x80\x9d said Alberto Colombo, the deputy general secretary of the European league body, in an interview.'
b'While representatives of the continent\xe2\x80\x99s richest and most powerful clubs and European soccer\xe2\x80\x99s governing body, UEFA, say any discussions for reforming club competitions like the Champions League remain in their infancy, league officials have grown increasingly concerned about details of the proposed changes that have started to leak.'
b'The most dramatic include reducing the size of national leagues and altering their schedules to allow European games to be played on weekends, a window historically reserved for domestic matches. The Bundesliga\xe2\x80\x99s chief executive called weekend Champions League matches a \xe2\x80\x9cred line\xe2\x80\x9d that could not be crossed. English officials similarly declared the idea a nonstarter.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt is the role of the Premier League and other English football organizations to govern the format of league and cup competitions in this country,\xe2\x80\x9d the Premier League spokesman Nick Noble said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt would be wholly inappropriate for European football bodies to create plans that would alter the structure of domestic English football.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Other proposals would see access to the Champions League itself severely restricted, with only 8 of 32 participants allowed to earn their places through success in domestic competition the previous season. The other 24 places would be reserved for teams already in the Champions League, or a handful of participants from a second-tier European club competition.'
b'Andrea Agnelli, the president of Juventus, who leads the powerful European Club Association, said at that group\xe2\x80\x99s annual meeting in Amsterdam last week that it would be at least a year before any changes would be finalized, and he refused to discuss details of proposals already under discussion. However, in an interview with The Guardian last year, he described reforms he would like to see that appear to be similar to those currently under discussion.'
b'While the E.C.A. represents more than 200 clubs from across Europe, it is increasingly dominated by a handful of the largest teams. That group includes the likes of Juventus and Bayern Munich but also heavyweights from Spain and England like Barcelona, Real Madrid and Manchester United. Those clubs have for years used their might \xe2\x80\x94 and threats to break away and form an exclusive competition outside the current domestic league structure \xe2\x80\x94 to wrest concessions from soccer\xe2\x80\x99s leaders.'
b'Javier Tebas, the frequently outspoken head of Spain\xe2\x80\x99s top league, said the proposal to restructure continental competitions for the benefit of the small group of rich clubs that already dominate them would spell doom for soccer in large parts of Europe. The changes would, Tebas said, allow the wealthiest clubs to widen the massive talent and resource gap they already enjoy, and tear away the fabric of the sport\xe2\x80\x99s traditions.'
b'Playing European competition matches on the weekend, in particular, would be \xe2\x80\x9ca recipe for the demise of football across Europe,\xe2\x80\x9d Tebas said in a statement. The Bundesliga\xe2\x80\x99s chief executive, Christian Seifert, concurred in a speech earlier this year.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe weekend must belong to the national leagues,\xe2\x80\x9d Seifert said. \xe2\x80\x9cThey are the heart and soul of professional football.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Access to the Champions League is currently linked to performance in domestic leagues, but under one set of proposals that could change drastically, with most participating teams allowed to compete year after year regardless of their league positions. In one plan, Europe\xe2\x80\x99s top 32 teams would be divided into four groups of eight teams, with the top four each season advancing to a knockout round to determine the winner.'
b'Such a change would dramatically reduce the attractiveness of national leagues for broadcasters, where the battle to qualify for European club competitions has long been part of the narrative sold to television companies. At times, in fact, the battle for Champions League positions has often been more compelling than the race for the title, which in some countries is often wrapped up months before the end of the campaign.'
b'Agnelli hinted that, in the future, qualification could be based on success within European competitions \xe2\x80\x94 a setup that would maximize places for teams already in, and serve as a significant barrier to clubs trying to break in.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt is certainly something that is logical,\xe2\x80\x9d he said when asked if teams could be promoted or relegated within a closed European system. The proposals could transform soccer\xe2\x80\x99s top club competition into one that resembles a similar event in European basketball, where 11 of the 16 teams in the EuroLeague are guaranteed spots regardless of their domestic performances.'
b'For the biggest clubs, a closed-off Champions League would offer financial certainty. But the leagues are vowing to defend a structure that currently allows any team the opportunity to win \xe2\x80\x94 on the field \xe2\x80\x94 a place among the giants.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe leagues defend the basic values of the European sport model, based on sporting merits, an open-access pyramid structure where all clubs form the foundation and all clubs could live the dream to reach the top,\xe2\x80\x9d said Colombo, of the European league body.'
b'While the top clubs have forged close links to UEFA thanks to a deepening friendship between Agnelli, the E.C.A. leader, and UEFA\xe2\x80\x99s president, Aleksander Ceferin, the leagues \xe2\x80\x94 faced with a critical leadership void at a vital moment \xe2\x80\x94 have struggled to present a cohesive opposing voice. The Premier League, for example, remains without a leader after stumbling in its search for a replacement for its longtime chief executive Richard Scudamore, who retired last year. And Lars-Christer Olsson, the chairman of the European League body, has only recently recovered from a serious illness.'

b'By Tariq Panja'
b'Not so long ago the idea of merely setting foot in the United States would have filled FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s leaders with dread. The idea of holding an important meeting there would have been rejected as absurd.'
b'That was because a sprawling corruption indictment by the United States Department of Justice in 2015 had threatened the very existence of FIFA, the governing body of world soccer. The investigation had produced the dawn arrests of more than a dozen top power brokers in the sport and eventually led to the ouster of some of the organization\xe2\x80\x99s most powerful figures. It left others fearful of traveling to the United States for any reason, lest they risk being picked up by the authorities.'
b'Yet this week, almost four years later, FIFA is bringing the members of its governing council \xe2\x80\x94 a body that, in an earlier incarnation, was accused by the American authorities of engaging in graft schemes dating back decades \xe2\x80\x94 to United States soil for the first time since the scandal broke. The 37-member body, an expanded group now known as the FIFA Council, will hold a meeting in Miami on Friday to discuss, among other things, a significant expansion of the 2022 World Cup and a multibillion-dollar plan for a new World Cup-style competition for clubs.'
b'The site of the meeting, FIFA says, is the latest sign that it has moved on from its corrupt past.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s probably fair to say that there is a symbolic significance for the FIFA Council to meet in the U.S.A. for the first time since 2015,\xe2\x80\x9d FIFA, which is based in Zurich, said in a statement.'
b'Four years ago, images of police officers leading soccer officials out of a luxury Swiss hotel in two separate dawn raids gripped the sporting world, unleashing a crisis that has cost FIFA millions of dollars and led to years of turmoil. Dozens of soccer officials, businessmen and companies have since pleaded guilty to charges in United States courts; others are fighting extradition; and two men, including the former head of South American soccer, were jailed after a 2017 trial in New York. The crisis also led to the ouster of a number of executives not named in the indictments, including FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s longtime president at the time, Joseph S. Blatter.'
b'While there is little sign another blockbuster raid is in the offing, United States authorities\xe2\x80\x99 interest in FIFA has not dimmed. Multiple defendants who have pleaded guilty in the case have not yet been sentenced, with prosecutors again agreeing this year to push back decisions about the punishments of at least five people, including an Argentine businessman who testified at the New York trial and has served as a key cooperating witness.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cFIFA remains ready to assist public authorities in all cases and, while the experience was difficult, we are finally very grateful that the U.S. Department of Justice intervened when it did to address some serious governance problems and, in so doing, help put FIFA on the path to reform,\xe2\x80\x9d its statement added.'
b'The current leadership has attempted to build bridges with the American authorities. FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s top legal official, the deputy secretary general Alasdair Bell, made it a priority to visit Brooklyn and meet with prosecutors upon joining the soccer body in September. His visit came a month after FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s president, Gianni Infantino, met with President Trump at the White House.'
b'Such trips were considered perilous four years ago. Blatter and his former No. 2, J\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xb4me Valcke, who faces a separate corruption investigation in Switzerland, skipped the Women\xe2\x80\x99s World Cup when it was held in Canada in the summer of 2015, only weeks after the first raids in Switzerland. Other officials also have stayed safely out of reach.'
b'FIFA has not confirmed whether any council members will skip next week\xe2\x80\x99s meeting, though at least one may not travel, according to a person familiar with the council member\xe2\x80\x99s thinking.'
b'Coming to Miami also renews focus on Concacaf, the regional confederation that governs soccer in North and Central America and Caribbean. Based in the city, Concacaf is one of soccer\xe2\x80\x99s six regional governing bodies, but it perhaps felt the most damage from the scandal: three of its former presidents were charged by United States authorities, and an internal probe later found multiple examples of rogue behavior, including self-dealing, indiscriminate use of private jets and even the recruitment of a private detective to snoop on individuals, including the former U.S. Soccer president Sunil Gulati, who still sits on the FIFA Council.'
b'Concacaf, which  nearly closed amid a banking crisis brought on by the Justice Department case, is largely prospering after introducing governance reforms. It has also changed headquarters, moving from a location in Miami Beach that was the target of F.B.I. raids in 2015 to a new office in the city\xe2\x80\x99s business district.'
b'Its current president, Victor Montagliani of Canada, said Concacaf had \xe2\x80\x9clong turned the page\xe2\x80\x9d on its existential crisis.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHaving FIFA come to Miami for the first time since the events of 2015 marks a momentum forward for world football,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cand we are glad to play our part.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'While its worst days may have passed, global soccer continues to be dogged by sporadic episodes of unethical behavior by senior figures. A Ghanaian member of the FIFA Council, Kwesi Nyantakyi, received a lifetime ban last year after being caught on camera accepting thousands of dollars in cash from an undercover reporter. And last week, another council member, Lee Harmon of the Cook Islands, received a three-month ban for the illegal resale of tickets to last year\xe2\x80\x99s World Cup in Russia.'
b'To Miguel Maduro, a former governance head at FIFA, the continuing problems are both structural and cultural, part of a system that he said was still being run as a \xe2\x80\x9cpolitical cartel.\xe2\x80\x9d Infantino, for example, will stand unopposed for re-election later this year in an election that will mirror the one for the presidency of European soccer in February. In that race, the incumbent, Aleksander Ceferin, was re-elected by acclamation.'
b'Perhaps the biggest sign of FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s difficulties in changing the culture is its inability to wean the council members who will be in Miami off the kind of lifestyle even they have acknowledged to be excessive. At previous meetings, for example, members have described being met on the airport tarmac and whisked to luxury hotels without having to go through the usual arrival protocol. Even after FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s reforms, they receive annual salaries of $250,000, plus an additional per diem, to attend as few as three meetings a year.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s one of the reasons you maintain the cartel,\xe2\x80\x9d Maduro said. \xe2\x80\x9cYou have to satisfy the people that keep you in power.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Rebecca R. Ruiz contributed reporting.'

b'On Soccer'
b'By Rory Smith'
b'DORTMUND, Germany \xe2\x80\x94 At first glance, it is easy to pinpoint the start of the Bundesliga\xe2\x80\x99s love affair with young English players. The opening scene of a story that has swept a host of England\xe2\x80\x99s brightest prospects out of the Premier League\xe2\x80\x99s overstuffed academies and into top-flight German soccer is set at a specific time \xe2\x80\x94 the first few days of October 2016 \xe2\x80\x94 and in a specific place: Pula, Croatia.'
b'That week, England\xe2\x80\x99s under-17 team took part in the Croatian Cup, a youth invitational that also featured teams from Germany, Greece and the host nation. England won it, and in some style, rounding off the competition with an 8-1 rout of Germany.'
b'Even before that, though, the amount of talent on display had turned heads. Several scouts from Bundesliga clubs had been in attendance at Pula\xe2\x80\x99s Aldo Drosina Stadium for England\xe2\x80\x99s first game, a 5-0 win against Croatia.'
b'Though many of the English players involved would go on to win the under-17 World Cup a little more than a year later, one, in particular, stood out. A scout, present that day, remembers being taken aback by the player\xe2\x80\x99s appetite. Even with England comfortably ahead, he said, he kept running, kept trying to score goals.'
b'The scout flagged the player, Jadon Sancho, to his superiors, but to no avail. Less than a year later, Sancho was on his way to Germany, but to sign with Borussia Dortmund, another of the clubs that had watched him that day. Within a few months, he was a regular on Dortmund\xe2\x80\x99s first team, a senior England international and one of the most coveted players in Europe.'
b'He was also a trendsetter. After Sancho, a flood of young British players have landed in the Bundesliga: Arsenal\xe2\x80\x99s Emile Smith Rowe \xe2\x80\x94 another veteran of that Croatian trip \xe2\x80\x94 and Reiss Nelson, on loan at RB Leipzig and TSG Hoffenheim; representatives at Augsburg and Borussia M\xc3\xb6nchengladbach and Schalke.'
b'In January, Bayern Munich was so determined to sign Chelsea\xe2\x80\x99s Callum Hudson-Odoi \xe2\x80\x94 another who featured in Croatia \xe2\x80\x94 that it offered 40 million euros (about $45 million) for a teenager who had made only a handful of senior appearances. Sancho\xe2\x80\x99s effect, the legacy of that day in Pula, has been powerful.'
b'It is a compelling story, but not necessarily an accurate one. Sancho has been presented as the trigger for German clubs\xe2\x80\x99 fascination with young English talent, but, in reality, he was the end result: a consequence, rather than a cause, of a trend that dates way beyond 2016, one that explains why, exactly, all of those Bundesliga scouts were watching that under-17 game in Pula.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAbout 10 years ago, we decided that young players had to be our focus as a club,\xe2\x80\x9d said Max Eberl, M\xc3\xb6nchengladbach\xe2\x80\x99s sporting director. \xe2\x80\x9cWe had no financial potential to do anything else. We had to create money and value a different way.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That meant keeping tabs on the best young talent not just in Germany, but across Europe. M\xc3\xb6nchengladbach\xe2\x80\x99s scouts started watching national youth teams, a shortcut to establishing which players were regarded as the best in their homelands, and a chance to compare them directly with the talent on the rise in Germany.'
b'The initial emphasis, Eberl explained, was on France, Belgium and Holland \xe2\x80\x94 traditionally fertile breeding grounds \xe2\x80\x94 as well as markets like Denmark, where his club had strong links. England \xe2\x80\x9cwas not a market we had focused on,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, but it did not take long to realize that there were a \xe2\x80\x9clot of top players\xe2\x80\x9d in England\xe2\x80\x99s age-group teams.'
b'Eberl dispatched scouts not to watch the Premier League, but to games between clubs\xe2\x80\x99 under-18 and under-23 teams. \xe2\x80\x9cAt the time, English clubs bought players but did not care about their academies,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe players they were developing \xe2\x80\x94 30 or 40 guys, really good, really well prepared \xe2\x80\x94 had no chance.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Around the same time, Dortmund came to the same realization. \xe2\x80\x9cFive or 10 years ago, we had the feeling that the education and development of youth players in England is quite good,\xe2\x80\x9d Michael Zorc, the club\xe2\x80\x99s technical director, said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe teams don\xe2\x80\x99t only spend money on transfers and salaries, but on infrastructure. When you see these academies, you cannot compare the standard with Germany. It is much, much higher.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Most important, these state-of-the-art facilities were churning out players with the skill sets Bundesliga clubs needed. \xe2\x80\x9cEngland had so many creative players,\xe2\x80\x9d Nils Schmadtke, formerly the head scout at Cologne, said. \xe2\x80\x9cKids like Sancho: good at penetrating the sidelines, not afraid in one against ones, good technique, fast.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Just as significant as discovering this steady supply of talent in England, though, was the increasing demand in Germany.'
b'Youth is the Bundesliga\xe2\x80\x99s calling card. Germany\xe2\x80\x99s top division prides itself on its clubs\xe2\x80\x99 willingness to give players an opportunity \xe2\x80\x94 a report compiled in February found that it is the youngest of Europe\xe2\x80\x99s major leagues \xe2\x80\x94 regardless of age or experience. It sees and sells itself, according to one recent mailing, as a \xe2\x80\x9ctalent factory.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Increasingly, though, there are concerns that less and less of that talent is emerging locally, at a time when German soccer \xe2\x80\x94 both at the international level and within the Bundesliga \xe2\x80\x94 is in need of renewal.'
b'The generation that won the 2014 World Cup failed miserably in Russia last summer, a disappointment compounded by relegation from its group in the inaugural Nations League last year. Joachim L\xc3\xb6w, the national team coach, has vowed to transform the side, informing several stalwarts \xe2\x80\x94 Mats Hummels, Thomas M\xc3\xbcller and J\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xb4me Boateng \xe2\x80\x94 that they will no longer be considered for selection.'
b'For the first time in more than a decade, the Bundesliga will not be represented in the Champions League quarterfinals. Bayern Munich is already planning for a substantial overhaul of its squad at the end of the season.'
b'It is telling that Hudson-Odoi, a young English winger, is at the forefront of its thinking: Zorc admitted last month that at the under-17 and under-19 levels, England had \xe2\x80\x9covertaken\xe2\x80\x9d Germany. Schmadtke said that he believed the \xe2\x80\x9cindividual skills\xe2\x80\x9d he saw from young English players \xe2\x80\x94 as well as on scouting trips to France \xe2\x80\x94 stood out because they are now so rare in his homeland. For Bayern, as for the national team, the pipeline of German talent has dried up.'
b'Eberl, for one, believes that Germany has \xe2\x80\x9cmade mistakes\xe2\x80\x9d in developing its young players. Clubs, he said, have fallen into the trap of trying to produce winning youth teams, rather than concentrating on individuals. Schmadtke feels German teenagers suffer because they are exposed too quickly to senior soccer, playing for so-called B teams in regional leagues, rather than in youth-specific competitions, as they do in England.'
b'Both are confident that it is a hiatus, rather than a full stop. \xe2\x80\x9cWe will have players in the future, but it will take time,\xe2\x80\x9d Eberl said. In the meantime, German clubs will continue to flock to England, hoping to find yet more players to follow the path Sancho has plotted. It is a result not of a love affair, but of the simple economics of supply and demand.'

b'By Rory Smith'
b'LIVERPOOL, England \xe2\x80\x94 Friday morning, and Goodison Park is quiet. There are no fans milling around the streets outside, spilling out of the Winslow pub, eagerly rushing to their seats. There is no noise, no color, no riot of blue and white. There are only a handful of cars in the parking lot. It is spitting with rain.'
b'A stadium is a home, but that is, in truth, only an occasional role. These are places that blossom only every other weekend, as Goodison will on Sunday when Liverpool arrives for the latest Merseyside Derby. For much of the rest of the time, though, a stadium is dormant, quiet: an empty, expectant shell.'
b'The day-to-day life of a club \xe2\x80\x94 the parts of it that are dedicated to the business of soccer, and the parts of it dedicated to the soccer business \xe2\x80\x94 happens elsewhere. For Everton, the former is at Finch Farm, its training facility on the eastern fringes of Liverpool. The latter is in the Liver Buildings, on the city\xe2\x80\x99s sparkling waterfront, where Everton relocated its offices last year, a new home for all those departments whose job it is to sell shirts and tickets and sponsorship deals. To most fans, a club is a team, hopefully to win games. To all owners, a club is a business, hopefully to make money.'
b'A club is more than that, though; there is another side, one which does its work not on the field at Goodison Park or in the suite of offices in the city, but in the tight warren of terraced streets that surround the stadium, in schools across Liverpool, in some of the most underprivileged parts of Merseyside.'
b'Across the street from Goodison Park, a group of children are playing on the Cruyff Court \xe2\x80\x94 a small, artificial soccer field surrounded by a metal cage, built in conjunction with the Johan Cruyff Foundation \xe2\x80\x94 behind Everton\xe2\x80\x99s community hub. Inside, teenagers mill and mingle with teachers and coaches in Everton polo shirts.'
b'Around the corner, in what was once a run-down working men\xe2\x80\x99s club, a few dozen retirees are spending the morning cycling through their memories \xe2\x80\x94 of Everton, of the city \xe2\x80\x94 over tea and cake. Pat van den Hauwe, a tough-tackling defender who played for the team in the 1980s, is helping serve the coffee.'
b'On Goodison Road, the club has bought three houses and converted them into drop-in centers, safe spaces for anyone who feels they need a place to go. Their doors are always open. There is always someone to talk to. There is always food in the fridge.'
b'All clubs run outreach programs, of course, and employ staff members to work in the communities they call home. But few, if any, can match Everton\xe2\x80\x99s for size and scope. The buildings that house Everton in the Community cost more than $10 million to develop; the program\xe2\x80\x99s annual budget is around $4 million. It has 125 staff members and 145 volunteers. It works in more than 200 locations: schools, youth clubs, community centers.'
b'There is barely a part of life in Liverpool \xe2\x80\x94 and particularly in the L4 postal code that is home to both Goodison Park and Anfield, Liverpool\xe2\x80\x99s stadium, and among the most deprived areas in Britain \xe2\x80\x94 that the club does not touch.'
b'It oversees more than 40 social programs, focused on issues as diffuse as mental health and serious organized crime; it reaches more than 20,000 people a year. Last year, Everton won a grant of 700,000 pounds, or about $925,000, to lead a government scheme on Merseyside to tackle gang culture. It has a presence in 150 schools. In September 2015, it became the first club to launch its own school.'
b'Everton has, for more than a decade, styled itself as Liverpool\xe2\x80\x99s People\xe2\x80\x99s Club, a term popularized by David Moyes, its former manager, to distinguish it from its near neighbor. Banners bearing the phrase flutter from Goodison Park; scarves embossed with the slogan can be bought from stands around the stadium on match day.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cOur fans hold us up against that image,\xe2\x80\x9d Everton\xe2\x80\x99s chief executive, Denise Barrett-Baxendale, said. \xe2\x80\x9cThey expect us to live up to it. It is not a corporate social responsibility program. It is long-term, strategic work. It is a huge component of what Everton is.\xe2\x80\x9d So substantial, in fact, that before she was promoted to running Everton last year, Barrett-Baxendale ran not the commercial section of the club, or its merchandising arm, but its community department.'
b'It is not just the scale of Everton\xe2\x80\x99s work that marks it as different, though; it is the scope of it, too. Everton goes into areas other clubs \xe2\x80\x94 and other charities, even \xe2\x80\x94 might find \xe2\x80\x9cintimidating,\xe2\x80\x9d as Barrett-Baxendale put it. Sue Gregory, Everton in the Community\xe2\x80\x99s director of youth engagement, recalls representatives of other teams marveling at the fact that Everton \xe2\x80\x94 in theory, just a soccer club \xe2\x80\x94 was prepared to work with convicted criminals, drug dealers, members of gangs. \xe2\x80\x9cYou could see it as the club risking its brand,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'Barrett-Baxendale does not. \xe2\x80\x9cWe work on these issues because these issues exist on the streets of Merseyside,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. It is a view supported throughout the club. At the start of the season, Everton\xe2\x80\x99s players signed a pledge that they would do their part to help with community work. A copy of it hangs on a wall in the Community\xe2\x80\x99s hub. There have been times that players have had to be reminded to leave after sessions there: Tom Davies, the midfielder, once insisted he was happy to stay for as long as possible at one session because he was busy \xe2\x80\x9ccoloring in unicorns.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Gregory, her staff and her volunteers know how much all of that matters. They hear all of the stories: the teenagers forced to work selling drugs for gangs to settle their parents\xe2\x80\x99 debts, or chased through the streets for punishment beatings; the boys sent hundreds of miles from home as part of the \xe2\x80\x9ccounty lines\xe2\x80\x9d phenomenon, in which city gangs seek to control the drug market in smaller towns; the children who stock up on food at the sessions because there is not enough to eat at home.'
b'Everton does not have a choice, in other words, but to confront those problems. Shying away from them would make all the work it does nothing but tokenism. \xe2\x80\x9cThis is our community,\xe2\x80\x9d Gregory said, adding: \xe2\x80\x9cThese are the issues our community faces. There is a culture of \xe2\x80\x98let\xe2\x80\x99s try.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Wherever it can, it makes the most of the power of its crest: The white-on-blue depiction of Prince Rupert\xe2\x80\x99s Tower, instantly recognizable, is part of the city\xe2\x80\x99s civic scenery. It transcends tribal loyalty \xe2\x80\x94 many Liverpool fans are part of the Everton programs \xe2\x80\x94 and represents, instead, permanence.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cPeople trust the badge,\xe2\x80\x9d said Richard Kenyon, Everton in the Community\xe2\x80\x99s chief executive. \xe2\x80\x9cThey respond to it in a really powerful way. They\xe2\x80\x99re drawn to it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Those who would normally eschew authority figures, those who would not respond to local government or a school principal, respond to that crest. Everton, they know, is not going anywhere.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe are a consistent presence,\xe2\x80\x9d Gregory said. \xe2\x80\x9cKids might have a really good connection with a teacher in one year, but then they move on, and the kids lose that. We are always there, so that bond is not lost.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'This, more than the team or the business, is what a club is, what a club can do. Not far from Goodison Park is one of Everton in the Community\xe2\x80\x99s smallest projects: a little corner of scrap land that has been converted into an herb garden. The plot is little more than a postage stamp. When Everton started it, encouraging children from these streets to tend to it, some worried that it would be ruined, vandalized, maybe even in its first few days. That was months ago. It is still pristine.'

b'By Ken Belson'
b'ATLANTA \xe2\x80\x94 Most teams that win championships enjoy a honeymoon. There are parades and victory laps and time to prepare for a title defense.'
b'Not so with Atlanta United, which won its first M.L.S. Cup on Dec. 8 and, because of Major League Soccer roster rules, had to spend the next day releasing some of the players who led it to the title. In fact, from almost the moment the final whistle blew in Atlanta United\xe2\x80\x99s 2-0 victory over the Portland Timbers, the club president, Darren Eales, has had to grapple with a host of changes, including finding a new coach, selling one of his team\xe2\x80\x99s best players and juggling the remaking of a star-studded roster.'
b'At times, the off-season has seemed comically short. Atlanta United reconvened as a team and opened its preseason training camp in mid-January, then flew to California before the Super Bowl to prepare for a preseason friendly against Club Tijuana. Last week, Atlanta United lost to Costa Rica\xe2\x80\x99s Herediano, 3-1, in the first stage of the Concacaf Champions League (the teams meet again in Atlanta on Thursday night), and on Sunday it opens its M.L.S. season against D.C. United in Washington.'
b'All of this meant Eales had to get his off-season work done quickly, and he has not wasted any time. On Jan. 14, Atlanta United introduced Frank de Boer, the former manager of Ajax, Inter Milan and Crystal Palace, as the replacement for Atlanta\xe2\x80\x99s former coach, Tata Martino, who took over Mexico\xe2\x80\x99s national team. Then Eales signed Josef Mart\xc3\xadnez, the league\xe2\x80\x99s most valuable player last season, to a five-year contract extension. Soon after, Pity Mart\xc3\xadnez, a 25-year-old Argentine midfielder, was signed; that move allowed Eales to sell Atlanta\xe2\x80\x99s playmaker, Miguel Almir\xc3\xb3n, to England\xe2\x80\x99s Newcastle United for a reported $23 million, smashing the M.L.S. transfer record.'
b'Two days before the Super Bowl, the hyperkinetic Eales sat down at his favorite Atlanta coffee shop \xe2\x80\x94 appropriately named Octane \xe2\x80\x94 to discuss the team\xe2\x80\x99s dizzying off-season, its sale of Almir\xc3\xb3n and whether, in fact, other teams in M.L.S. can copy the Atlanta model.'
b'You knew you were going to have a lot of holes to fill in the off-season. What was the process?'
b'When we went out and built the club, our intention was to be clear with the fans from the very start. We were going to attract players who were young, or going toward the prime of their career, rather than a last contract or a last hurrah for a player from Europe. The idea here is, we\xe2\x80\x99re part of this global network of soccer clubs. Miggy came to us, he had two fantastic years, won the M.L.S. Cup in the second season, had tremendous success on the pitch, and then he got a chance to fulfill his dream to go to the Premier League and play for a club there. So obviously, it was good for him, good for the league, because now the league can say, \xe2\x80\x98We have a mechanism for you to showcase yourself, so come to M.L.S., play in a short window, and when the right moment comes, you can move to a top league in Europe.\xe2\x80\x99 That was the dream we sold, and we had to at least prove the concept because otherwise it was going to be difficult for us to recruit other players if we didn\xe2\x80\x99t do that.'
b'This business model is routine elsewhere, but it\xe2\x80\x99s still new to M.L.S. Wasn\xe2\x80\x99t it hard to see Almir\xc3\xb3n go?'
b'Miggy delivered everything we could have expected, and we won an M.L.S. Cup. On top of that, we didn\xe2\x80\x99t spend dead money on a player at the end of his contract and get nothing in return. We actually got well in excess of what we had spent on the player in the first place. So it makes good business sense, good sporting sense, and that was always the vision.'
b'You signed Josef Mart\xc3\xadnez to a contract extension, then acquired Pity Mart\xc3\xadnez, before you sold Almir\xc3\xb3n. Was that sequencing deliberate?'
b'We\xe2\x80\x99re really pleased that we did the whole succession plan in reverse. We got our player in [Mart\xc3\xadnez] before we moved the player on to Europe [Almir\xc3\xb3n]. Hypothetically, if we first sold a player for $30 million and went out to buy a player, everyone\xe2\x80\x99s going to quote us $30 million. It\xe2\x80\x99s the nature of the beast. So to secure our replacement in advance with a number we were comfortable with, it gave us a little more carte blanche.'
b'You also had to replace Tata Martino, whose reputation was instrumental in attracting young players to Atlanta for the first year.'
b'When we sat there after winning the Cup, we knew the coach was going. The reality is, it\xe2\x80\x99s no different than Nick Saban, who has said how he loses his coordinators every year but he doesn\xe2\x80\x99t mind because he knows the replacements come in and work hard because they have a chance to move on. We can embrace that as a club. When coaches want to come to Atlanta, they can see that as well. Frank de Boer coached at Ajax, at Inter and Crystal Palace. For me, I\xe2\x80\x99m really excited because certain coaches fit players. With Ajax, he had great success. He went into situations [at Inter and Crystal Palace] that weren\xe2\x80\x99t good fits. But he was the right fit for us.'
b'A lot has had to go right: Not just the success on the field, but an owner with deep pockets, a new stadium, enthusiastic fans. You have all of that.'
b'Everyone\xe2\x80\x99s been asking when soccer is going to succeed in America, but if you watched the Cup final, with 73,000 passionate fans who were tailgating all afternoon, with an exciting style of play, it really has happened in America already. It\xe2\x80\x99s great for me because yes, I wanted to make Atlanta United a real success story. But we\xe2\x80\x99re also part of the bigger story, which is growing the game of soccer in America, being the pioneers to hopefully one day make it one of the top leagues in the world.'
b'Can other M.L.S. teams replicate what you\xe2\x80\x99ve done?'
b'I\xe2\x80\x99m not sure about replicating, but like every other business, you look at what other businesses are doing successfully and try to take those things that might work. I\xe2\x80\x99m a fan of how L.A.F.C. came into the league. You saw the way they filled out their roster; there were similarities. I wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t say they were copying us, but there were similarities. That\xe2\x80\x99s a good thing. We were in a strange situation as pioneers trying to grow the league. There will be more teams looking, when they think of their out-of-pocket expenditures, money above the cap, not just the salaries \xe2\x80\x94 there\xe2\x80\x99s much more awareness around investing more than we would have in a transfer fee for a younger player because we might have a chance to make a profit, or make our investment back. That\xe2\x80\x99s going to open up an avenue for a few more clubs.'
b'With all this activity, did you get a chance to take any time off this winter?'
b'My aim is to get to March, the international break. I promised the wife and family I\xe2\x80\x99ll take a week off, and football won\xe2\x80\x99t be mentioned. I\xe2\x80\x99m hoping to get to the end of March and then I\xe2\x80\x99ll crash.'

b'MIAMI \xe2\x80\x94 Against the wishes of European soccer leaders, FIFA pushed through plans for a revamped World Cup of clubs featuring 24 teams at a meeting of its governing council on Friday. The decision ended a debate that had lasted a year, while at the same time raised doubts about the caliber of participants in a major new competition championed by FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s president, Gianni Infantino.'
b'The remaking of the competition from winter afterthought to potential summer moneymaker \xe2\x80\x94 a replacement for the Confederations Cup, an unpopular national-team competition usually held a year before the World Cup \xe2\x80\x94 has led to a major breakdown in relations between FIFA and European soccer\xe2\x80\x99s governing body, UEFA. All the European members at the FIFA meeting voted against the plan for the new tournament on Friday.'
b'European club teams, whose participation will be critical to the success of the reimagined Club World Cup, reiterated their opposition to the event only minutes after FIFA made its announcement that it had been approved. The European Club Association, an umbrella body for the continent\xe2\x80\x99s top teams, said its members would not participate in the event, even though FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s plan includes slots for eight European teams.'
b'Infantino, though, described himself as \xe2\x80\x9ca happy president,\xe2\x80\x9d saying he was confident that after further talks, opposition to the event would subside and the world\xe2\x80\x99s top teams would take part. He pointed out that the event \xe2\x80\x94 held every four years \xe2\x80\x94 could bring in billions of extra dollars to FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s coffers, which currently benefit from more than $6 billion from each World Cup.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe hope all the greatest teams will participate,\xe2\x80\x9d Infantino said at a news conference. \xe2\x80\x9cThe best teams should have this world platform.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The main opposition to the plans largely relates to adding more events to soccer\xe2\x80\x99s already busy global calendar, with fears that even more games could burn out top players, or leave them susceptible to injuries. b'The Club World Cup plan had led to an almost complete breakdown in the relationship between Infantino and Aleksander Ceferin, the UEFA president. The men had not held talks for a year since a meeting last year in Colombia during which Infantino first unveiled the proposal. They did, however, meet for an hour on Thursday morning, where Ceferin outlined UEFA\xe2\x80\x99s continued opposition.'
b'In other news Friday, the FIFA Council agreed to push ahead with plans to expand the World Cup in Qatar to 48 teams, an undertaking fraught with complexity amid an ongoing diplomatic and economic standoff between Qatar and a group of its Gulf neighbors.'
b'A study conducted by FIFA recently found Qatar, a desert state smaller than Connecticut, could not host an event with 16 more teams on its own. Unless the blockade \xe2\x80\x94 led by Saudi Arabia and the United Arab Emirates \xe2\x80\x94 is lifted, only Oman and Kuwait could be considered viable partners in the region. But both countries would be required to spend significant amounts on the infrastructure required to meet FIFA standards.'
b'Greg Clarke, a FIFA vice president from England, told the meeting that FIFA must consider the human rights records of any additional host country, according to people present at the meeting. That scrutiny would likely shift to its neighbors, Clarke told the council members.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHow can you not think of human rights wherever you go? It must be an issue,\xe2\x80\x9d said Evelina Christillin, a FIFA Council member from Italy.'
b'A delegation from Qatar, which was awarded the World Cup almost a decade ago, was also present in Miami. Hassan al-Thawadi, the executive responsible for 2022 World Cup preparations, said Qatar remained open-minded about expansion, provided it benefited Qatar as much as it did FIFA. He failed to answer when asked to provide one example of a benefit that his country could derive from an expanded tournament.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe are open to exploring the options,\xe2\x80\x9d al-Thawadi said, adding it would be a \xe2\x80\x9cbig, big challenge\xe2\x80\x9d to host a 48-team event if the blockade, now in its second year, continued. FIFA must make a final decision at a meeting of its 211 members in Paris in June; qualifying for the tournament begins that month, and teams and federations would need to know how many places are available.'
b'Should the World Cup be enlarged, FIFA would need to play six matches per day to ensure the tournament can be completed within 28 days, a stipulation it agreed with European clubs after moving the tournament to November to avoid the searing Gulf summer. b'By Tariq Panja'
b'FIFA President Gianni Infantino\xe2\x80\x99s plans to reorder world soccer are being stymied by a familiar foe: Europe.'
b'Since proposing several major changes to the sport\xe2\x80\x99s calendar last spring, Infantino has spent months traveling the world hosting minisummits with the leaders of FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s 211 member federations. His goal is to win support for a proposal to introduce two new tournaments \xe2\x80\x94 an expanded World Cup for clubs and a new league for national teams \xe2\x80\x94 that would be underwritten by a $25 billion offer from a group led by the Japanese conglomerate SoftBank.'
b'The listening exercise follows repeated failures by Infantino to force the proposals through FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s governing council, but if they are approved they would represent the biggest changes to soccer in a generation, and their adoption \xe2\x80\x94 and the multibillion-dollar cash infusion to FIFA \xe2\x80\x94 would provide Infantino with a signature success ahead of his bid to secure a second term as FIFA president later this year.'
b'Each of the meetings on Infantino\xe2\x80\x99s tour, including the most recent one held in Marrakesh, Morocco, has included about 50 federation leaders from across soccer\xe2\x80\x99s six regional confederations. At the end of each session, the federation representatives are handed electronic tablets and asked to select their preferred options for the new tournaments.'
b'Infantino\xe2\x80\x99s problem is that European officials attending the meetings have stubbornly refused to offer any opinions. Instead, they have told Infantino and his team that the feelings of Aleksander Ceferin, the president of the European governing body, UEFA, and his governing council represent their views.'
b'Some of the Europeans balked because the list of options for the Club World Cup did not include the option of not holding the tournament, which is often an annoyance for the European champion who attends, at all. On FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s tablets, voters are asked to pick from only three choices: a tournament with 16, 24 or 32 teams.'
b'Ceferin, under pressure from clubs and federations in Europe, has clashed repeatedly with Infantino over the proposed changes both to the Club World Cup and to the broader global soccer calendar, with Ceferin most frustrated by new initiatives that could challenge the hegemony of existing club tournaments like UEFA\xe2\x80\x99s Champions League and add to the workload of players.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI cannot accept that some people who are blinded by the pursuit of profit are considering to sell the soul of football tournaments to nebulous private funds,\xe2\x80\x9d Ceferin said in a speech last May. \xe2\x80\x9cMoney does not rule \xe2\x80\x94 and the European sports model must be respected. Football is not for sale. I will not let anyone sacrifice its structures on the altar of a highly cynical and ruthless mercantilism.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Infantino first presented details of a plan for an expanded Club World Cup at a FIFA Council meeting in Bogot\xc3\xa1, Colombia, last March. Citing a nondisclosure agreement, he refused to identify the financial backers of the proposal, which are believed to include not only SoftBank but also financing from the Middle East, which Infantino eventually denied were directly linked to sovereign wealth funds. (Saudi Arabia remains the biggest individual backer over Softbank\xe2\x80\x99s Vision Fund, the biggest private-equity fund ever raised.) Instead, Infantino pressed the council to let him close the deal on his own.'
b'European leaders at the meeting balked, and Ceferin and Infantino have not held a meeting since the Colombia summit. In October, European officials threatened to walk out of the last meeting when Infantino suggested he planned to call another vote.'
b'The vote did not take place; instead, FIFA set up a task force involving representatives from the six confederations and asked it to produce an acceptable plan before a scheduled FIFA Council meeting in March in Miami.'
b'At the last summit, in Morocco, Infantino expressed frustration to the officials who declined to take part in the vote for his plans, according to multiple people present at the meeting.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAs part of this discussion, people are asked to give their feedback on a series of proposals and, as in any democratic consultation process, every member can express its opinion freely,\xe2\x80\x9d FIFA said in a statement. \xe2\x80\x9cThe feedback received will be fed back to the Council together with the results of the other consultation platforms.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'FIFA\xe2\x80\x99s task force for the two tournaments will hold its next meeting on Feb. 21 in Rio de Janeiro. As tensions grow, however, there is a chance that European executives will not attend, according to a person familiar with the continental leaders\xe2\x80\x99 plans.'
b'UEFA declined to comment. The organization has been seeking the support of European clubs and leagues to oppose Infantino\xe2\x80\x99s proposals. At the last two meetings, Ceferin has arrived armed with signed letters of opposition from The European Club Association, a union of the continent\xe2\x80\x99s top clubs, and a separate group representing the continent\xe2\x80\x99s domestic leagues.'
b'The proposals to expand the Club World Cup and to create a new global Nations League similar to the recently created UEFA version largely have the backing of officials from South America, Africa and Asia \xe2\x80\x94 likely enough to win a vote should Infantino choose to take one at the Miami meeting. Any such move would exacerbate the growing rift with Europe, however, and potentially lead to a larger crisis if top clubs and leading nations from UEFA refuse to participate in the new FIFA-controlled tournaments.'

b'Supported by'
b'By Andrew Keh'
b'LEIPZIG, Germany \xe2\x80\x94 Upon moving to Germany from the United States last summer, Jesse Marsch, his wife, Kim, and their three children made a pact of sorts regarding their new life abroad: When a situation that felt foreign made them want to turn inward, they would challenge themselves to do the opposite, to turn outward and embrace it, to accept and understand it.'
b'Such discomfort has been precisely the point for Marsch, the very reason he diverged from an ascendant coaching path in the United States last summer and sought out the unknown across the Atlantic Ocean.'
b'In July, Marsch left his job as coach of the New York Red Bulls in Major League Soccer to accept a post as an assistant coach for RB Leipzig in the Bundesliga. While unquestionably a step up in competition, it was, in some respects, still an unconventional move, and Marsch said even some of his friends in soccer asked him if taking a job as an assistant might be a step backward.'
b'But what represents a step backward, and what is the convention, when you are navigating a mostly uncharted path? Because while opportunities for American players in Europe continue to expand, there is not yet much of a road map for what Marsch wants to be: an American coach who builds a long, successful career in one of the continent\xe2\x80\x99s top leagues.'
b'And so he has chosen to seek out that challenge, to take chances and to face the unknown and the unfamiliar head on.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve gotten more comfortable,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cwith being uncomfortable.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After decades of battling stereotypes and preconceived ideas about their abilities, American players have, slowly, found a level of acceptance in European soccer. One of the players Marsch brought into the Red Bulls\xe2\x80\x99 first team, for example, was viewed even here as a solid addition when he joined RB Leipzig this month. That player, the 19-year-old Tyler Adams, and other American prospects now head to the continent in waves, and in general the professional pathways there have become well worn and widely available.'
b'A similar process has yet to unfold for American coaches, however. There are no set pathways, and there are few pioneers.'
b'Marsch regards one of them, Bob Bradley, as the \xe2\x80\x9cbiggest mentor\xe2\x80\x9d in his career, and he has found Bradley\xe2\x80\x99s experiences instructive. From 2014 to 2016, Bradley held head coaching jobs for clubs in Norway, France and England. Looking back, his stint abroad was as notable for the milestones he set for American coaches \xe2\x80\x94 he was the first American to coach a team in England\xe2\x80\x99s Premier League \xe2\x80\x94 as it was for the relentless stream of misgivings from fans and pundits in whatever new locale he landed. (Bradley\xe2\x80\x99s Premier League tenure lasted all of 11 games.)'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe perception of Bob, I think, when he was here is that he probably wasn\xe2\x80\x99t as knowledgeable because he\xe2\x80\x99s from America, that his accent and the way he talked about football may have brought questions up within fan bases about how do Americans think about football, how do they talk about football, even use the word football,\xe2\x80\x9d Marsch said. \xe2\x80\x9cAll those things are unfair, but they\xe2\x80\x99re realities we have to deal with.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That is what Marsch knows he is up against now, and it is the reason he says he has tried to take a holistic approach to this new chapter of his life.'
b'Under RB Leipzig\xe2\x80\x99s manager, Ralf Rangnick, Marsch has assumed what he described as a fluid, all-encompassing role. At the same time, he is responsible for a weekly set of tasks \xe2\x80\x94 running different elements of training, game analysis and opponent preparation \xe2\x80\x94 whose strict implementation he has found exhilarating in a way only a knowledge-hungry coach can.'
b'While RB Leipzig and New York\xe2\x80\x99s Red Bulls are both technically part of the same corporate sports empire, his first months experiencing the nuances of German soccer culture \xe2\x80\x94 the structure, the specificity, the attention to detail \xe2\x80\x94 reiterated for him how much he still can learn.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt would have been easy for me to stay in New York,\xe2\x80\x9d Marsch said about his last job in Major League Soccer, where he spent three and a half seasons and compiled the most wins in franchise history. \xe2\x80\x9cBut in the end, that wasn\xe2\x80\x99t really what I was interested in.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Instead, Marsch, who had begun the process of obtaining his UEFA pro coaching license in 2017, accepted an offer to join the Leipzig coaching staff and left the Red Bulls in midseason. Rangnick, an experienced coach and former Red Bull sporting director, is in his second stint leading Leipzig but plans to coach only for this season. The club has previously announced that Hoffenheim\xe2\x80\x99s Julian Nagelsmann, a rising star in German coaching, will take over this summer.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI know the league, the team and I speak the language,\xe2\x80\x9d Rangnick said when he returned to the bench. \xe2\x80\x9cThat isn\xe2\x80\x99t the case yet for Jesse Marsch, so that\xe2\x80\x99s why he will be working as an assistant coach.\xe2\x80\x9d Still, the club noted specifically when it hired Marsch that he had signed a two-year contract, with the expectation that he would continue in the role once Nagelsmann arrives.'
b'Until then, Marsch has been stockpiling professional experiences like a backpacker collecting souvenirs. That mind-set was one reason he was not interested in pursuing the United States national team coaching job, which still sat vacant when he left for Europe. Marsch wants to hold the position one day, he said, but only after he has accumulated more experience.'
b'Now, he said, it better that the American soccer ecosystem put its collective support behind the coach who was chosen, Gregg Berhalter, and move away from the negativity that seemed to infest its culture in the past year.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf I were to be critical of the sport in our country in general, I think we have failed ourselves miserably because everyone is the smartest guy in the room and everyone is the biggest critic, inside the game and out,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd that will never be successful.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Marsch also said he hoped more of his coaching peers from the United States would pursue unfamiliar pathways and leaps of faith, like the one he is taking now, so that opportunities for American coaches in the top levels of the game might one day seem as plentiful as they have become for players.'
b'Adams is one such player, and Marsch said he was eager to throw new challenges at him, too. Adams made his debut for RB Leipzig in a friendly during Germany\xe2\x80\x99s winter break, and was included in the first team for this weekend\xe2\x80\x99s game against Dortmund, though he was an unused substitute in Leipzig\xe2\x80\x99s 1-0 defeat.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen you see this kid up close every day, it\xe2\x80\x99s almost like you\xe2\x80\x99re watching a weed grow by the second,\xe2\x80\x9d Marsch said of Adams. \xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s how he is. You throw something difficult at him, and he eats it up and spits it out.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'These days, Marsch takes German language lessons three times a week and uses the language in coaches meetings and with players on the field. While he has improved, he said, the process also has made look, at times, \xe2\x80\x9clike a fool.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'But those minor indignities, he noted, could serve as positives within a team context.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think it\xe2\x80\x99s an important lesson in an leadership position to show that you\xe2\x80\x99re willing to be vulnerable, you\xe2\x80\x99re willing to make mistakes, and that\xe2\x80\x99s how I\xe2\x80\x99m going to get better,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI think that\xe2\x80\x99s the same thing we want to portray to our players: \xe2\x80\x98We all mistakes. You\xe2\x80\x99re going to make mistakes. But let\xe2\x80\x99s all learn from them. Let\xe2\x80\x99s get better together.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d'
