b'Supported by'
b'By Tariq Panja'
b'BILBAO, Spain \xe2\x80\x94 Europe\xe2\x80\x99s midseason soccer transfer window is open this month. For teams battling relegation, and potential financial ruin, it brings a last, vital chance to strengthen a leaky defense or fortify a goal-shy forward line ahead of the second half of the season.'
b'Among those teams is Athletic Bilbao, which is in 17th place in La Liga, the 20-team Spanish league, and already on its second manager this season.'
b'Financially, Athletic, a century-old power on Spain\xe2\x80\x99s northern coast, has little in common with the clubs that find themselves in a similarly grim position. The team is flush with cash, with about 200 million euros, or about $228 million, in reserves, and has access to another 90 million euros that \xe2\x80\x94 if deployed to lure talent from soccer\xe2\x80\x99s global marketplace \xe2\x80\x94 would probably go a long way toward firing it up the league standings and out of danger. But unlike almost every other team in the market, Bilbao cannot spend those millions on just anyone.'
b'Athletic is a throwback. Tradition dictates that it can only field players who were born in the Basque Country \xe2\x80\x94 territory that includes seven provinces that stretch from northern Spain into France \xe2\x80\x94 or who moved to the region in their youth and learned to play soccer here.'
b'That purity has been a point of pride for the 121-year-old club. Athletic Bilbao has long celebrated that it has never been relegated from Spain\xe2\x80\x99s top league, a feat it shares with only Barcelona and Real Madrid. But it is only one slot away from relegation position in La Liga, and its purity presents obvious difficulties when it comes to recruitment. Lately it has placed the team in a financial vise, transforming it into something of a unicorn in a sport in which nearly every other club is desperate for cash. Bilbao, with its flush coffers and narrowed options, has become soccer\xe2\x80\x99s poor little loaded club.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe don\xe2\x80\x99t really need the money,\xe2\x80\x9d Josu Urrutia, a stocky, 50-year-old former Bilbao midfielder, said in an interview last month, shortly before he ended a seven-year run as Athletic\xe2\x80\x99s president.'
b'His replacement, Aitor Elizegi, though critical of some of Urrutia\xe2\x80\x99s decisions, was quick to confirm that the team\xe2\x80\x99s commitment to Basque-only players would not be changed.'
b'Athletic can in some ways blame its recent success for its current fate. In the last eight years, the team has played six seasons in the second-tier Europa League (reaching the final once) and one in the Champions League. In 2012 and again in 2015, it reached the final of the Spanish cup.'
b'The success of those largely homegrown squads quickly drew interest from bigger clubs, in Spain and abroad, and led to tough decisions for a conveyor belt of young, talented players. When the club\xe2\x80\x99s management had any say, the answer to any inquiries to negotiate a multimillion-euro sale was a simple one: no.'
b'Athletic, at least under Urrutia, never negotiated, whatever the price. Players would leave only if their buyout clause \xe2\x80\x94 a fee that would trigger a sale \xe2\x80\x94 was met, and Athletic\xe2\x80\x99s management hoped it never would be.'
b'Urrutia, sitting in an austere drawing room full of lacquered furniture on the ground floor of a mansion built in 1900 and bestowed to the club by one of the city\xe2\x80\x99s historic trading families, described how the club lost defensive midfielder Javi Mart\xc3\xadnez to the German giant Bayern Munich a year into his presidency in 2011. This all happened after he tried to ignore Jupp Heynckes, then Bayern\xe2\x80\x99s manager, who had coached Urrutia, a tough tackling midfielder during two spells at Athletic, and Bayern\xe2\x80\x99s top two officials, Karl Heinz Rummenigge and Uli Hoeness.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cJupp says, \xe2\x80\x98We consider Javi is a player for the future, and 40 seems a lot; we are ready to pay 22 or 23,\xe2\x80\x9d Urrutia recalled. \xe2\x80\x9cWe said: Perfect. So we don\xe2\x80\x99t have to worry ourselves about it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In the end, Bayern paid the full 40 million euro buyout fee for Mart\xc3\xadnez, a sum that broke Germany\xe2\x80\x99s transfer record.'
b'Since then, the team has lost other players in a similar fashion. Ander Herrera, another defensive midfielder, joined Manchester United in 2014. Defender Aymeric Laporte became Manchester City\xe2\x80\x99s costliest acquisition when he joined for 65 million euros. Most recently, Chelsea made Kepa Arrizabalaga the most expensive goalkeeper in the world after paying his full 80 million euro release clause.'
b'All those deals, regardless of the fee, frustrated Urrutia. He wished all of Athletic\xe2\x80\x99s players shared his values. Urrutia came through the club\xe2\x80\x99s youth system and never wore another jersey in a two-decade career. The club, he said, tries to instill loyalty from the moment players enter the system.'
b'Athletic officials like to play the guilt card and remind players that the Basque-only policy was probably the reason they were able to have a professional career in the first place \xe2\x80\x94 that the club could have picked other, better athletes if it had the option of shopping on the global market.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s as though you\xe2\x80\x99ve left the family business started by your granddad,\xe2\x80\x9d Urrutia said.'
b'Urrutia and others explain that if players who came before the current ones had decided to leave, the club might have been forced to change its mission. If that had happened, Basque players might not have gotten their chance. The players should live these values, they said.'
b'Money plays a role as well. Athletic now pays some of the highest salaries in Spain, far more than teams of an equivalent standard, Urrutia said. He said the average annual salary of a first-team player was four million euros.'
b'When faced with replacing a departing player, the club always gives first preference to products formed at its Lezama academy, a world-class facility six miles outside Bilbao, the largest city in the Basque region. In each of the last five seasons, at least two academy players have graduated to the first-team roster.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe give them opportunities to play for the first team even when they\xe2\x80\x99re too young, because we need them,\xe2\x80\x9d Urrutia said.'
b'Some players, so committed to the club\xe2\x80\x99s philosophy, like midfielder Iker Muniain, 26, who has had offers to leave, have shunned the opportunity to play elsewhere. Just before Christmas, Muniain, an attacker who has been with the club for more than a decade and scored Monday, signed a new contract and asked that it have no buyout clause. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m pleased to do it,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99ve had cases in which colleagues have left and people have felt sad and touched. This is a way for me to demonstrate my loyalty to the club.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Occasionally, the team does have to turn to the transfer market. The options are limited to players born in the Basque region or those who trained here during their formative years. That allows sellers to take advantage of Athletic\xe2\x80\x99s limitations.'
b'This season, the team agreed to pay Paris St.-Germain a fee that could eventually reach 24 million euros for defender Yuri Berchiche, a defender who joined the French team from Real Sociedad for about eight million euros less just a year earlier.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey know, and they try to squeeze us because they know that there are not so many possibilities for us,\xe2\x80\x9d Urrutia said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe don\xe2\x80\x99t have so many options in the transfer market.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Athletic can afford this because only four teams last season received more money from Spanish television rights, which, for now, is determined by how often a team\xe2\x80\x99s matches are shown. But a new distribution model aimed at reducing inequalities between teams is narrowing that gap. In the past, the biggest teams could get as much as 12 times more than others. That ratio is down to about 3.5.'
b'Though the change is generally considered to be a positive one, it disproportionately affects Athletic because far smaller teams can now trawl the world for talent they could not afford before, boosting their squads, while Athletic remains committed to its local-only policy and other quirks that make it unique.'
b'Its headquarters bear little resemblance to those of most teams. No brash logos, no video screens showing loops of historic success, no shop hawking memorabilia. Like the club, it is a throwback.'
b'There are small if understated markers, like the modernist painting hanging on a wall inside a ground floor reception room. It depicts a great flood that has overwhelmed an entire city. The only visible structure is an arch resembling one from Athletic\xe2\x80\x99s former stadium that was delicately moved to its training ground. It is a symbol, club officials say, that the team\xe2\x80\x99s past will always be a part of its present and future, whether it risks relegation or fights for titles.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe know the challenge: It\xe2\x80\x99s a solitary challenge,\xe2\x80\x9d Urrutia said. \xe2\x80\x9cThis is a voyage full of difficulties. There could be a tsunami, but at the end, we really believe in the strength of our boat and want to keep going.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'Supported by'
b'On Soccer'
b'By Rory Smith'
b'MANCHESTER, England \xe2\x80\x94 At last, it seems, among all of the hundreds of millions of pounds that float around the Premier League, the penny has dropped.'
b'The January transfer window has come and gone, barely noticed. There has been no orgy of excess, no frantic scramble to spend as much money as possible, no broken transfer-spending records, no helicopter dashes, no late-night drama.'
b'For once \xe2\x80\x94 for the first time, perhaps \xe2\x80\x94 English soccer has been a model of restraint and of prudence. For once, it has looked not at price, but at worth. As one executive at a Premier League team told The Times of London, \xe2\x80\x9cPeople are asking crazy money for average players.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That, of course, should hardly have come as a shock. The clubs in the cash-soaked Premier League, with its lucrative broadcasting deals and its seemingly bottomless pit of wealth, had no sooner helped to create soccer\xe2\x80\x99s superheated transfer market than they began to suffer from it.'
b'In England, managers and technical directors and chief executives whisper darkly of an \xe2\x80\x9cEnglish tax,\xe2\x80\x9d claiming that their counterparts on Continental Europe routinely quote them higher prices than they would a team from Germany, Italy or Spain.'
b'In public, those working in sales or recruitment in Europe dismiss that allegation \xe2\x80\x94 two sporting directors told The Times in 2017 that they work \xe2\x80\x9cwith one price in mind\xe2\x80\x9d for a player, regardless of origin or destination \xe2\x80\x94 but there can be little doubt that, at the very least, many see English teams as easy marks.'
b'In part, that is to their credit. According to one executive at a Bundesliga team, selling to a Premier League club is a much more straightforward business than offloading a player to Italy or Spain: The money is invariably paid upfront, one lump sum deposited into your account upon completion of the deal, rather than an installment plan contingent on a host of clauses. It is also rather more palatable to fans: Clubs in Germany, he said, have broadly welcomed English interest in their best players simply because the alternative is seeing them move, with dread predictability, to Bayern Munich.'
b'That is not, however, the limit of its appeal. The evidence is anecdotal but nonetheless compelling: Europe\xe2\x80\x99s clubs see the Premier League as a cash cow, and its member clubs as rather deeper of pocket than they are of thought.'
b'There are, for example, executives who tell stories of hanging up the phone to a Continental team and then immediately doubling the asking price when an English club calls. There are sporting directors who recall scarcely being able to conceal their glee when a Premier League team asks to buy one of their players, or the celebrations when they complete a deal for a vastly inflated price.'
b'And there is the manager who was presented with a tall South American forward by his club\xe2\x80\x99s owner a few years ago and told that it did not matter if the deal worked out, because even if he did not score goals, \xe2\x80\x9can English team will come and buy him for more than we paid anyway.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'There will be plenty, then, who will see the drip-feed of small-beer deals and loans-with-an-option-to-buy that have populated this January transfer window and believe that it is just an exception, something cyclical, that come summer, the Premier League will be showering its largess on Europe once more.'
b'It is worth noting, though, that year-on-year spending last summer was down, too: barely noticeable in the raw figures \xe2\x80\x94 \xc2\xa31.2 billion ($1.57 billion), as opposed to \xc2\xa31.4 billion in 2017 \xe2\x80\x94 but in the context of a global market that had been distorted beyond recognition by the fee Paris St.-Germain paid for Neymar, an eye-catching drop.'
b'As unlikely as it sounds, the possibility has to be considered that the Premier League has finally managed to shake its reflex reaction to spend its way out of any problem, to break free of its shopaholism, to overcome its addiction to the short-term high of a lavish transfer.'
b'It would be reductive to attribute that to one cause; it is the result, in all likelihood, of a confluence of factors. Few in soccer, for example, believe that the uncertainty that has infected most British industries because of Brexit has had much of an effect, but it is hard to believe the weakness of the pound against the euro has not given at least some clubs pause.'
b'Then there is the assumption in the Premier League that English soccer\xe2\x80\x99s television boom might have plateaued, and that the next broadcast deal will not deliver the exponential rise in income to which the clubs have grown accustomed. That, too, may have persuaded clubs to become just a little more frugal.'
b'If certain clubs have chosen not to spend \xe2\x80\x94 Liverpool and Manchester City for fear of disrupting the delicate harmony they have established, Manchester United because a permanent manager and a technical director must be appointed first \xe2\x80\x94 others have been unable to do so.'
b'In the case of Tottenham, with a new stadium to consider, and Chelsea, subject to a FIFA investigation over rule breaches related to young players, those circumstances are bespoke; for others, the issue is much broader. The short-term cost-control measures established by the league\xe2\x80\x99s clubs effectively link increases in a team\xe2\x80\x99s wage bill to growth of its commercial revenue; that Arsenal, for example, has not increased the latter means it is not in a position to throw money at the former.'
b'None of that, though, explains why everyone has been so parsimonious, so uncharacteristically cautious. Yet the trend is widespread enough to suggest that there has been a more fundamental change, that English teams no longer suspect they are being taken for a ride, but know they are, and are determined to put a stop to it.'
b'England for many years stood as a last, defiant bulwark against the idea that recruitment should be overseen not by a club\xe2\x80\x99s manager, but by a technical \xe2\x80\x94 or sporting \xe2\x80\x94 director. Such an appointment, it was thought, would only undermine the authority of the man tasked with picking the team; in a country that sanctified the memories of Matt Busby and Alex Ferguson and Brian Clough, the manager\xe2\x80\x99s position was inviolable.'
b'That is no longer the case. Of the elite, only Manchester United does not have a technical director, and it is in the process of finding one. Away from Old Trafford, most teams have moved to bring in an individual or a team of people to sift through data, to compile scouting reports, and to assist \xe2\x80\x94 to choose a euphemism \xe2\x80\x94 the manager with recruitment. The days of a coach being allowed to bring in players on a whim are over.'
b'It is not a perfect system, but it is designed to prevent a club\xe2\x80\x99s having to resort to last-minute purchases, desperate rolls of the dice. It is structured to make clubs less wasteful, more efficient. Its corollary is that it attracts managers more accustomed to working with what they have, or what they are given, rather than demanding money be spent to solve problems that have proved beyond them.'
b'And this is its effect: a handful of unremarkable deals, players brought in to cover a particular need rather than to meet a vague desire, over the course of a month that does not warrant the comic, childlike pomp and ceremony England usually reserves for the transfer window. A dull January is not a cause for concern. It is not a sign of a lack of ambition, but the hallmark of a league that is getting that little bit smarter, that at last is thinking with its head, rather than its pocket.'

b'MANCHESTER, England \xe2\x80\x94 As he trudged, wordlessly, away from the field, away from the crowd, away from the burning humiliation, Maurizio Sarri looked like a man who knew. He is not the first in his position to have worn that look, to have made that walk, to sense that, sooner or later, Chelsea has a decision to make.'
b'In these circumstances, that ordinarily means only one thing. Historically, when Chelsea is presented with the choice of whether to fire a manager or not, it tends to act as if it has no choice at all.'
b'Roman Abramovich has fired managers early and fired them late. He has fired them after winning the Premier League title but not the Champions League; he has fired them after winning the Champions League but not the Premier League. He has fired them against the fans\xe2\x80\x99 wishes, and he has fired them to their intense relief. He has fired them for less than being beaten, 6-0, by Manchester City, as Sarri\xe2\x80\x99s Chelsea was on Sunday, and he has fired them for more.'
b'Abramovich has been through 13 permanent managers since he arrived in English soccer in 2003. By this stage of this season, Abramovich \xe2\x80\x94 or, more pertinently, those who run Chelsea at his behest \xe2\x80\x94 knows the signs. Not just the obvious ones: the back-to-back collapses away from home, first at Bournemouth and now in Manchester; the inexorable slide down the Premier League table, initially out of the title race and now, usurped by a resurgent Manchester United, out of the Champions League qualifying places.'
b'There are the subtle ones, too: Not once, but twice since the turn of the year Sarri has criticized his players publicly, questioning both their mentality and their motivation. After a 2-0 defeat to Arsenal last month, he took the unusual step of making his public comments through a translator, just in case he could not find quite the right phraseology as he laid bare his complaints about his squad.'
b'It is a risky strategy, one with the air of a final throw of the dice. It is telling, then, that there has been no visible uplift in performance since Sarri\xe2\x80\x99s public intervention; if anything, things are getting worse. Chelsea has still not scored a Premier League goal away from home in 2019; Sarri\xe2\x80\x99s team was, if anything, somewhat fortunate only to concede six on Sunday.'
b'That, too, does not bode well. When he arrived from Napoli \xe2\x80\x94 belatedly, after a long legal tussle between Chelsea and his predecessor, Antonio Conte, that is still not resolved \xe2\x80\x94 Sarri warned that his methods were sufficiently bespoke that the players might need some time to adapt to them. There would be, he admitted, teething troubles.'
b'Curiously, they were not immediate. Chelsea hit the ground running. Eden Hazard declared himself delighted to be playing \xe2\x80\x94 at last \xe2\x80\x94 for a manager who prioritized attacking soccer, who might let him have the \xe2\x80\x9cfun\xe2\x80\x9d he seeks.'
b'The problems came later, Sarri\xe2\x80\x99s prediction coming good on a satellite delay and the season slowing to a halt as winter set in. It is as if Chelsea\xe2\x80\x99s players have unlearned what Sarri taught them, as if they tried his way for a while and then decided, actually, no, this wasn\xe2\x80\x99t right for them.'
b'This is familiar ground at Chelsea: the manager and the players drifting apart, the words no longer seeming to carry weight, the instructions and ideas not quite cutting through. The same thing happened to Jos\xc3\xa9 Mourinho, in 2015, and then to Conte, last year. Everybody knows how the story ends; it is not with the players moving on.'
b'Sarri, judging by his demeanor at the final whistle Sunday, recognizes that. This is the sort of result, he will know, that brings with it immediate jeopardy, that provides compelling evidence to support his dismissal. There is, though, an equally convincing case to be made for precisely the opposite, an argument that might make Chelsea pause, even as it begins to prepare the severance check.'
b'It runs like this: Manchester City has what Chelsea has always craved \xe2\x80\x94 not just success, but sustained success, consistent success, an unwavering direction. More than that, it has a distinctive, immediately apparent style, an enviable character and identity, a devastating beauty.'
b'It is not that Chelsea has not been successful, of course: Abramovich has brought five Premier League titles to Stamford Bridge, one Champions League crown, and more F.A. Cups than anybody would want, too. Chelsea still outstrips City, the two great transformative clubs of modern English soccer, in terms of honors won.'
b'But Chelsea\xe2\x80\x99s has been a boom-and-bust kind of success, bountiful years followed invariably by fallow ones \xe2\x80\x94 one that is the result not so much of a carefully crafted plan but of the harnessing of chaos. It has long seemed fragile, somehow.'
b'City\xe2\x80\x99s is different. City has had a little chaos in its time too, of course \xe2\x80\x94 the firings of Mark Hughes and Roberto Mancini, the existence of Carlos Tevez and Mario Balotelli \xe2\x80\x94 and its prominence was hard-won, just a little slower than many might have expected given the riches injected into the club by its Emirati benefactors.'
b'But now, a little more than a decade since their arrival, the path is set. City may not win the Premier League title this year \xe2\x80\x94 this victory showed just how well Liverpool and Tottenham have done to keep pace with Pep Guardiola\xe2\x80\x99s team for this long \xe2\x80\x94 but it will at least come close. It will be the favorite to lift the trophy again next year, and the year after that. It is hard to imagine City slipping to sixth in the near future.'
b'That is a consequence of the amount of money spent on the club, but it is also testament to the way that money has been spent: building a team that is capable of playing the sort of soccer Guardiola preaches, that rival players \xe2\x80\x94 and fans \xe2\x80\x94 look on with envy, that takes the breath away.'
b'That is what Abramovich has always wanted for Chelsea. It is why he pursued Guardiola for so long, why he appointed Andr\xc3\xa9 Villas-Boas in 2011, supposedly cut from the same cloth, and why he brought in Sarri last summer.'
b'It is not just a latent aestheticism, it is also an economic argument. The sort of identity that City has brings results; not always, not every year, but over the long term. It helps lure new signings, and it pinpoints who, precisely, those players should be. It staves off the need to fire managers every year or so, to rip up the blueprint, to start again by scouring the transfer market for new players or asking old ones to learn new tricks. A defined identity staves off the turmoil of a poor run of form, of a disappointing season \xe2\x80\x94 the difference between a detour and a road to nowhere. It means there can be certainty where otherwise there may be doubt.'
b'The problem, of course, is that it takes time. Even Guardiola, as it turned out, needed a year to shape City into what he wanted it to be, and that was with a team that had been built with him in mind, long before he joined. It requires patience, and understanding. It cannot be conjured over a summer, or over a season. It does not materialize if you keep firing your manager.'
b'That, then, is the choice that Chelsea faces. Fire Sarri, and the boom-and-bust cycle will be prolonged. And perhaps that would be the right decision: Perhaps he is too inflexible to succeed in England; perhaps what he achieved at Napoli cannot be repeated; perhaps his tactics have been worked out by opponents, and he has nothing more up his sleeve.'
b'At some point, though, Chelsea will have to do the opposite. It will have to stick with someone, to accept that time is just as important as money, to go through a fallow year in the hope that bounty follows. It wants what City has. To get it, it must start to do what City does.'

b'MARBELLA, Spain \xe2\x80\x94 It was just after lunchtime on Tuesday, and Christian Pulisic was facing a rare free afternoon. There was a nap in his plans, for sure, and maybe dinner at a local restaurant afterward.'
b'Pulisic was in this southern Spanish town, bracketed by mountains and the Mediterranean Sea, for a weeklong training camp with his German club, Borussia Dortmund. The sun was shining. Waves skimmed across the beach. Any leisure time was to be cherished.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThis is always fun,\xe2\x80\x9d he said about German soccer\xe2\x80\x99s annual winter break, when most teams pack their bags and go in search of a week of warm-weather training abroad. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a week to get away, get some sun, just to change things up a little bit.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It was also, he acknowledged with a laugh, most likely the last time for a while that he would enjoy this particular type of holiday rest.'
b'Last week, Pulisic announced that he would leave Dortmund \xe2\x80\x94 the only professional club he has known \xe2\x80\x94 at the end of the season to join Chelsea of the English Premier League. They have winter breaks in Germany; in England, they do not.'
b'It is one of the countless changes, some small and many big, that the 20-year-old Pulisic will encounter in his planned move to the supercharged world of English soccer. It is a situation he says he relishes, a personal milestone in a young career already full of them.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThis was a big dream of mine,\xe2\x80\x9d Pulisic said of playing in England, \xe2\x80\x9cand I feel this was the right time to make this step.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Pulisic announced his move himself on social media with an open letter to Borussia Dortmund fans. In it, he declared, with a \xe2\x80\x9cheavy heart,\xe2\x80\x9d that he would move to London after finishing the remainder of the season in Germany. He referred to Dortmund as \xe2\x80\x9c(y)our world-famous club,\xe2\x80\x9d the parentheses at once reflecting the deep ties he formed with the team, which signed him at age 16 and is the only professional club he has known, and his looming exit.'
b'Pulisic, who was born in Hershey, Pa., said he took great care to get the wording of the letter right, working with a team staff member to make sure a German translation posted at the same time captured the message\xe2\x80\x99s nuances \xe2\x80\x94 and made clear his deep gratitude to the club and its fans.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe five years I\xe2\x80\x99ve been at Dortmund have been unbelievable, and I don\xe2\x80\x99t want them to think that I took any of that for granted,\xe2\x80\x9d Pulisic said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s not going to be easy for me to leave. I\xe2\x80\x99ll miss it here.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In the United States, where every turn in Pulisic\xe2\x80\x99s career can be viewed through the prism of what it means for the American national team, news of the transfer generated a splash befitting the country\xe2\x80\x99s best player. The fee Chelsea paid for Pulisic, 64 million euros (about $73 million), was the highest ever paid for an American player, more than tripling the previous mark.'
b'Pulisic acknowledged the enormousness of the figure, and the expectations that come with it, but he brushed aside the notion that it might burden him.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIn the soccer world, especially now with these numbers you have, who really knows who\xe2\x80\x99s worth what?\xe2\x80\x9d Pulisic said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is what it is. They wanted me obviously enough to pay that much, but I\xe2\x80\x99m just excited to go there and give my best.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'As transfers go, the deal was a congenial one. Borussia Dortmund had approached Pulisic last summer about extending his contract, which had two years remaining. But Pulisic signaled that he was hoping to move on.'
b'Michael Zorc, the team\xe2\x80\x99s technical director, was disappointed. But he also knew such a day would come: Pulisic had never been shy about his ambition to play in England.'
b'So Dortmund and Pulisic quickly set about moving forward with parallel goals: the club hoping to maximize the value of an attractive young asset still under its control, the player trying to make sure his dream move landed him in the right place.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere was a lot of trust in these talks,\xe2\x80\x9d said Zorc, who said multiple clubs expressed interest in Pulisic and that at least one other Premier League team was willing to pay Dortmund\xe2\x80\x99s final asking price.'
b'His transfer will bring an end to three remarkable years at Dortmund. As a 17-year-old, he broke into the club\xe2\x80\x99s first team and promptly became the youngest non-German to score a Bundesliga goal. But his rise slowed somewhat this season as injuries and the emergence of other young players diminished Pulisic\xe2\x80\x99s playing time. Zorc said he suspected the transfer negotiations had distracted Pulisic this season \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cmaybe his mind was not so clear\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 but hopes the resolution will have a positive effect on the field. Pulisic agrees.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI feel much, much clearer in my head now that all this is passed,\xe2\x80\x9d he said about making the deal public.'
b'Pulisic has five more months to contribute at Dortmund, which leads the Bundesliga with 42 points \xe2\x80\x94 6 ahead of Bayern Munich \xe2\x80\x94 through 17 games. After that, he will continue his development at Chelsea, a club not particularly known for nurturing young players.'
b'Still, it was not lost on Pulisic \xe2\x80\x94 or his father, Mark, who worked closely with him to evaluate his transfer destination \xe2\x80\x94 that Chelsea\xe2\x80\x99s roster situation, with several forwards potentially moving on this summer, could work in his favor.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cOf course that was part of the equation: You look at what a team is going to look like over the next few years,\xe2\x80\x9d Mark Pulisic said. \xe2\x80\x9cChelsea will be having some turnover due to the ages of players. But, at the end of the day, that doesn\xe2\x80\x99t matter. When you\xe2\x80\x99re at the highest level of your sport, there\xe2\x80\x99s going to be new competition coming in constantly.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mark Pulisic also said the recent narrative that his son\xe2\x80\x99s acquisition by Chelsea had been completed without the knowledge of the club\xe2\x80\x99s Italian coach, Maurizio Sarri \xe2\x80\x94 an impression fueled by a television interview in which Sarri implied he had been left in the dark about the move \xe2\x80\x94 was \xe2\x80\x9cfar from the truth.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe obviously met with Sarri for quite a long time,\xe2\x80\x9d Mark Pulisic said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe had a chat with him. Christian got to meet with him for a bit, and it just felt good.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The resulting move will represent a return of sorts for Pulisic, who spent a year with his family in Tackley, England, when he was 7 years old.'
b'His memories from that year are few, but vivid: winning a few tournaments with the youth team he joined, going to professional games with his father, wearing his soccer uniform all day at school, playing on a concrete soccer court afterward for hours.'

b'On Soccer'
b'By Rory Smith'
b'BARCELONA, Spain \xe2\x80\x94 In the last eight days, an era has ended, a dynasty has been dismantled, an aristocracy has crumbled and a balance of power that held for a decade has shifted. Change has swept through the Champions League. European soccer\xe2\x80\x99s landscape has been transformed. Not that it was easy to tell from Barcelona last night. Here, where the hosts thrashed Lyon, 5-1, on Wednesday, it all felt the same as ever.'
b'This has been a tumultuous week. The peak came right away: Real Madrid \xe2\x80\x94 the team that had held this competition in its thrall, seemingly incapable of not winning it, its opponents apparently dazzled by the mythology of those bright white jerseys \xe2\x80\x94 humbled, at home, by a young and vibrant and entirely dismissed Ajax.'
b'The next night, Paris St.-Germain fell, the prize its Qatari backers covet more than any other once again proving elusive, despite the cushion provided by a two-goal lead from the first leg and the insurance policy of a squad assembled at extravagant expense.'
b'There might, ordinarily, have been some solace in being eliminated by one of Europe\xe2\x80\x99s true giants, Manchester United, but that would only have applied if it had been Manchester United\xe2\x80\x99s first team. It was not. It was a patchwork, scratch sort of a side, cobbled together with what little material Manager Ole Gunnar Solskjaer had at hand, and it was still enough.'
b'And then, on Tuesday night, that other great cornerstone of European soccer \xe2\x80\x94 Atl\xc3\xa9tico Madrid\xe2\x80\x99s defense, so miserly and obdurate \xe2\x80\x94 came unstuck. It was generally held to be inconceivable that a team as disciplined and well organized and gnarled as Diego Simeone\xe2\x80\x99s could contrive to throw away a two-goal first-leg lead, but contrive to it did. \xe2\x80\x9cIt was not a lack of character,\xe2\x80\x9d Simeone said in Turin. \xe2\x80\x9cJuventus was just better than us.\xe2\x80\x9d He has not built his reputation on such acquiescence to defeat.'
b'Wednesday brought one more: Bayern Munich beaten comfortably on home territory by Liverpool, its players and coach, Niko Kovac, admitting that they had deserved no more. For the first time in 13 years, there will be no German teams present on Friday when the draw for the quarterfinals is made. There will be four representatives from the Premier League, for the first time in 10.'
b'No wonder, then, there is a sense that the guard is changing, that this will prove to be the season that bridges two distinct ages. The time of this incarnation of Real Madrid has passed, most obviously, but perhaps that can be said of others among the clutch of superclubs who have, for the last decade, dominated the latter stages of this competition, too.'
b'Bayern is gearing up to rejuvenate its squad. Atl\xc3\xa9tico will lose the player that has best encapsulated its recent history \xe2\x80\x94 the grizzled Uruguayan defender Diego God\xc3\xadn \xe2\x80\x94 this summer.'
b'As they stumble, the English rise: Manchester City\xe2\x80\x99s destruction of Schalke cemented its place as the favorite to inherit Real Madrid\xe2\x80\x99s crown; Liverpool reached the final last year, and is a more rounded, more durable side this time around. Tottenham beat Borussia Dortmund in both legs, displaying a maturity it has previously lacked. Manchester United, reborn under Solskjaer, has a sense of abandon and fun that makes it dangerous.'
b'The Premier League is, at last, benefiting not only from its vast financial advantage over the rest of Europe, but from its decision \xe2\x80\x94 belated, admittedly \xe2\x80\x94 to spend a rather greater proportion of that on managers, rather than players.'
b'That is one reading of the situation, anyway. It is not the only one. The Champions League is about teams, of course, and about dynasties and eras and power bases and all of that, but more than anything, it is about players. Indeed, if the dominance of Real Madrid taught us anything, it was that, currently at least, this is a competition defined by individuals more than by systems. And those individuals have not changed at all.'
b'On Tuesday, it was Cristiano Ronaldo, scoring yet another hat-trick to pull Juventus clear of Atl\xc3\xa9tico, to send the Allianz Stadium into raptures, to deliver on the reputation that convinced the Italian champion to spend somewhere north of $100 million on a 33-year-old forward last summer.'
b'And on Wednesday \xe2\x80\x94 obviously \xe2\x80\x94 it was Lionel Messi, scoring twice, creating twice, and orchestrating Barcelona\xe2\x80\x99s demolition of a courageous, fearless but utterly outgunned Lyon.'
b'For a while, the French visitor discomfited Barcelona; for a while, there was a gentle draft of change here, too, if not quite a full wind. Lyon defended valiantly, and counterattacked with zest, before Barcelona broke the deadlock \xe2\x80\x94 a Messi penalty, deftly, almost thoughtlessly, chipped past Anthony Lopes.'
b'For a few minutes in the second half, too, Lyon had hope: Lucas Tousart had made it 2-1; a single strike, a bounce of a ball, would have been enough to add Barcelona to the list of giants toppled this season. It did not last long. Messi soon snatched it away.'
b'His second goal \xe2\x80\x94 a delicate shot at the end of one of those mazy dribbles where the ball seems to fall completely, hopelessly under his spell \xe2\x80\x94 effectively killed the game, before his two assists, for Gerard Piqu\xc3\xa9 and Ousmane Demb\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa9, helped a victory bleed into a rout.'
b'But that is not what stood out. What makes Messi so captivating is that it is not just the killer blows that count, but all of the jabs and the thrusts and the parries. It is watching him dance around and skip over and ghost away from tackles. It is the precision of his passing, his unerring ability to make the right choice. Messi rarely tries the spectacular, the unlikely: he does not abuse his status, his talent. He just makes sure he does everything, almost everything, right. His gift has always been his simplicity; that is not fading, not at all, not yet.'
b'Eras do end, and times do change. Identifying when is not an exact science, of course: they tend to drift into each other; there are rarely clean breaks. But perhaps it is fair to say that Real Madrid\xe2\x80\x99s period of dominance is at an end, or that the age of the superclubs has been put on hiatus, or even that Spain\xe2\x80\x99s pre-eminence in European competition (every Champions League title since 2014, and 7 of the last 10) is over.'
b'But it is equally possible that none of those eras existed in the first place, and that instead they were simply consequences of the age of Messi and of Ronaldo, their teams the beneficiaries of their greatness, their ability to decide games and define seasons. That has not changed. Their age is not over yet. Everything might look different. Messi and Ronaldo, though, are still the same.'

b'By Tariq Panja'
b'ABU DHABI \xe2\x80\x94 The message to the D.J. was short and to the point: no Arabic music.'
b'That was the edict from the organizers of the Asian Cup match here on Thursday, an attempt to limit even the opportunity for a flash point in the first soccer match between Saudi Arabia and Qatar since the start of a bitter political feud nearly two years ago. The dispute, and the Saudi-led blockade of Qatar, has so divided countries in the region that even the prematch music at the tournament is now viewed through that prism.'
b'At other matches at the Asian Cup, the most important soccer event on the sprawling continent, the soundtrack has included music from the participating countries. That was not the case Thursday at the Zayed Sports City Stadium, where the sound system blasted western dance music in an effort to avoid even the risk of inflaming tensions between rival supporters.'
b'In the case of Qatar, that support was limited to a Korean woman, a male student from China and band of Omanis who arrived during the second half after acquiring free tickets. Almost no Qatari fans have traveled to the tournament amid the blockade of the tiny emirate by a Saudi-led group of its neighbors, including the United Arab Emirates, that has made travel extremely difficult \xe2\x80\x94 and entry into the U.A.E. close to impossible.'
b'In the end, in front of a stadium that was mostly empty \xe2\x80\x94 despite Saudi officials\xe2\x80\x99 handing out free tickets and bussing in fans \xe2\x80\x94 Qatar was a comfortable 2-0 winner. The game was largely tension-free until Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s exuberant on-field celebrations led to a minor skirmish with a despondent Saudi striker, one of few players from his team who did not head straight to the dressing room after the referee blew the final whistle.'
b'Coaches from both teams had tried to play down the political cloud that had hung over Thursday\xe2\x80\x99s game since the teams were drawn into the same first-round group months ago. After the game, they steered a similar course, brushing aside any questions related to matters out of their control, and instead focusing on the challenges awaiting them in the knockout rounds. Qatar, which won the group, will face Iraq; Saudi Arabia faces a more difficult game against Japan, a regional power.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt has nothing to do with football so I won\xe2\x80\x99t give a response,\xe2\x80\x9d Juan Antonio Pizzi, Saudi Arabia\xe2\x80\x99s Argentine coach said in response to a question about the off-field tension. F\xc3\xa9lix S\xc3\xa1nchez, Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s Spanish coach, conceded only that hearing his team\xe2\x80\x99s national anthem roundly jeered by most of the fans was a \xe2\x80\x9cdifficult moment\xe2\x80\x9d for his players, but he concluded the game was played in a positive spirit on the field.'
b'Controversy flared outside the lines, however. Local organizers were said to have reacted with fury after a commentator on the Qatar-owned network beIN Sports mentioned the blockade during the live broadcast of an earlier Iran-Iraq game. In response, the Saudi Sports Media Federation released a statement Thursday accusing beIN, which is broadcasting the tournament across the Middle East, of using its exclusive rights to push its political agenda.'
b'The U.A.E. and Saudi Arabia have been in lock step in their opposition to Qatar, and that divide was visible in the stands. Behind the goal where Almoez Ali, the tournament\xe2\x80\x99s top scorer, delivered the first of his two goals for Qatar, three men stood for the entire match, holding aloft two flags, one a Saudi one and the other Emirati, fused together.'
b'Saudi efforts to boost crowd numbers included commandeering two desks at the entrance of the Bab al Qasr hotel, situated yards from the U.A.E.\xe2\x80\x99s presidential palace. There, officials armed with fist-sized stacks of tickets, distributed them for free to fans \xe2\x80\x94 whether Saudi or not \xe2\x80\x94 with only one request: Support Saudi Arabia.'
b'The efforts largely fell flat. The attendance was declared at just over 16,000, though the actual number of fans appeared far lower. Qatar had almost none: a Qatar soccer federation spokesman said as many as 2,000 fans would have made the trip in normal times. In the end, Qatar had to make do with a small and curious collection of followers that included Janko Yang, a 23-year-old Chinese student who grew fond of Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s soccer team after its under-23 squad visited his hometown, Changzhou, last year.'
b'At the other end of the stadium, Mary Lee, the Korean communications worker who has become relatively well-known around the team, had somehow snagged a seat in the media area. Sporting a silk dress she had made in the maroon and white colors of Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s flag \xe2\x80\x94 a direct challenge to rules that forbid public support of Qatar in the U.A.E. \xe2\x80\x94 Lee, 45, vowed to stay at the tournament until her adopted country completes its run. (Asked to change clothing by security officials before she attended the tournament opener between the U.A.E. and Bahrain, Lee has been given dispensation to wear her elaborate outfit only at Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s games.)'
b'The most voluble support, though, came from the group of Omanis who had raced across the city after watching their team clinch berth in the knockout rounds with a 3-1 victory over Turkmenistan. Beneficiaries of the free Saudi tickets, they cheered Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s players as they celebrated their victory. Oman has historically enjoyed a friendly relationship with all its neighbors, and has adopted a neutral role in the Gulf dispute.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe are like one country, we are one people in the Gulf, and we are cheering for them because they haven\xe2\x80\x99t got fans here,\xe2\x80\x9d said Abdullah Moqubuli, 30, before adding that he and his friends would have cheered for Saudi Arabia, too, had the Saudis managed to score a goal.'
b'S\xc3\xa1nchez, Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s coach, acknowledged their contribution after the match.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe appreciated it and we want to thank them because it\xe2\x80\x99s important to us to have also some people with the team,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s captain, Hassan al-Haydos, had a similar message for Yang, the Chinese student.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99d like to thank him, and tell him to come to the next game,\xe2\x80\x9d al-Haydos said.'

b'By Caitlin Murray'
b'LOS ANGELES \xe2\x80\x94 When the members of the United States women\xe2\x80\x99s national team negotiated their current collective bargaining agreement with U.S. Soccer in 2017, they secured what seemed to be a significant victory on match bonuses.'
b'In addition to seeing those bonuses increase as much as sixfold for winning certain games, the players no longer needed to win to collect extra pay. For the first time, they would also earn bonuses even if they tied matches against top-tier opponents.'
b'The compromise \xe2\x80\x94 ceding some guaranteed compensation from salaries in exchange for higher performance bonuses \xe2\x80\x94 helped break a deadlock in negotiations amid a broader fight over pay equity and working conditions, a battle that recently moved to federal court. But the players also decided the arrangement was a calculated risk worth taking: Playing for one of the world\xe2\x80\x99s best teams, they view every game as winnable. And with each victory set to be worth as much as $8,500 per player, the bonuses brought the potential for tens of thousands of dollars in extra income.'
b'Yet two years after striking their deal, the players are coping with the reality that winning isn\xe2\x80\x99t always entirely within their control. Experiments with roster selections, starting lineups, tactical formations and even substitutions by Coach Jill Ellis \xe2\x80\x94 all within her purview and part of the normal evaluation period between major championships \xe2\x80\x94 have led to uneven performances and to frustration within a team that now has large payouts on the line every time it takes the field.'
b'During the two years since the new C.B.A. took effect, in fact, the team has missed out on roughly $1.7 million in performance bonuses \xe2\x80\x94 sometimes as much as $200,000 for a single match. For some players, that is as much as $74,250 each. The analysis of bonus pay is based on figures contained in the team\xe2\x80\x99s C.B.A., which has not been released publicly.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe have a very bonus-heavy structure, purposefully \xe2\x80\x94 we win a lot of games and expect that we\xe2\x80\x99ll win a lot of games,\xe2\x80\x9d forward Megan Rapinoe said. \xe2\x80\x9cThat is part of the balance, understanding that we have a lot of money tied to wins and especially wins against top teams.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The payments, which for the first time are based on the quality of a given opponent, are worth a maximum of $8,500 per player for a win against the four top-ranked teams in the world, plus Canada, and up to $1,750 for a draw. Against a tier of opponents ranked Nos. 5 through 8, wins are worth $6,500 and draws $1,250. If the Americans beat a team in the lowest bonus tier, like Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s 6-0 thrashing of Belgium, each player on the roster earns a bonus of $5,250.'
b'Lose, though, for any reason, and the players on U.S. Soccer contracts get no bonus at all.'
b'Asked about how experimentation may cost the team short-term results \xe2\x80\x94 and thus, bonuses \xe2\x80\x94 Ellis said her priority has been looking long term and leaving no stone unturned before the World Cup.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou want to win,\xe2\x80\x9d Ellis said, \xe2\x80\x9cbut I\xe2\x80\x99d rather get every box checked.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It is also worth noting that the team isn\xe2\x80\x99t losing more than it has historically; from the end of 2017 to the start of 2019, the United States even went on a 28-game unbeaten streak. But with each result now carrying a higher price tag for each player, the unpredictability created by abrupt experiments by Ellis has been unsettling to some in the locker room.'
b'Ellis\xe2\x80\x99s experiments have varied, including using three-back systems that featured a midfielder, Allie Long, as a center back, or others that pushed wing Mallory Pugh into a central midfield role for the first time against several of the world\xe2\x80\x99s top teams. Once, Ellis asked Crystal Dunn to play three positions in a single match.'
b'When there was a reprieve from such tests during the team\xe2\x80\x99s World Cup qualifying tournament last year \xe2\x80\x94 Ellis kept her approach simple as the United States bulldozed through the event \xe2\x80\x94 the players noticed.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99ve seen a lot more consistency in the lineups and within the roster, so we\xe2\x80\x99re seeing more consistency on the field and on the score sheets,\xe2\x80\x9d Alex Morgan said at the time.'
b'But once the Americans clinched their spot in France, the tinkering resumed, and it has continued, even as the World Cup nears.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSometimes it\xe2\x80\x99s O.K. to sacrifice results in terms of performance to get the best out of the team and figure out what that is,\xe2\x80\x9d Rapinoe said last week, \xe2\x80\x9cbut we\xe2\x80\x99re probably past that point \xe2\x80\x94 or we should be.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The players were aware of the potential downside of their new C.B.A. even before they ratified it two years ago: A month before the players approved the deal, which retroactively covered all results in early 2017, they had been trounced at a new tournament, the SheBelieves Cup, while struggling to adapt to a new tactical system.'
b'The team lost the SheBelieves Cup again this year when continued tinkering by Ellis resulted in draws against Japan and England. Because the tournament also offers a $5,000 bonus per player for a first-place finish \xe2\x80\x94 another carrot in the new C.B.A. \xe2\x80\x94 the team missed out on a total of nearly $400,000 in combined bonuses over a single two-week period.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe paycheck was a little light last month, that\xe2\x80\x99s for sure,\xe2\x80\x9d Rapinoe joked last week. \xe2\x80\x9cUnfortunately.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Those paychecks, though, represent the optimistic stance the team took in its C.B.A. negotiations in 2017. With U.S. Soccer unwilling to increase guaranteed salaries, the team sought other ways to increase its compensation and maximize the upside of future success. Unlike their men\xe2\x80\x99s counterparts, however, the women\xe2\x80\x99s players do not have large club salaries to fall back on if they get injured, fall out of favor or \xe2\x80\x94 in a worst-case scenario \xe2\x80\x94 miss out on the biggest bonuses by failing to qualify for the World Cup.'
b'That made the women\xe2\x80\x99s new C.B.A. a stark departure for a team that had prioritized the stability of guaranteed pay. But it also means that a single poor performance now stings far more than it used to, even if it helps Ellis collect valuable insight.'
b'Ultimately, though, the prize that matters most to the players is winning the World Cup. If they successfully defend their world title this summer, all the dropped results and experimenting will have been worth it.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf we just breeze through and beat every team, 2-0 or 3-0, we\xe2\x80\x99re not going to learn anything,\xe2\x80\x9d defender Becky Sauerbrunn said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s good to get players who don\xe2\x80\x99t have a lot of experience playing time. It\xe2\x80\x99s good to play different formations and see if it works, or not, against the top teams in the world.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI see a lot of value in the losses, the wins and the ties.\xe2\x80\x9d'

She carefully pulls a diamant\xc3\xa9 out of a pile and, using tweezers, daubs it with glue and then applies it to her nail bed. \xe2\x80\x9cI have to touch them up, as a few have fallen off,\xe2\x80\x9d she says.'
b'Kocher, who founded her eponymous line, Koch\xc3\xa9, in 2015 \xe2\x80\x94 and who also currently serves as the artistic director of the Parisian M\xc3\xa9tiers d\xe2\x80\x99Art feather and floral embroidery house, Lemari\xc3\xa9 \xe2\x80\x94 is known for her mastery of rich embellishment. For Koch\xc3\xa9, she brings her hands-on crafty sensibility to streetwear-inspired ready-to-wear, finessing nylon sports jackets with lace inserts and encrusting catsuits with studs and Swarovski crystals. \xe2\x80\x9cI love the culture of couture, and I am fascinated to see how I can continue the story and make it more contemporary with a relaxed attitude,\xe2\x80\x9d she says. \xe2\x80\x9cTo create a new vocabulary between these worlds.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'Her fall 2019 collection, presented in Paris last month, was perhaps her most apt mash-up yet \xe2\x80\x94 a pastiche of iconic sportswear fabrics and racy graphics mixed with evening wear in the form of bias cut gowns assembled from deconstructed soccer jerseys (representing 19 soccer teams all around the world) and bike shorts paired with a sequin-and-satin tuxedo jacket. Some of these looks heralded Kocher\xe2\x80\x99s new collaboration with Nike, a partnership that reached full bloom at a sports-star-studded fashion show last week, at which Nike unveiled 14 national team soccer kits for their sponsored women\xe2\x80\x99s teams, ahead of the Women\xe2\x80\x99s World Cup in Paris this summer. Featured alongside the new team uniforms were 13 one-off looks \xe2\x80\x94 dresses, jerseys, track pants and bodysuits \xe2\x80\x94 that Kocher designed and spliced together from an assortment of Nike women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer jerseys specifically for the occasion.'
b'An alignment with Nike seems like a natural fit for the designer, who was an avid athlete throughout her teenage years in Strasbourg. She played in the French Junior League for handball from a young age; now, she runs in the nearby Buttes-Chaumont Park almost every day. \xe2\x80\x9cSports really helped me to develop my personality: I was a very shy kid, and it gave me this sense of team spirit,\xe2\x80\x9d Kocher says. \xe2\x80\x9cI liked the comfort of the clothes as well, and I think that has influenced me a lot.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Still, high fashion, not sportswear, has been the constant on her CV. After studying at Central Saint Martins, Kocher clocked up experience at Chlo\xc3\xa9, Dries Van Noten and Bottega Veneta \xe2\x80\x94 the latter while also juggling her role at Lemari\xc3\xa9, where she has honed her skills in applied crafts. \xe2\x80\x9cThe history is so interesting because it developed through women who obviously were always working on it from home,\xe2\x80\x9d Kocher says of the art form. Though she works on 12 collections a year (eight for Chanel and four for her own brand), it is here, when she\xe2\x80\x99s fixated on the minutest details, that she seems most in her element.'

b'Supported by'
b'On Soccer'
b'By Rory Smith'
b'Memory has a tendency to smooth over the edges, to conceal the blemishes, to dust over the pockmarks. Hindsight can be distorted, and history with it: Knowing how something ended creates the illusion it was always going to end that way, a narrative reverse-engineered from the bare facts, happenstance prettified to look like destiny.'
b'And so Real Madrid \xe2\x80\x94 the Real Madrid of Cristiano Ronaldo and Luka Modric, of Zinedine Zidane and Florentino P\xc3\xa9rez \xe2\x80\x94 will be immortalized as the team that was champion of Europe for more than a thousand days, the first team since 1990 to repeat as European champions, the first since 1976 to win the European Cup three times in a row, the winner of four of the last five editions of club soccer\xe2\x80\x99s most prestigious tournament.'
b'It will be remembered as a team that built an empire and defined an era, a team that swept all before it right up until the point that a vibrant, fearless Ajax Amsterdam arrived at the Santiago Bernab\xc3\xa9u and brought it all crashing down in one night, the Dutch team\xe2\x80\x99s 4-1 victory in the last 16 on Tuesday sending Real Madrid out and shock waves around Europe.'
b'But though the score line \xe2\x80\x94 the extent of the rout as much as the identity of the team that administered it \xe2\x80\x94 was eye-catching, the fact that it felt like an impossibility is, to an extent, a trick of the memory.'
b'Real Madrid\xe2\x80\x99s dominance of the Champions League has been more fragile than the trophy cabinet and history books make it look. Lifting the club\xe2\x80\x99s 10th, 11th, 12th and 13th European Cups was not an inevitability, the manifest destiny of a club that thinks of itself as the king of Europe.'
b'The best example is the first: Real Madrid was a few seconds from losing that final, against Atl\xc3\xa9tico Madrid in Lisbon; only a 93rd-minute equalizer from Sergio Ramos took the game to extra time, and gave Real Madrid a reprieve.'
b'But there are more, far more. In 2016, just a few months into Zidane\xe2\x80\x99s tenure as coach, Real traveled to Wolfsburg for a quarterfinal. It seemed a favorable draw, as close to a gimme as the Champions League offers at that stage. Real Madrid was down, 2-0, within 25 minutes, and secured a place in the semifinals only in the 77th minute of the second leg, with Ronaldo striking a pose as he celebrated his hat trick. Real would win the tournament that year, beating Atl\xc3\xa9tico again in the final in Milan, this time on penalty kicks.'
b'The next year, its progress to the final in Cardiff was stately, serene, but that final hurdle was anything but. Real eventually beat Juventus, 4-1, but if that implies an overwhelming superiority, it did not feel like that inside the Principality Stadium. Indeed, for a time, after Mario Mandzukic had drawn Juventus even in the first half, Real Madrid seemed to be swaying. Its players would later admit that they needed to regroup at halftime.'
b'And then last year, when Real almost conspired to throw away a three-goal lead against Juventus in their quarterfinal, edged past Bayern Munich in the semifinals thanks to a momentary lapse in concentration and ability from the stand-in goalkeeper Sven Ulreich, and then overcame Liverpool \xe2\x80\x94 and the even more hapless Loris Karius \xe2\x80\x94 in the final in Kiev.'
b'None of that, of course, is to suggest that Real has ridden its luck, or to lessen the significance or glory of its triumphs, or to claim that what happened against Ajax on Tuesday, as the Bernab\xc3\xa9u bypassed the rage it usually reserves for defeats and fell straight into grief, was only a matter of time.'
b'Real Madrid deserves its place in history, and its most recent generation merits its reputation as a dynasty team, one perfectly calibrated in talent and temperament to excel on soccer\xe2\x80\x99s most exalted stage. But that history does not need to be airbrushed, to have all trace of blemish surgically removed.'
b'It has been tempting, these last few years, to see all of Real Madrid\xe2\x80\x99s close shaves, its flirtations with disaster, as proof of inherent greatness: a team that knows exactly what to do to win, that always finds something more when it is required, a group of players whose gifts can guide them out of any situation.'
b'That is true, too, though it is not the whole truth. What Wolfsburg and Juventus and Ulreich and the rest prove is that Real Madrid\xe2\x80\x99s grip on the competition was not as viselike as it seemed. It was, at times, only the bounce of a ball away from being loosened entirely. What Ajax did on Tuesday Juventus might have achieved a year ago, but for one moment, one slip, one whistle.'
b'Those blemishes matter, not because they can be deployed as false harbingers of what was to come against Ajax, or because they serve to diminish Real Madrid\xe2\x80\x99s status, but because they act as proof that all those trophies were achieved not because of destiny but because of the players, and coaches, involved.'
b'Real Madrid does not have a divine right to win the Champions League. It was not carried to Lisbon and Milan and Cardiff and Kiev, and to constant glory, by its reputation or its aura or its history. It was carried by Ronaldo, his significance only highlighted by his absence, and his own refusal to countenance defeat, his desperate quest for greatness; and by Zidane; and before him by Carlo Ancelotti, and his subtle, shrewd, unspoken ability to elicit the best from the best.'
b'Real Madrid could easily not have won four of the last five Champions Leagues. At times, it has been hard to explain \xe2\x80\x94 particularly in an age when soccer is enthralled by complexity, by philosophies and systems \xe2\x80\x94 quite how it has done so. Perhaps that is why it has been so easy to revert to thoughts of a special bond between this club and this competition, to start to believe in destiny. How easily it might all have come apart was illustrated perfectly on Tuesday, how fragile even the supreme can be. That it did not, for so long, is what this team will be remembered for; the picture will not be complete, though, without the pockmarks, the blemishes, the edges, ragged and rough.'

Juventus will be joined there \xe2\x80\x94 most likely in China and Singapore \xe2\x80\x94 by the Premier League teams Tottenham Hotspur and Manchester United.'
b'Ronaldo, a five-time world player of the year, is in his first season in Italy\xe2\x80\x99s top league after Juventus paid more than $114 million to acquire him from Real Madrid last July. Only months after his transfer, the Las Vegas Metropolitan Police Department said it had reopened an investigation into accusations by an American woman, Kathryn Mayorga, who said Ronaldo raped her in a Las Vegas hotel room in 2009 and later paid her $375,000 for her silence.'
b'Ronaldo and his lawyers repeatedly denied the rape accusation when it emerged in September; Ronaldo labeled it \xe2\x80\x9cfake news\xe2\x80\x9d in a video posted on one of his social media accounts, and at one point his lawyers threatened to sue the German newsmagazine that was the first to publish Mayorga\xe2\x80\x99s accusations. Around the same time, the Las Vegas Metropolitan Police Department said it had reopened its investigation into the rape accusation, following up on information it said had been provided by the victim.'

b'A number of the documents Mayorga\xe2\x80\x99s lawyers say support her claim were published by Der Spiegel, which also published a lengthy interview with Mayorga. Ronaldo\xe2\x80\x99s lawyers have questioned the authenticity of some of the documents published by Der Spiegel, but have not denied that Ronaldo and Mayorga had a sexual encounter, which they contend was consensual.'

b'The body of the Argentine soccer striker Emiliano Sala was recovered from the plane that crashed into the English Channel last month, the British authorities said late Thursday.'
b'The body, recovered a day earlier from the channel, was identified by the coroner for the County of Dorset, England, the police said in a statement. The police said that the families of Mr. Sala and the pilot, David Ibbotson, had been informed.'

b'The recovery crews from the British Air Accidents Investigation Branch tried to retrieve the wreckage itself, but bad weather forced them to give up, investigators said in an earlier statement. Privately funded search teams had also joined the search for Mr. Sala and Mr. Ibbotson.'
b'Mr. Sala, 28, who had recently transferred to the English Premier League club Cardiff City from Nantes in the French league, was flying to Cardiff from Nantes on Jan. 21 when the single-engine, propeller-driven Piper Malibu vanished.'

b'Several current and former coaches, some with national titles and many with ties to U.S.C., were named in a federal indictment Tuesday.'
b'By Andrew Das, Marc Tracy and Naila-Jean Meyers'
b'The coaches led soccer teams and sailing teams, guided water polo champions and budding volleyball stars. At least two had won N.C.A.A. championships. A third gave Michelle Obama and her daughters tennis lessons from his post at Georgetown. '
b'The coaches charged Tuesday in a massive federal college admissions fraud scandal were some of the most prominent in their fields. But it was their apparent willingness to exploit their access to the admissions process at several exclusive universities that has them facing federal charges. '
b'Who are they? Several had deep associations with the University of Southern California, where Donna Heinel, a senior athletic department administrator, is accused of playing a central role in the scandal. For nearly a decade, Heinel had overseen the admissions of athletes into U.S.C., working closely with several of the current and former Trojans coaches who have been indicted. She was fired Tuesday.'
b'Here is a brief look at the current and former coaches identified by a federal complaint.'
b'U.S.C. water polo coach'
b'Vavic won 16 national titles at U.S.C., more than any coach in university history (10 in men\xe2\x80\x99s water polo, the most recent coming in December, and six in women\xe2\x80\x99s water polo). He was fired Tuesday after he was arrested in connection with the admissions scheme. He had coached the women\xe2\x80\x99s team, currently ranked No. 1 and the defending national champion, since 1995 and had been the sole head coach of the men\xe2\x80\x99s team since 1999. A 15-time national coach of the year, Vavic was named the Pac-12 Conference\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9ccoach of the century\xe2\x80\x9d for water polo in 2015. '
b'According to the indictment, the co-conspirators in the admissions fraud paid $250,000 to an account that financed the U.S.C. water polo program, and in return Vavic recommended two students as recruits to the water polo team. The ringleader of the scheme, William Singer, known as Rick, is said to have paid the private school tuition for Vavic\xe2\x80\x99s children through one of his company\xe2\x80\x99s charitable accounts \xe2\x80\x9cunder the guise of a fabricated scholarship.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Former Georgetown tennis coach'
b'According to the indictment, Ernst, known as Gordie, earned more than $2.7 million between 2012 and 2018 in payments that were falsely labeled \xe2\x80\x9cconsulting\xe2\x80\x9d fees. He \xe2\x80\x9cdesignated at least 12 applicants as recruits\xe2\x80\x9d for Georgetown\xe2\x80\x99s tennis teams, court papers said, \xe2\x80\x9cincluding some who did not play competitively.\xe2\x80\x9d One such player, listed in the complaint, was encouraged to make playing tennis part of her application essay and claimed to be a top-50-ranking player in the U.S.T.A. for junior girls, which was not true. She was accepted at Georgetown in 2016. '
b'A spokeswoman for Georgetown said Tuesday that the university had fired Ernst in December 2017 after an internal investigation found he had violated university rules concerning admissions. Ernst, a native of Rhode Island who is in the New England Sports Hall of Fame, was named the women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis coach at the University of Rhode Island last August. The university placed him on administrative leave on Tuesday. '
b'Wake Forest volleyball coach'
b'Ferguson has been the women\xe2\x80\x99s volleyball coach at Wake Forest since 2016. Before that, he coached the men\xe2\x80\x99s team at U.S.C., winning 150 matches and leading the Trojans to three N.C.A.A. Final Fours. He was the American Volleyball Coaches Association coach of the year in 2009 and 2012. His success has not continued at Wake Forest, where he was 22-41 in his first two seasons. After Tuesday\xe2\x80\x99s charges were unsealed, Wake Forest announced that he has been placed on administrative leave. Ferguson is accused of accepting $100,000 from Singer in 2017 to help Singer\xe2\x80\x99s client\xe2\x80\x99s daughter, who had been wait-listed by the school, gain admittance to Wake Forest as a volleyball recruit.'
b' U.C.L.A. men\xe2\x80\x99s soccer coach'
b'Salcedo has been U.C.L.A.\xe2\x80\x99s men\xe2\x80\x99s soccer coach since 2004. The Bruins are one of the nation\xe2\x80\x99s top programs annually, and Salcedo has produced dozens of players who have gone on to play professional soccer. A former All-American at U.C.L.A. who had a brief career in Major League Soccer and other leagues, he has been a member of the Bruins\xe2\x80\x99 soccer program as either a player, assistant coach or head coach for two decades. He is accused of helping two students gain admission to U.C.L.A. as student-athletes in exchange for $200,000. The Los Angeles Times and others reported that he had been placed on leave Tuesday.'
b'Former U.S.C. women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer coaches'
b'Khosroshahin won a national championship in his first season with the Trojans in 2007, when he was named national coach of the year, but he was fired in 2013 after missing the N.C.A.A. tournament three years in a row. U.S.C. went 8-10-2 in his final season; he was 82-53-15 over all. '
b'Janke joined Khosroshahin\xe2\x80\x99s U.S.C. coaching staff as an assistant after playing for him in his previous job at Cal State-Fullerton. A biography of her at the Geffen Academy, a private school in Los Angeles for students in grades 6 through 12, lists her as the physical education department chair. A previous announcement hailed her hiring as the head of the school\xe2\x80\x99s girls soccer program. '
b'In the indictment, Singer is said to have contributed $350,000 a private soccer club run by Khosroshahin and Janke in exchange for their suggesting four children of Singer\xe2\x80\x99s clients as recruits. '
b'Khosroshahin and Janke were also asked to create misleading recruiting profiles and to serve as references for students who were not competitive soccer players in order to help them gain admission to other colleges. '
b'Former Yale women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer coach'
b'A third cooperating witness in court papers was an unnamed person whose description closely matches Meredith, who served as Yale\xe2\x80\x99s women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer coach from 1995 through late last year. Meredith was also a participant in the scheme, according to court filings. Meredith resigned as Yale\xe2\x80\x99s coach in November after a disappointing season, but also after, the authorities said Tuesday, he had accepted hundreds of thousands of dollars of payments to facilitate the admission of a non-soccer-playing soccer recruit to Yale. When he stepped down after last season, Meredith told the university that \xe2\x80\x9cit is time to explore new possibilities and begin a different chapter in my life.\xe2\x80\x9d A month later, he was elected to the Connecticut Soccer Hall of Fame. '
b'Stanford sailing coach'
