b'On Soccer'
b'By Rory Smith'
b'LONDON \xe2\x80\x94 At the start of February, Lionel Messi broke another record. When Messi converted a penalty against Valencia, a few minutes before halftime, it was his 20th Liga goal of the season. He had reached that mark every year for the last 11 years. No player had done that before.'
b'It is a fairly common occurrence, of course, Messi breaking a record. He broke two others in December: reaching the most wins for Barcelona, overtaking Xavi Hern\xc3\xa1ndez, and becoming the first player to score 10 Liga goals in 13 consecutive seasons. November, by contrast, was quiet: He only broke one, for Champions League goals scored for a single club.'
b'Sometimes, he etches his name on significant milestones \xe2\x80\x94 highest scorer in Spanish history; most goals in a calendar year \xe2\x80\x94 and sometimes his feats seem more like statistical quirks, curious pieces of trivia: no player has scored two goals in more La Liga games than Messi, for example. All of the records, though, serve as testament to his greatness. Each one offers further proof of the consistency of his brilliance.'
b'And yet the more records he breaks, the more remarkable his career becomes, the less impact each new mark has. Messi\xe2\x80\x99s scaling heights previously thought unimaginable, surpassing marks once deemed indelible, is now so frequent as to be mundane. Messi rewriting the history books is the natural order of things. His excellence has been normalized.'
b'What he has done, in effect, is a sort of impish, Argentine equivalent to what, in politics, is known as shifting the Overton Window; in public discourse, it refers to the gradual process of taking concepts previously considered unthinkable and making them first seem feasible and then, finally, ordinary.'
b'The Messi effect works on the same lines. Before he and Cristiano Ronaldo made a habit of scoring unfathomable numbers of goals, it was assumed that such tallies were impossible. The more they have done it, the more they have made it seem attainable. The more attainable it seems, the less special it looks.'
b'If the worst consequence of the phenomenon, for Messi, is that his splendor is occasionally a little underappreciated \xe2\x80\x94 something that is more of a loss for those watching than it is for him \xe2\x80\x94 for others, suffering the same genius fatigue, the consequences can be more severe.'
b'This week, Tottenham faces Burnley, Chelsea and Arsenal in the Premier League. It must, most likely, win all three games to keep within touching distance of Manchester City and Liverpool in England\xe2\x80\x99s rocket-fueled title race.'
b'So fine are the margins that even a single slip may prove fatal, and once again condemn Spurs Manager Mauricio Pochettino and his team to accusations that they lack the cutting edge, the carat mass, to shine among the elite. Pochettino, like Messi, will suffer because of the standards he has set.'
b'It is worth considering, though, the nature of Tottenham when Pochettino took over in 2014: that Tottenham was a team deep in the shadow of its two fiercest rivals, Arsenal and Chelsea; one that only occasionally featured in the Champions League; one that few, even among its most ardent fans, considered genuine contenders for the Premier League title.'
b'Over the course of Pochettino\xe2\x80\x99s almost five seasons at the club, all of that has been transformed. Tottenham is now, certainly, a better team than either Arsenal or Chelsea. It has become a fixture in the Champions League, with a place in this season\xe2\x80\x99s quarterfinals well within its grasp.'
b'Since Pochettino took charge, only one team \xe2\x80\x94 Manchester City \xe2\x80\x94 has won more points in the Premier League. Twice, Tottenham has mounted sustained challenges for a first English championship since 1961. This season, it has managed to cling to the coattails of City and Liverpool, both of whom have more points at this stage of the season than all but a handful of teams in history.'
b'Given those circumstances, the season Pochettino has overseen thus far may rank as his finest yet. When the transfer window closed on Jan. 31, Tottenham became the first team in Premier League history not to add a single player over the course of an entire campaign.'
b'If that parsimony was extreme, it was not out of character: Since Pochettino arrived in May 2014, Tottenham has spent barely half of the amount lavished on Manchester City and Manchester United\xe2\x80\x99s squads. The sale of midfielder Mousa Demb\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa9 in January meant that, since Pochettino arrived, the club has invested less than $30 million, net, in the transfer market.'
b'On several occasions in recent months, that has seemed set to curtail the club\xe2\x80\x99s ambitions. Pochettino has had to navigate several weeks without Harry Kane and Dele Alli, the lodestars of his attack, because of injury. In January, he lost Son Heung-min, the captain of South Korea\xe2\x80\x99s national team, to the Asian Cup, too.'
b'The club continues, unhappily, to play its home games at Wembley, after a series of delays on the completion of its new stadium, now likely to be available in April at the very earliest, though even Pochettino seems to suspect even that target is ambitious. He suggested earlier this month that it would be \xe2\x80\x9ctough\xe2\x80\x9d to play there before the start of next season.'
b'That Tottenham is still there, then, its breath on the necks of Manchester City and Liverpool yet again, is a remarkable feat. And yet, just as with Messi, it does not always feel as though it is celebrated as such.'
b'Pochettino, like Messi, has changed the parameters of a conversation. He has made the extraordinary ordinary. It was previously unthinkable that Spurs might be title contenders. Now, it is not just accepted but almost expected. Indeed, the question more often posed to Pochettino is whether his team is falling short because it does not yet have a trophy to show for its progress.'
b'There is some validity to that question. As the Sky Sports commentator Jamie Carragher pointed out earlier this season, when this Tottenham team comes to be remembered, fans will not take into account where it played its home games or how much was spent to reinforce it; they will simply ask what it won. But it is hard to avoid the feeling that its relevance is overplayed.'
b'Soccer, like all sports, is about the creation of collective memories. That is why England continues to hold its twin cup competitions in such high esteem, though winning them is often not enough to save a coach\xe2\x80\x99s job or build a player\xe2\x80\x99s reputation or slake a fan\xe2\x80\x99s thirst for success. It is why Pochettino\xe2\x80\x99s bullish disregard for them \xe2\x80\x94 in words, if not always in actions \xe2\x80\x94 strikes such a discordant note among many commentators.'
b'But soccer is also about pride, and status. What Pochettino has done is restore both to Tottenham. That is not some meaningless intangible: It has concrete consequences, both in the stadium the club is building, a monument to its new reality, and the players it will, at some point, be able to attract there.'
b'Pochettino has not won anything, but he has created a club that expects \xe2\x80\x94 and is expected \xe2\x80\x94 to do so in the future. He has fundamentally altered the fabric of the place that he found. He has made what was once unthinkable entirely feasible, and he has done it so often that his brilliance has become mundane. It is easy to be fooled into thinking this is normal. It is not, and the best measure of how extraordinary it is may well be how ordinary it seems.'

b'MANCHESTER, England \xe2\x80\x94 That sinking feeling, that sense that it was all happening again to Paris St.-Germain, might have set in a couple of weeks ago, when Neymar limped off a field in Strasbourg, his face crumpled with tears, the fifth metatarsal in his right foot broken.'
b'Or it might not have come until a little later, until last weekend, until the point when Edinson Cavani, wincing from the pain in his hip, was told he would not be able to return to the field at the Parc des Princes for the second half of a Ligue 1 game against Bordeaux.'
b'Or maybe it was not the injuries, but the composite effect of them: Maybe it was the slow drift in P.S.G.\xe2\x80\x99s performances these last few weeks \xe2\x80\x94 their first domestic defeat of the season, at Lyon; being taken to extra time in a cup game by Villefranche, a third-division team; squeezing past Bordeaux, once Cavani had gone.'
b'It all pointed in the same direction: that just as the mercury was rising and thoughts were turning once again to the Champions League, the most ambitious club project in Europe, the team that has distorted the transfer market and \xe2\x80\x94 allegedly \xe2\x80\x94 bent the rules in its relentless pursuit of success in this competition, was splintering and fracturing and crumbling once again.'
b'Suddenly, it felt as if a meeting in the last 16 with Manchester United was rather more daunting than it had seemed when the draw was made, back in December, back before Neymar\xe2\x80\x99s tears, back before Cavani\xe2\x80\x99s grimace, back before Villefranche.'
b'That was partly because of P.S.G.\xe2\x80\x99s travails, of course, but partly because United looked reinvigorated. b'Solskjaer had not lost a game as United manager before Tuesday\xe2\x80\x99s visit from P.S.G. Anthony Martial and Marcus Rashford were thriving, too.'
b'Old Trafford had its smile back, a predator\xe2\x80\x99s grin, ready to become the latest place where P.S.G.\xe2\x80\x99s finest-laid plans fell to pieces, just as they had at the Bernabeu last year, and at the Etihad and the Nou Camp in the years before that.'
b'Old glory would, once again, trump new money; an elimination from a knockout soccer contest would once again become a morality play about the dangers of consumerism, the perils of knowing the price of everything and the value of nothing.'
b'And then, just when it was happening again, it did not. P.S.G. produced a performance not just of class but of cunning and courage, and swatted Manchester United aside, 2-0.'
b'Presnel Kimpembe and Kylian Mbapp\xc3\xa9 \xe2\x80\x94 this great international vision, this expression of Qatari soft power, delivered by two boys from Paris\xe2\x80\x99s sprawling banlieues \xe2\x80\x94 scored a goal each, and P.S.G. might feel slightly disappointed not to have left with more. Later on, Pogba \xe2\x80\x94 against his hometown club \xe2\x80\x94 was sent off, meaning United\xe2\x80\x99s standout performer will miss the return leg next month. With his exit, all reasonable hope of a turnaround in Paris departed, too.'
b'As it turned out, the harbinger of what was to come here was not Neymar\xe2\x80\x99s injury, or Cavani\xe2\x80\x99s, or any of the other feints and misdirections offered by P.S.G. in recent weeks. Instead, it was in November, in the aftermath of the French champion\xe2\x80\x99s victory against Liverpool in the opening stage of this competition.'
b'It was then, as his players danced on the field, celebrating a victory in a group-stage game \xe2\x80\x94 one high on tension and fraught with traps, admittedly, but still a group-stage game \xe2\x80\x94 that Thomas Tuchel, P.S.G.\xe2\x80\x99s German coach, saw something.'
b'His team had not just beaten Liverpool for talent, not relied on Neymar\xe2\x80\x99s virtuosity or Mbapp\xc3\xa9\xe2\x80\x99s breathtaking speed; it had beaten them for effort, too. It had dug in and ground it out. It had proved, against a dogged, determined opponent, that it could fight, too. \xe2\x80\x9cNow, we feel something,\xe2\x80\x9d Tuchel said.'
b'Those were the characteristics P.S.G. fell back upon Tuesday night in Manchester: Thiago Silva, among the club\xe2\x80\x99s first wave of superstar signings, all the way back in 2012, towering in defense; Marquinhos, deployed to stifle and to shadow Pogba, dominant in midfield; the bustle of Marco Verratti, the hustle of \xc3\x81ngel Di Mar\xc3\xada.'
b'Those are the traits that teams need to overcome these challenges, to shine on these stages, to thrive in this competition, just as much as they need star power and sublime skill. Those are the traits that, in previous years, P.S.G. has not been able to call on. It cowered against Real Madrid last season, as if waiting meekly for its fate. It melted away against Barcelona the year before that, unable or unwilling to resist as Neymar and Lionel Messi ran riot.'
b'It would be dangerous to suggest that this victory provided a blueprint for P.S.G.\xe2\x80\x99s future, to use this exception to prove some wayward rule. b'Neymar improves every team he is part of; if Tuchel harbors designs to win the Champions League, he will need the Brazilian back. Better teams than Manchester United, of which there are several, would pose more questions, and find more answers.'
b'That Tuchel found a way to win in their absence, though, suggests that something has shifted, that the P.S.G. project has reached another stage, that after years of searching for a way to win even when all seems arrayed against them, they have found what Tuchel, that night in November, called a \xe2\x80\x9cnew culture.\xe2\x80\x9d Now, they feel something. b'MANCHESTER, England \xe2\x80\x94 The movement is so slick that it seems almost automatic, a machine whirring to life. In the best possible way, Manchester City\xe2\x80\x99s players become thoughtless, operating on muscle memory. They do not need to pause, to think: They know.'
b'Fernandinho has the ball, midway inside Arsenal\xe2\x80\x99s half. To his left, Raheem Sterling makes a run, darting outside Stephan Lichtsteiner. Fernandinho does not need to look: He knows where Sterling is.'
b'Now Sterling cushions the ball, perfectly, back to Ilkay Gundogan, a few yards behind him, but his work is not done. He dashes forward again, in expectation rather than hope.'
b'Gundogan flicks the ball over Arsenal\xe2\x80\x99s defensive line, disorientated, straight back to Sterling. It looks like creativity, like Gundogan is extemporizing, because that is what we want it to be, because that would make it somehow magical, but the chances are it is exactly the opposite: He will have played that ball, and Sterling will have made that run, a thousand times in training, until the timing is perfect and Pep Guardiola is satisfied.'
b'Only a few seconds have elapsed, but the trap has been set. Sterling is in, down the left side of Arsenal\xe2\x80\x99s penalty area, and Sergio Ag\xc3\xbcero knows where he has to go, where he is meant to be. By now it seems, from the crowd, to be effortless, almost telepathic, but it is mechanical, really. Ag\xc3\xbcero has materialized at the far post. The ball is at his foot. The goal is open.'
b'That was the second of the three goals that Ag\xc3\xbcero, and Manchester City, scored in a 3-1 victory against Arsenal on Sunday, though it was not especially different in style from the first or the third: The only real variation, the only distinguishing mark, was how he chose to convert. He put the first past Bernd Leno with his head, the second with his foot, and the third, though the referee Martin Atkinson did not spot it, with the help of his arm.'
b'There was a sense of inevitability about all three of them, a dread predictability. Not because Arsenal \xe2\x80\x94 with its new manager and its handful of new players and its new dawn after years of elegant decline under Ars\xc3\xa8ne Wenger \xe2\x80\x94 is still, at heart, the most generous and most accommodating of opponents, but because that goal is now City\xe2\x80\x99s hallmark, its calling card.'
b'This has been a challenging week for Manchester City. Guardiola kept his players in their changing room for some time after a defeat at Newcastle United on Wednesday, picking over the flaws that had led to their downfall. It had been a fourth defeat in nine league games; something was amiss.'
b'Even first-place Liverpool\xe2\x80\x99s failure to take advantage of the slip-up 24 hours later, J\xc3\xbcrgen Klopp\xe2\x80\x99s team drawing at home against Leicester City, brought little solace. \xe2\x80\x9cWe said that we did not recognize our team,\xe2\x80\x9d Guardiola said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe players felt it, too. b'What they needed, then, was a reassertion of identity, and there is no better expression of that identity \xe2\x80\x94 of what this City team is, or of what its manager would like it to be \xe2\x80\x94 than that second goal. \xe2\x80\x9cWe have scored a lot like that,\xe2\x80\x9d Guardiola said after the game.'
b'That is something of an understatement. No team in the Premier League has scored more goals from cutbacks this season, according to the analytics company Opta; 19 of City\xe2\x80\x99s 66 goals this year have been scored from inside the 6-yard box. City scores that goal so often that it has become its default setting. Here, it felt almost like it was a comfort blanket, this City team\xe2\x80\x99s artful, devastating version of going back to basics. Guardiola\xe2\x80\x99s players do not have to think to score that goal. They can do it on autopilot.'
b'That was true during the manager\xe2\x80\x99s time at Barcelona and at Bayern Munich, too, of course: More than City\xe2\x80\x99s goal, it is Guardiola\xe2\x80\x99s. Perhaps, in time, just as a chipped penalty has become known as a Panenka for the man who made it famous, a far-post tap-in from a low cross will take his name.'
b'He has done more than anyone else, after all, to evangelize its effectiveness: According to his journalistic confidante, Mart\xc3\xad Perarnau, Guardiola has always agreed with his erstwhile Barcelona teammate Miquel Soler that a \xe2\x80\x9chard, low cross across the 6-yard box is a goal half-scored.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It is the goal he encouraged Jordi Alba and Dani Alves to help create at Barcelona, though neither needed much encouragement. b'It is the goal that has characterized City\xe2\x80\x99s success, too, since he arrived here: 57 times, one of his players has scored from inside the 6-yard box in his time in England. b'But that is the thing: Once the machine is working, there is little that can stand in its way. It is the most predictable goal in English soccer, but that does not seem to diminish its effectiveness.'

'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cDear Los Angeles,\xe2\x80\x9d it read. \xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99re welcome.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'A few months later, when LeBron James announced that he, too, was moving to Los Angeles, to sign with the Lakers, Ibrahimovic welcomed him via his Instagram page.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNow L.A. has a God and a King,\xe2\x80\x9d he wrote.'
b'Ibrahimovic \xe2\x80\x94 who, to be clear, was the god in that situation \xe2\x80\x94 joined the Galaxy last year after star turns with European powerhouses like Juventus, Barcelona and Manchester United. Joining the Galaxy, he finished with 22 goals in 27 games but fell short of leading the team to the postseason, a disappointment for a player who has added to his collection of championship trophies \xe2\x80\x94 more than two dozen at last count, in five European leagues \xe2\x80\x94 nearly everywhere he has played.'
b'So Ibrahimovic has created a new challenge for himself this season: to dominate on a new continent with a surgically repaired knee and countless skeptics \xe2\x80\x94 real or imagined \xe2\x80\x94 fueling him.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe age, the knee, not like before \xe2\x80\x94 all this baloney,\xe2\x80\x9d said Ibrahimovic, who used a more colorful word than baloney. \xe2\x80\x9cThey trigger me.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Ibrahimovic\xe2\x80\x99s stateside odyssey was a long time coming. He recalled making his first trip to America in 1999, as a 17-year-old prodigy with Malmo, his hometown club in Sweden, for a summer youth tournament near Minneapolis. He visited Los Angeles about 10 years later, at the height of his powers, for a training camp with the Italian club Inter Milan. The team worked out twice a day, which left little time for sightseeing.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou see the football field, you see the hotel and you see the bus,\xe2\x80\x9d Ibrahimovic said. \xe2\x80\x9cI mean, I heard that a lot of characters live in Los Angeles, a lot of personalities \xe2\x80\x94 actors, singers, all of this. And I was curious: Why do people live here?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He investigated when he spent a month at the Beverly Hills Hotel with his wife and their two sons before he joined Manchester United in 2016. They enjoyed the weather and the easygoing vibe. \xe2\x80\x9cI think the sun brings energy, brings happiness,\xe2\x80\x9d Ibrahimovic said.'
b'When he sustained a serious knee injury with Manchester United the following year, he got a rare sense of his own sporting mortality \xe2\x80\x94 and it persisted when he faltered during his comeback.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was not easy,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI didn\xe2\x80\x99t feel comfortable. It was different.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He was also eager for a fresh start. Enter the Galaxy, who signed him a few weeks into last season for the bargain-bin price of $1.5 million. Ibrahimovic\xe2\x80\x99s arrival at Los Angeles International Airport was streamed live on the internet, and Tomas Hilliard-Arce, a defender then in his rookie year with the Galaxy, said he was among the viewers.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI kind of felt like it was a big day for me for some reason,\xe2\x80\x9d Hilliard-Arce said, \xe2\x80\x9cbecause I got to meet a hero.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It was soon clear to his new teammates that Ibrahimovic wanted to incorporate himself into the fabric of the team, no small thing for a player of his stature. As he prepared for his first game, the inauguration of the Galaxy\xe2\x80\x99s nascent cross-city rivalry with Los Angeles F.C., he made playful small talk with Emmanuel Boateng, a young midfielder.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m going to need you to score two goals today,\xe2\x80\x9d Ibrahimovic said.'
b'Ibrahimovic started the game on the bench, where he sat next to Hilliard-Arce. After the Galaxy gave up two quick goals, and then another at the start of the second half, Ibrahimovic began to mutter to himself. \xe2\x80\x9cI think he was mostly just psyching himself up,\xe2\x80\x9d Hilliard-Arce said.'
b'Ibrahimovic entered the game in the 71st minute and promptly delivered a dose of his hallmark magic: a stunning half-volley from nearly 40 yards and then a headed game-winner in stoppage time. Amid the celebrations, Ibrahimovic sought out Boateng.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI told you to score two goals,\xe2\x80\x9d Ibrahimovic said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut since you couldn\xe2\x80\x99t do it, I had to do it myself.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The rest of the season was less pleasant for the Galaxy \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cLet\xe2\x80\x99s say it went not good,\xe2\x80\x9d Ibrahimovic said \xe2\x80\x94 and the club regrouped by hiring a new coach, Guillermo Barros Schelotto, who was coming off a successful stint with Boca Juniors, the most decorated team in Argentina, and by re-signing Ibrahimovic to a one-year deal worth a league-record $7.2 million.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe club wanted to give me a 10-year deal,\xe2\x80\x9d Ibrahimovic said, \xe2\x80\x9cbut I said, \xe2\x80\x98One year at a time.\xe2\x80\x99 Because I need to feel good physically, and I don\xe2\x80\x99t want to put the club in a situation where they\xe2\x80\x99re stuck with me and I cannot perform for them.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'For all his self-assurance, though, there are jarring moments when Ibrahimovic at least seems to acknowledge the toll of age and injury.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cImagine how I was last year? And then think five years, 10 years back,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI would do the same things but repeating them 10 times more. I was a machine. You could not stop me. And this is not me trying to make myself big for you. This is who I was. I was a different animal. I\xe2\x80\x99m still an animal, but I was a different animal.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Yet even at 37, Ibrahimovic has the same gravelly voice, the same marbled physique and the same sharp edge. His teammates say that he raises the intensity of everyone around him, and that every moment on the field is a competition to him. In training, he wants to win every drill so he has bragging rights in the locker room. And he does not hide his disgust when things do not go well.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhat shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be lost in his big personality is that this is one of the best players to ever play the game,\xe2\x80\x9d Don Garber, the M.L.S. commissioner, said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd his focus on being a consummate professional is really his biggest value.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Ibrahimovic\xe2\x80\x99s transparency runs counter to the way many high-profile American athletes carry themselves. He has found that they tend to be too conscious of their image, he said \xe2\x80\x94 so polished, in fact, that they come off as artificial.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m not an act,\xe2\x80\x9d Ibrahimovic said. \xe2\x80\x9cI will do mistakes, and I will learn from mistakes, and I will do mistakes again, and I will learn. I\xe2\x80\x99m not perfect. I\xe2\x80\x99m just being myself.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He does not, for example, need to travel with a group of 20 advisers, he said. He does not need a stylist. He does not need to censor himself. He does not need to be anyone other than Zlatan, because usually that is more than enough.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI am the real deal,\xe2\x80\x9d Ibrahimovic said as readied himself for a new season. \xe2\x80\x9cI am coming, and I am original.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'A former national soccer star and political dissident thanks the outside world for securing his freedom from Thailand, which imprisoned him on the request of his homeland. '
b'By Hakeem al-Araibi'
b'Mr. al-Araibi fled Bahrain in 2014. '
b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 I will never forget the love and support I was greeted with the moment I arrived here on Feb. 12 after spending 76 days in detention in Thailand. The combined international engagement on my case is what gave me my freedom back. I am home now with my wife, and for that we deeply thank all who played a role in my safe return.'
b'What kept me going during these dark 76 days? Knowing that the whole world was witnessing the injustice. Millions of people saw me barefoot and shackled at a hearing in Bangkok, not because I had committed any crime \xe2\x80\x94 I had not \xe2\x80\x94 but because, I believe, Thailand\xe2\x80\x99s ruling family happened to be tightening its relations with the Khalifas, the family that rules Bahrain, where I was born and which I had represented on its national soccer team. '
b'The shackles were humiliating. I am not a criminal, though I had been tried in absentia on what are widely accepted to be made-up charges \xe2\x80\x94 including the nonsensical accusation that I participated in burning a police station at a time I was playing soccer in a televised match \xe2\x80\x94 and was sentenced to 10 years in prison. I strongly believe my only \xe2\x80\x9ccrime\xe2\x80\x9d was upsetting the Bahraini royal family by drawing attention to the failure of Sheikh Salman bin Ibrahim al-Khalifa, the president of the Asian Football Confederation, to protect athletes, and his alleged involvement in their arrest and torture, after pro-democracy demonstrations in the country in 2011. '
b' I escaped Bahrain in 2014 after learning of the charge against me, and took up residence in Australia, where I was granted refugee status in 2017. Feeling safer, I often forgot there were still unfair charges against me, and my wife and I planned our honeymoon.'
b'I arrived in Thailand only to find myself rapidly separated from my wife and confined to a detention center. '
b'Many people believe that my return to Australia was a glorious victory, but to me it is only a half victory. I am safe and reunited with my wife, but I am also reminded that my dream of eventually going back to Bahrain will not be a reality any time soon.'
b'Bahrain has only a jail cell to offer me, while Australia is now my home and its government and people have stood by me.'
b'While in prison, I had a long time to consider how I got there. I have no doubt my imprisonment in Thailand was a punishment for my criticism of Sheikh Salman, a member of the Bahraini royal family, during his 2016 campaign to be elected president of FIFA, the international soccer organization. My highlighting of his alleged violations of human rights in 2011 likely contributed to his failure to win the election.'
b'I am a free man now, but what about the more than 150 Bahraini athletes and sports officials who were arrested and in some cases tortured in 2011? Some remain in prison to this day. No credible investigations into these abuses were carried out.'
b'There is a dark side to sports in Bahrain. The kingdom uses wealth and sports to whitewash its legacy of abuses, and silences those who try to draw attention to this pattern.'
b'The activist Najah Ahmed Yousif was tortured, sexually abused and imprisoned in 2017 for daring to criticize the Bahrain Grand Prix auto race, and the journalist Ahmed Ismail Hassan was shot and killed while attempting to cover protests surrounding the race in 2012. Salah Abbas Habib Musa, a protest leader, was shot by the police during the weekend of the race, and nobody was held accountable for his death. Next month Formula One racing is scheduled in Bahrain; if the Formula One management fails to secure the release of Ms.Yousif, it should cancel the race. '
b'In Bahrain there are consequences for speaking up, but I am willing to take a personal risk and stand up for human rights no matter what, as are many brave Bahrainis. Don\xe2\x80\x99t be mistaken, as I was when I went on my honeymoon to Thailand: I may be free now, but I and many other peaceful critics remain a target for Bahrain. Relatives of my friend Sayed Ahmed are imprisoned in Bahrain for his speaking out against the regime from his home in London. This week, Bahrain\xe2\x80\x99s court upheld its three-year sentence in what the United Nations considers an unlawful act of reprisal through family connections. '
b'Bahrain has been emboldened thanks to President Trump, who has made it clear to Bahrain that \xe2\x80\x9cthere won\xe2\x80\x99t be strain with this administration.\xe2\x80\x9d The United States was in a powerful position to help end my ordeal, but instead it chose to stay silent. '
b'Indeed, Secretary of State Michael Pompeo traveled to Bahrain and praised the strategic partnership between the two countries, but made no mention of my case. Not only did he not mention my situation while I was still detained in Thailand, he failed to raise the issue of human rights at all. The United States had the means to use its leverage, since Bahrain is a close ally and host of the Fifth Fleet, but it failed to take a stance. Britain, similarly and shamefully, avoided offering support for my situation.'
b'If Bahrain has learned anything from seeking to extradite me, it is that the government can arrest, torture and repress its people and countries like the United States and Britain will continue to look the other way. My case underscores Bahrain\xe2\x80\x99s enormous power to flout international standards, like lodging an illegitimate \xe2\x80\x9cred notice\xe2\x80\x9d with Interpol to stop a refugee while he travels. '
b'It also shows Bahrain that the United States and Britain consider their own interests more important than the lives of individual Bahrainis. These countries are abandoning human rights at a time when things are worsening in Bahrain and will only continue to deteriorate.'
b'I am so fortunate to have been able to return to Australia and continue my life, but many other Bahrainis are not as lucky. If they received the same level of international support I did, they might be enjoying the same freedom I am now.'
b'Hakeem al-Araibi, a former member of Bahrain\xe2\x80\x99s national soccer team, plays for Pascoe Vale Football Club in Melbourne.'

b'Follow The New York Times Opinion section on Facebook, Twitter (@NYTopinion) and Instagram.'

b"Pele, considered by many as soccer's best-ever player and the winner of three World Cups with the Brazilian national team, was treated with antibiotics and said on Friday he was feeling much better."

b'Supported by'
b'On Soccer'
b'By Rory Smith'
b'AMSTERDAM \xe2\x80\x94 Last summer, seven of Ajax\xe2\x80\x99s brightest stars were summoned to a room at the Dutch club\xe2\x80\x99s training facility. Edwin van der Sar, the goalkeeper-turned-chief-executive, and Marc Overmars, once a jet-heeled wing and now the Ajax sporting director, had a video to show them.'
b'Its premise was simple. Each of the players was paired with an iconic figure from Ajax\xe2\x80\x99s illustrious history, one who shared a position, a nationality or (in one case) a bloodline. Goalkeeper Andre Onana, in one example, had van der Sar. Forward Kasper Dolberg got Zlatan Ibrahimovic. Justin Kluivert was juxtaposed with his father, Patrick. Frenkie de Jong had Christian Eriksen, and Matthijs de Ligt was compared to Barry Hulshoff, a defender from Ajax\xe2\x80\x99s all-conquering team of the 1970s.'
b'The idea, van der Sar said, was to \xe2\x80\x9cshow them how to become a legend at Ajax, and in Holland.\xe2\x80\x9d The film was designed to persuade the players, the club\xe2\x80\x99s crown jewels, to resist the temptation to move to England, to Spain, to Italy, for another year or so, to \xe2\x80\x9cstay with each other, to win prizes and trophies here and then make the next step.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The tactic worked. Six of the seven players should feature for Ajax when it hosts Real Madrid in the last 16 of the Champions League on Wednesday. De Ligt will marshal the defense. De Jong will orchestrate the attacks.'
b'Only one of the seven will be absent: Kluivert resisted the emotional overture to follow in his father\xe2\x80\x99s footsteps. He refused to extend his contract and was sold to Roma. At Ajax, they understand why he made that decision \xe2\x80\x94 the allure, for a teenager with a famous name, of forging his own path \xe2\x80\x94 but when they mention Kluivert now, it is with a hint of regret, a tinge of frustration.'
b'Not because he left, but because he left so soon. \xe2\x80\x9cIf a player goes after just half a year in the first team, like Kluivert, we are disappointed,\xe2\x80\x9d said Said Ouaali, the director of De Toekomst, Ajax\xe2\x80\x99s famed youth academy.'
b'In January, Ajax made another video. This time, it was for public consumption, posted on the club\xe2\x80\x99s social media channels. It was a little more than a minute long, but it showcased all of what Erik ten Hag, Ajax\xe2\x80\x99s current manager, called de Jong\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9cspecial qualities.\xe2\x80\x9d It was titled, \xe2\x80\x9cFrenkie Futuro,\xe2\x80\x9d and was released to celebrate the confirmation of the 21-year-old\xe2\x80\x99s move to Barcelona, set to be completed this summer.'
b'De Jong is the shining light of this Ajax team, a player so promising that he has, more than once, been compared to Johan Cruyff himself. Yet there was no regret at his departure. \xe2\x80\x9cBarcelona, enjoy the future, like we do,\xe2\x80\x9d Ajax wrote on its official Twitter account.'
b'The feelings will be the same, this summer, when de Ligt \xe2\x80\x94 a player who has been at Ajax since he was 8 \xe2\x80\x94 departs, as he is expected to do. A 20-year-old defender who is regarded by some Premier League scouts as the best prospect in any position in world soccer, de Ligt could join his friend at Barcelona, or he might end up at Juventus.'
b'Either way, there will be no sadness, no sense of loss at what might have been. Ten Hag might allow himself to wonder a little, he said, at what could happen if \xe2\x80\x9cI could keep them for two or three years,\xe2\x80\x9d into their prime, but that is it.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI will be proud,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe scouts who found them will be proud. Marc Overmars will be proud. Everyone will be. If they transfer to a big club, you are happy for them.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'This is, of course, what Ajax has always done. Since Cruyff himself left for Barcelona in 1973, it has churned out a stream of talent for others to enjoy: Johan Neeskens, Marco van Basten, Frank Rijkaard, Clarence Seedorf, Edgar Davids, Kluivert, Wesley Sneijder, Rafael van der Vaart, Eriksen, Ibrahimovic, Jan Vertonghen, Luis Su\xc3\xa1rez. The Ajax alumni list reads like a who\xe2\x80\x99s who of modern soccer.'
b'The formula that has allowed it to do so hangs on the wall in ten Hag\xe2\x80\x99s office, opposite a series of black-and-white portraits of Rinus Michels, the mastermind of the great team of the 1970s; Cruyff, its star; and Louis van Gaal, the man who restored Ajax to the European pinnacle in the 1990s, with a team reared almost entirely at De Toekomst.'
b'Ten Hag laughs when he looks at that wall \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cThey set you a standard,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, blowing out his cheeks \xe2\x80\x94 but he is serious when he discusses the Ajacied, a cross between a mission statement and a creed for the club.'
b'These are the traits the club seeks to instill in every player who wears its jersey, or who passes through De Toekomst, as well as its coaches and staff. There are 11 of them; they have been arranged like a team. This being Ajax, they are set out in a 4-3-3 formation. They range from taking responsibility and initiative to remaining disciplined and having fun.'
b'The approach, clearly, works. No team in Europe produces more professional players than Ajax. The club\xe2\x80\x99s figures put it ahead of Partizan Belgrade and Dynamo Kyiv. According to Ouaali, a staggering 86 percent of players who are at De Toekomst at age 16 will go on to have pro careers.'
b'But that is not to say it has not been adapted, altered, fine-tuned over the years. That process started in 2011, when Cruyff returned to a club that \xe2\x80\x94 in van der Sar\xe2\x80\x99s words \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cdid not feel like Ajax anymore.\xe2\x80\x9d Cruyff and the cadre of former players he brought with him wanted not only to restore the focus on youth development, to shed highly paid, aging players, but to change the way Ajax worked.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe focus always on the individual,\xe2\x80\x9d Ouaali said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe don\xe2\x80\x99t think about age groups, like the Dutch federation or like other clubs. It can be hard for coaches because they want results as well \xe2\x80\x94 to be successful, to be promoted to the next step up \xe2\x80\x94 but we try to find coaches who focus on the development of players, who learn the individual, not the team.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The club recognized, too, that it had to work faster than before. Players were no longer staying in the Eredivisie until they were 23 or 24; they were leaving at 20 or 21, if not earlier. \xe2\x80\x9cAt 19, they needed to be ready to play in the first team,\xe2\x80\x9d ten Hag said, \xe2\x80\x9cbecause at 20, they are gone.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That meant more physical work at younger ages, and an end to players going to school outside Ajax. Now, they study at De Toekomst, so they can maximize the hours they spend in the classroom and on the training field.'
b'Ajax borrowed methods found in Montessori education to mix age groups, and its under-18 team was abolished to \xe2\x80\x9cincrease pressure on the talent,\xe2\x80\x9d Ouaali said.'
b'The club\xe2\x80\x99s second team, Jong Ajax \xe2\x80\x94 which plays in Dutch soccer\xe2\x80\x99s second tier \xe2\x80\x94 no longer would be filled with senior players; now, most of its members are still in their teenage years. \xe2\x80\x9cWe had to speed up the process,\xe2\x80\x9d ten Hag said. \xe2\x80\x9cThey had to be good quicker.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'All of it was a formal acknowledgment of Ajax\xe2\x80\x99s place in the 21st century soccer firmament. It is telling, for example, that Ouaali sees his job, and that of De Toekomst, not as to produce players for the first team, but to produce them for \xe2\x80\x9cAjax, then the Dutch national team, then the top international level.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The order is important. Ajax is not just about developing players; it is also concerned with winning. Van der Sar, in particular, was keenly aware of the need to keep its prot\xc3\xa9g\xc3\xa9s long enough to benefit from them. It is why he has loosened the wage budget enough to make staying around for an extra year or two appealing. It is why the club is seeking to expand its global footprint, opening an office in New York; agreeing to run a youth system at Guangzhou R&F, the Chinese Super League team; finding ways to monetize its name.'
b'De Jong and de Ligt have done what they were asked to do when they watched that video last summer. They might not have won a trophy, but by carrying Ajax to the last 16 of the Champions League, to a meeting with Real Madrid, they have \xe2\x80\x9cgiven something back,\xe2\x80\x9d as van der Sar put it.'
b'When they \xe2\x80\x94 and possibly other members of the seven \xe2\x80\x94 depart, they will go with the best wishes of the club, and then the whole system will start again.'
b'That, after all, is Ajax\xe2\x80\x99s real gift: its ability not to produce one player, or one generation of them, but to keep on going. It is what makes players\xe2\x80\x99 leaving not only desirable but necessary.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe have to give the path to the next one,\xe2\x80\x9d van der Sar said. \xe2\x80\x9cIf players stay too long, the next one cannot play. The whole thing chokes.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He cited an example from just a couple of years ago. Davy Klaassen was Ajax\xe2\x80\x99s captain then. He was 24. The club had high hopes for a young midfielder, Donny van der Beek, but he needed a place to play.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cDonny was saying, \xe2\x80\x98O.K., Davy, come on now, it\xe2\x80\x99s your time to go,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d van der Sar said.'
b'Klaassen did go: to Everton. On Wednesday, van der Beek will be in midfield against Real Madrid. Another player, another one off the production line, giving something back.'

b'By Tariq Panja'
b'ABU DHABI \xe2\x80\x94 Qatar forward Almoez Ali joined a small group of record-makers at the Asian Cup last week, becoming only the fourth player in the tournament\xe2\x80\x99s history to score four goals in a single game. His exploits in his country\xe2\x80\x99s 6-0 thrashing of North Korea were cheered by just one fan sporting the Gulf country\xe2\x80\x99s colors.'
b'That was one more than team officials expected.'
b'That is because the Asian Cup is being played this month in the United Arab Emirates, one of the main players in the punishing Saudi Arabia-led blockade of Qatar that began in 2017 and already has led to inconveniences for visiting Qatari officials, visiting Qatari journalists and, clearly, given their tiny number, visiting Qatari fans. The looming specter of the political dispute has produced a surreal air around Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s matches, one that is expected to be repeated at its showdown against Saudi Arabia on Thursday at Zayed City Sports Stadium.'
b'Because of the geopolitical implications, that match could be one of the most-watched games of the tournament, though it will most likely not include many, if any, Qataris in the stands. The official attendance figure for the Qatar-North Korea game on Sunday in Al Ain was announced as 452, though several people who attended said the actual number most likely was closer to 100. Similarly low attendance figures have been a feature of the tournament, Asia\xe2\x80\x99s most important soccer championship, in its first two weeks.'
b'The one flag-waving fan in Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s maroon colors Sunday was a South Korean woman who had traveled from her homeland to root for Qatar, according to Qatari officials. Two other unidentified men sat nearby behind a Qatari flag, a rare spot of color in a sea of white seats. The sparse crowd only avoided setting another tournament record, for the lowest attendance, because of two groups of fans bused in by North Korea\xe2\x80\x99s delegation.'
b'The soporific atmosphere most likely will give way to something far different and far more political when Qatar and Saudi Arabia meet to decide the winner of Group E. The countries have not met on the soccer field since diplomatic ties between the countries were severed 18 months ago, but the game\xe2\x80\x99s location in this Emirate capital adds another layer of tension.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s almost more difficult to imagine than the U.S. national soccer team playing Iran in Tehran,\xe2\x80\x9d said Neil Quilliam, a senior research fellow with the Middle East and North Africa program at London\xe2\x80\x99s Chatham House, a British foreign-affairs think tank. \xe2\x80\x9cThere will be some jittery people in Qatar hoping their players make it home.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Political intrigue large and small is nothing new at the Asian Cup. On Tuesday, Palestine played Jordan, which has been home to Palestinian refugees for over half a century. A day later, Iran faced Iraq. Yemen, which is on the brink of famine amid a prolonged Saudi-led assault on Houthi rebels, is among the first-time participants in the event.'
b'This year\xe2\x80\x99s tournament also has been accompanied by significant issues in the soccer world. The A.F.C.\xe2\x80\x99s president, Sheikh Salman bin Ebrahim Al Khalifa, a member of the Bahraini royal family, has been assailed over his silence about the fate of Hakeem al-Araibi, a refugee soccer player of Bahraini descent who was detained in Thailand on the orders of Bahrain\xe2\x80\x99s government. And the event is the latest staging point for discussions related to FIFA President Gianni Infantino\xe2\x80\x99s desire to expand the 2022 Qatar World Cup to 48 teams, a move that almost certainly would require Qatar to share games with countries currently leading the blockade, as well as a simmering battle for the leadership of the A.F.C. Sheikh Salman faces two challengers: one from Qatar, and another from the U.A.E.'
b'But the main crisis at this year\xe2\x80\x99s Asian Cup remains the ongoing blockade of Qatar. The U.A.E. and Saudi Arabia have been in lock step in their opposition to Qatar, which they have accused of financing terrorism, interfering in their domestic affairs and growing too close to Iran. The countries were especially incensed by Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s support for a range of activists across the Arab world, including the political Islamists that other Gulf monarchs consider a threat to their rule.'
b'Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s leaders have denied the accusations of interference and of financing terrorism, arguing that it is their country\xe2\x80\x99s independence that has most angered their neighbors. But the blockade\xe2\x80\x99s effects on the tournament is not difficult to spot.'
b'Saoud al-Mohannadi, a Qatari and the Asian Football Confederation\xe2\x80\x99s senior official responsible for the tournament, was initially barred from traveling to the U.A.E. on the eve of the competition. Initially prevented from boarding a flight from Oman, he was allowed through a day later. Five journalists cleared to cover the event by the A.F.C. weren\xe2\x80\x99t so lucky; they were turned back upon arrival, though one photographer was allowed in. (Saudi Arabia has 47 print reporters accredited for the tournament.)'
b'Local organizers and the Abu Dhabi Sports Council were not made available for interviews. Neither group responded to emailed questions related to the tournament.'
b'Complicating matters further is the tournament\xe2\x80\x99s television agreement. Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s beIN Sports holds the broadcast rights for the event, but several top hotels, including the guest rooms of the Fairmont, where A.F.C.\xe2\x80\x99s official delegation is based, and the hotels adjacent to the stadiums refuse to air beIN\xe2\x80\x99s lineup of channels.'
b'Since the start of the crisis, beIN\xe2\x80\x99s broadcasts \xe2\x80\x94 matches for which it has paid hundreds of millions of dollars for the exclusive rights \xe2\x80\x94 have been pirated by entity known as beoutQ, which Qatar contends is based in Saudi Arabia. As it did during last summer\xe2\x80\x99s World Cup, beoutQ is broadcasting the Asian Cup in its entirety, overlaying beIN\xe2\x80\x99s logo with its own.'
b'Asian Cup organizers have issued statements of frustration and threats of legal action, with little effect. In Bahrain, Sheikh Nasser bin Hamad al-Khalifa, a son of the country\xe2\x80\x99s ruler, posted a video on Instagram this week of his reaction to his country\xe2\x80\x99s last-minute triumph against India on Monday. His chosen broadcaster, made clear by the logo on the screen, was beoutQ. (The A.F.C\xe2\x80\x99s president is a member of Bahrain\xe2\x80\x99s royal family.)'
b'On the eve of the game, beIN launched a website that outlined evidence against the channel, which it describes as a Saudi-supported operation.'
b'The broader dispute has been visible inside stadiums, too; at several, the partnership between the U.A.E. and Saudi Arabia in opposition to Qatar is on display in banners that display both countries\xe2\x80\x99 flags and a set of shaking hands.'
b'What will happen on the field Thursday at the Zayed Sports City Stadium remains anyone\xe2\x80\x99s guess. At an under-19 game between the U.A.E. and Qatar in October, the Emirati captain refused to shake hands with his Qatari counterpart at the pregame coin toss.'
b'Qatari officials and players have tried to play down the political cloud hanging over their presence. They say they are focused on improving ahead of the next men\xe2\x80\x99s World Cup, which Qatar will host in 2022.'
b'On Tuesday, Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s players appeared to be in good humor as they ran out to practice around sunset at a local field in Abu Dhabi, joking and teasing one another as a group of Spanish coaches put them through their paces. Apart from having no fans present at its games, the team has not faced any issues with the A.F.C. and local tournament organizers, according to a spokesman for the Qatari soccer federation, Ali al-Salat. But the players were briefed to avoid discussing politics ahead of the Saudi Arabia match.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou might look at it as special, but in our case it\xe2\x80\x99s not that special,\xe2\x80\x9d midfielder Salem al Hajri said in a short interview as he prepared to join Tuesday\xe2\x80\x99s training session.'
b'Asked about the political implications of the game, Saudi Arabia\xe2\x80\x99s captain and its coach both demurred, saying those thoughts were for others.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe are thinking exclusively on the sports part of the game tomorrow,\xe2\x80\x9d said Juan Ant\xc3\xb4nio Pizzi, Saudi Arabia\xe2\x80\x99s Argentine coach. \xe2\x80\x9cWhatever the surrounding issues, we are not entitled to talk about things off the field.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Al Hajri and his Qatar teammates are guaranteed at least one supporter. The South Korean woman at the team\xe2\x80\x99s first two matches, Mary Lee, confirmed that she would attend. Her relationship with the team is a curious one; al-Salat said she has links to the Qatar embassy in South Korea.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe appreciate the support because she\xe2\x80\x99s the only fan who holds the Qatari flag in the U.A.E.,\xe2\x80\x9d al-Salat said. In normal times, she would be joined by at least 2,000 Qatari fans, he said, but the regular flights between Qatar\xe2\x80\x99s capital, Doha, and Abu Dhabi have also been shut down by the blockade.'
b'Qataris now need special clearance and two layers of vetting to travel into the Emirates, where many have family members. But without direct flights between the countries, fans interesting in traveling to the Asian Cup would be required to fly through another country \xe2\x80\x94 typically Oman or Kuwait \xe2\x80\x94 as the national team was required to do on its way here. (Sheikh Hamad bin Khalifa bin Ahmed al-Thani, a member of the Qatari royal family who leads the soccer federation, has based himself in Oman and flies in for his team\xe2\x80\x99s games.)'
b'Saudi\xe2\x80\x99s soccer federation, meanwhile, has secured thousands of tickets for its games, but their fans\xe2\x80\x99 presence has had little effect at a tournament notable for its paltry attendance figures. The lack of fans has created a strange atmosphere inside the stadiums, with loud music echoing around largely empty arenas and M.C.s who exhort those present to \xe2\x80\x9cmake some noise.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Despite tickets priced as low as about $7, even neutral fans are staying away. Several migrant workers, a group that heavily outnumbers U.A.E. nationals in Abu Dhabi, said their biggest obstacle was not ticket prices or geopolitical intrigue but something far more basic: As one Nigerian taxi driver said, he was just too busy.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m always at work,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'

b'In her words'
b'The U.S. women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer team has filed a gender discrimination lawsuit. The players are the latest athletes to demand equal treatment. '
b'By Maya Salam'
b'You\xe2\x80\x99re reading In Her Words, where women rule the headlines. Sign up here to get it delivered to your inbox. Let me know what you think at dearmaya@nytimes.com.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cEveryone thinks women should be thrilled when we get crumbs, and I want women to have the cake, the icing and the cherry on top, too.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x94 Billie Jean King, a tennis legend who led the charge for pay equality in her sport'
b'Last week, all 28 players on the U.S. women\xe2\x80\x99s national soccer team \xe2\x80\x94 the greatest women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer team in the world \xe2\x80\x94 filed a gender discrimination lawsuit against the United States Soccer Federation, another move in its long-running battle for equality.'
b'The athletes \xe2\x80\x94 including the stars Alex Morgan, Megan Rapinoe and Carli Lloyd \xe2\x80\x94 are not just taking issue with their paychecks but also with where they play, how they travel to matches, and the medical treatment and coaching they receive, in what they called \xe2\x80\x9cinstitutionalized gender discrimination,\xe2\x80\x9d as my colleague Andy Das reported.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99ve always, dating back to forever, been a team that stood up for itself and fought hard for what it felt it deserved and tried to leave the game in a better place,\xe2\x80\x9d Rapinoe told The New York Times on Friday.'
b'The women\xe2\x80\x99s team holds a record three World Cup championships and four Olympic gold medals.'
b'[READ MORE: U.S. Women\xe2\x80\x99s Soccer Team Sues U.S. Soccer for Gender Discrimination]'
b'The issue of pay inequality in sports is of course not just soccer\xe2\x80\x99s problem. Women across all sports are paid less, and many have fought for equity in salary and in prize money. '
b'Here are other cases where pay inequality has been stark, compelling female athletes to speak out.'
b'The U.S. Open. After long-fought battles by champions like Billie Jean King, Chris Evert, Martina Navratilova, and Venus and Serena Williams, tennis has seen the most progress when it comes to pay equity.  The first real appeal was made in 1970 by King, after a tournament in Italy for which she was paid just $600 for taking the women\xe2\x80\x99s title. The men\xe2\x80\x99s winner was awarded $3,500. King would later make this statement: \xe2\x80\x9cEveryone thinks women should be thrilled when we get crumbs, and I want women to have the cake, the icing and the cherry on top, too.\xe2\x80\x9dIn 1973, King threatened to sit out the U.S. Open unless the prize money was made equal. It worked. That year, the men\xe2\x80\x99s and women\xe2\x80\x99s champions were paid equally, and the U.S. Open has paid its winners equally since. Other Grand Slams, though, were slow to follow suit.'
b'[READ MORE: Eight Times Women in Sports Fought for Equality]'
b"The Australian Open, and other Grand Slams. Prize money for the Australian Open had fluctuated for decades: In 1978, the men\xe2\x80\x99s winner was paid about 585 percent more than the women\xe2\x80\x99s, ESPN reported last year. And in the mid-1980s, the women\xe2\x80\x99s winner was paid slightly more. By the mid-1990s, men were again paid more, prompting officials in the Women's Tennis Association to push hard for equal pay. In 2001, the Australian Open agreed, and winners have been compensated equally since. The French Open came around in 2006, and then Wimbledon in 2007, a change led by Venus Williams. Williams made a failed plea to Wimbledon\xe2\x80\x99s governing body the night before she took the title in 2005. And in 2006, she wrote an op-ed in The Times of London titled \xe2\x80\x9cWimbledon Has Sent Me a Message: I\xe2\x80\x99m Only a Second Class Champion.\xe2\x80\x9d In 2007, she was awarded $1.4 million for her victory, the same as the men\xe2\x80\x99s champion, Roger Federer. More recently, Novak Djokovic, currently the No. 1 men\xe2\x80\x99s player in the world, suggested men deserve more money. \xe2\x80\x9cThe stats are showing that we have much more spectators on the men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis matches,\xe2\x80\x9d he said in 2016. \xe2\x80\x9cI think that\xe2\x80\x99s one of the reasons why maybe we should get awarded more.\xe2\x80\x9d"
b'The W.N.B.A. When compared with the N.B.A., athletes in the W.N.B.A. face extreme pay disparities \xe2\x80\x94 though, as is often pointed out, the N.B.A. is a multibillion dollar industry, while the W.N.B.A. is not. Nonetheless, in 2018, the W.N.B.A. set an individual salary cap of $117,500, and rookies earned a minimum of about $50,000. The minimum starting salary for N.B.A. players is about $580,000.'
b'Last summer, A\xe2\x80\x99ja Wilson, a star rookie who was the No. 1 overall W.N.B.A. draft pick in 2018, commented on LeBron James\xe2\x80\x99s $154 million contract with the Los Angeles Lakers. \xe2\x80\x9cMust be nice. We over here looking for an M but Lord, let me get back in my lane,\xe2\x80\x9d she tweeted. Wilson earned about $53,000 that season. The top N.B.A. draft pick last year, Deandre Ayton, is expected to earn $6.8 million in his first year.'
b'U.S.A. Hockey. In March 2017, the women\xe2\x80\x99s national hockey team announced that it would boycott the coming world championship if U.S.A. Hockey did not increase the women\xe2\x80\x99s wages. The risk paid off. Within days, the team and U.S.A. Hockey reached a four-year deal that gave the female players a $2,000 training stipend each month from the United States Olympic Committee and larger bonuses for winning medals. \xe2\x80\x9cWe want to do the fair thing, and the right thing \xe2\x80\x94 not just for hockey but for all women,\xe2\x80\x9d Meghan Duggan, the team\xe2\x80\x99s captain, said at the time.'

b"(Reuters) - Shares in Juventus plunged as much as a quarter in value on Wednesday after the Italian soccer club was knocked out of Europe's Champions League by Ajax Amsterdam."
b'Shares in the Dutch club, in contrast, surged to a record high as it advanced to the semi-final of the lucrative competition for the first time since 1996/97.'
b'Turin-based Juventus lost 1-2 at home to Ajax on Tuesday in the second leg of the quarter finals, resulting in a 2-3 aggregate defeat.'
b'At 0830 GMT, Juventus shares were down 16.15 percent at 1.4150 euros, after trading as low as 1.275 euros. Ajax shares were up 8.45 percent at 1.4500 euros.'
b"Juventus signed Portuguese star Cristiano Ronaldo for a transfer fee of 100 million euros (\xc2\xa386.6 million) in the hope he would help the club win Europe's elite soccer competition, as he did with Real Madrid for the last three seasons."
b'Juventus has won the Italian league title seven times in a row, but has never managed to win the "treble" of the domestic league, Italy\'s cup competition and the Champions League. '
b'Inter Milan is the only Italian club to have achieved such a feat, under coach Jos\xc3\xa9 Mourinho in the 2009-2010 season.'
b'Juventus, which has already been knocked out of the domestic cup competition this season, missed the chance to clinch an eighth consecutive Serie A title on Saturday after a surprise 2-1 defeat at SPAL.'
b' (Reporting by Silvia Recchimuzzi in Gdynia; Editing by Mark Potter)'

b'By Reuters'
b"NICOSIA \xe2\x80\x94 The second tier of Cyprus soccer will resume on April 19 after a week-long suspension prompted by match-fixing suspicions, the island's soccer governing body said, giving teams a warning of points deductions and financial penalties in future."
b"The Cyprus Football Association (CFA) received a number of warning letters from the European game's ruling body UEFA concerning second division fixtures in early April, and announced a suspension on April 9. "
b'Four unspecified matches are being investigated by the police.'
b'The CFA said teams who had played in a game whose result had been found to be suspect by UEFA would not receive their allotted 60,000 euro (\xc2\xa352,073) season funding from the CFA. '
b'There would be further points deduction and fines if a team participated in two suspect matches or more, with a five-year ban for clubs subject to inquiries for five fixtures.'
b'CFA Chairman Georgios Koumas told reporters UEFA was consulted during the decision-making process.'
b'"The situation was so critical that we needed to take charge and make decisions," Koumas told reporters late on Tuesday.'
b'The CFA has also decided that from next season the second division will be split into two groups of eight, with the top four from each group facing off to decide which two will get promoted to the first division. '
b'Those finishing in the final four places of each group will play each other to decide which four teams are relegated to the third division.'
b' (Reporting by Peter Stevenson; Editing by David Holmes)'

b'By Iliana Magra and Palko Karasz'
b'LONDON \xe2\x80\x94 Parts of seat cushions believed to be from the small plane carrying the Argentine soccer player Emiliano Sala and his pilot that disappeared over the English Channel have been found on a French beach, the British authorities said on Wednesday.'
b'The cushions were discovered by the French authorities on Monday near Surtainville, a coastal area in northwestern France, Britain\xe2\x80\x99s Air Accidents Investigation Branch said in a statement.'
b'British investigators have identified a search area of approximately four square miles based on the plane\xe2\x80\x99s path and last known radar position. A specialist vessel will search the seabed for the wreckage at the end of this week, weather permitting, the statement added.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe are aware that a privately operated search is also being conducted in the area, and we are liaising closely with those involved to maximize the chance of locating any wreckage and ensure a safe search operation,\xe2\x80\x9d the statement said.'
b'Mr. Sala, a 28-year-old forward, had recently been transferred to the Premier League club Cardiff City after emerging as a prolific goal scorer for Nantes, in the French league. The plane carrying him and the pilot, David Ibbotson, disappeared en route to Cardiff on the night of Jan. 21; Mr. Sala was scheduled to practice with the Welsh team for the first time the next day.'
b'An underwater search conducted by a high-tech submarine is scheduled to start at the end of the week, in what will be a privately led attempt to find the Piper Malibu plane, a single-engine, propeller-driven aircraft.'
b'The initiative to start the private operation was made by Mr. Sala\xe2\x80\x99s family, after the authorities decided end the search on Thursday.'
b'But people from all over the world have chipped in to help support of the family\xe2\x80\x99s search for answers about what happened. Sport Cover, a Paris-based soccer agency, started a GoFundMe page on Friday that by Wednesday evening had raised more than 369,000 euros, about $422,000, to aid the search.'
b'The page has attracted a significant amount of attention, including donations by soccer stars like Kylian Mbapp\xc3\xa9, a member of the French national team that won the World Cup last year, and Ilkay G\xc3\xbcndogan, a German player with Manchester City in the Premier League.'
b'Cardiff City paid tribute to Mr. Sala on Tuesday, at its first match since he disappeared, against Arsenal in London. Players and staff wore daffodils in his honor, and his name was included in the team roster in the match-day program. Both Cardiff and Arsenal, which won the match, laid floral tributes to Mr. Sala at Emirates Stadium.'
b'At several English Premier League matches this week, the teams observed a moment of silence in memory of Mr. Sala.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt is very difficult to even describe how the players are feeling,\xe2\x80\x9d Sol Bamba, a Cardiff defender, told BBC Sport Wales.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe have all been affected by it \xe2\x80\x94 the lads, the city, the whole club.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'News reports have questioned whether Mr. Ibbotson should have been piloting the plane. He held a private pilot\xe2\x80\x99s license in the United States, and his medical certification was up to date, according to records on the Federal Aviation Administration\xe2\x80\x99s website.'
b'But to fly the plane in Britain with a paying passenger, Mr. Ibbotson needed a commercial pilot\xe2\x80\x99s license, and to fly at night, he needed a so-called instrument rating. Britain\xe2\x80\x99s Civil Aviation Authority would not comment on Mr. Ibbotson\xe2\x80\x99s credentials, but the authorities said the investigation into the plane\xe2\x80\x99s disappearance would cover personnel records.'
b'The flight went through rough, wintry weather over the Channel, and Mr. Sala left a voice message for friends and relatives saying that he was afraid that the plane would break apart.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThis would not have posed a problem for a pilot with a current instrument rating, but difficult for a pilot without one,\xe2\x80\x9d David Learmount, a former flight instructor, said in an email.'
b'Shortly before the plane vanished from radar, Mr. Ibbotson requested and received permission from air traffic control to descend to 2,500 feet, possibly to go under the worst of the weather, or to avoid icing, which can cause a plane to crash.'
b'Willie McKay, Mr. Sala\xe2\x80\x99s agent has told the BBC that he was involved in selecting the plane or the pilot and that he did not own the plane that flew Mr. Sala. He said the flight was organized through a man named David Henderson, \xe2\x80\x9cwho has flown us and many of our players all over Europe on countless occasions.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'Supported by'
b'Embracing scouting strategies now common elsewhere and an ambition bigger than its wallet, Racing Club rides a new plan into first place. '
b'By Rory Smith'
b'AVELLANEDA, Argentina \xe2\x80\x94 Partially obscured by a rusting rack of weights, the back wall of the gym at Racing Club\xe2\x80\x99s youth academy has been painted dark blue and daubed with symbols.'
b'On one side are four bright, color-coded dots; on the other, four numbered yellow circles. Rising from the floor are two miniature depictions of goal posts, no more than a foot wide; fixed at the top are two hooks, looped with string, a ball hanging from each.'
b'Diego Huerta, an assistant at the academy and one of the club\xe2\x80\x99s scouts, walks past with barely a glance, stopping only when he registers the confused looks. At Borussia Dortmund, he explains, the academy boasts a Footbonaut, a futuristic piece of training equipment designed to improve speed of thought and skill of execution. Standing inside a cage, Dortmund players receive a ball every few seconds. Simultaneously, a box on one of the four walls will light up. The player must swivel, fire the ball into the correct box, and then be ready to receive the next pass.'
b'Dortmund is one of just two clubs in the world to have one; T.S.G. Hoffenheim is the other. Coaches believe that two or three minutes inside the Footbonaut can have the same impact as multiple training sessions, but it does not come cheap: Each machine costs from $2 million to $4 million, and requires updates to the software that runs it.'
b'That price tag is way beyond Racing\xe2\x80\x99s means. It is working with a local software developer on a pared-down, budget-friendly equivalent, but in the meantime, its answer, adapted for the realities and restrictions of the game in Argentina, includes the dots and circles painted on the weight room walls, the soccer balls hanging from strings. \xe2\x80\x9cThis,\xe2\x80\x9d Huerta said, \xe2\x80\x9cis our version.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The same ethos is struck through everything Racing does. Like all of Argentina\xe2\x80\x99s traditional powerhouses, this is a club conscious of its history. The walls of the cafe at the academy are lined with images of former stars; half of the room is given over to an extensive timeline of the club\xe2\x80\x99s achievements, from the swath of championships it claimed in the early part of the 20th century to its first Copa Libertadores success, in 1967.'
b'That year, it became the first Argentine team to win the Intercontinental Cup, beating the European champion, Glasgow Celtic, over two bad-tempered legs. It has styled itself \xe2\x80\x9cel primer grande\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 the first of Argentina\xe2\x80\x99s great clubs \xe2\x80\x94 ever since.'
b'Unusually, though, Racing is not beholden to that history, or content to be swaddled by its traditions. Argentina\xe2\x80\x99s biggest clubs are run as social institutions, in which members vote for presidents every few years. The system is cherished as a bulwark against corporate creep, a way of ensuring that clubs\xe2\x80\x99 identities are not leveraged to the highest bidder, but it can make them cumbersome and conservative, structurally resistant to change.'
b'In that context, Racing stands out as a bastion of innovation. It is not just the homemade Footbonaut. It is the support available to the 55 boys who live at the club\xe2\x80\x99s academy, far in advance of what most of their peers in Argentina would be offered, ranging from social workers and psychologists to academic tutors. It is the approach to player development, centering less on results and more on individual progress. Most of all, it is the work done in a small, subterranean office in the parking lot of the club\xe2\x80\x99s stadium.'
b'Here, Javier Weiner\xe2\x80\x99s team of four scouts, including Huerta, sits at a bank of four desks, each one dominated by an iMac. The scouts scour games from Argentina\xe2\x80\x99s lower leagues and a handful of South American countries on Wyscout, a content platform that streams action from across the world.'
b'Each scout has an area to cover: Weiner takes Argentina and Colombia; Huerta monitors youth soccer and Venezuela.'
b'Using the analytics service InStat, they compile dossiers on potential acquisitions, drawing together not just raw performance data but also players\xe2\x80\x99 psychological, emotional and medical backgrounds. They track information from journalists on social media.'
b'Most clubs of this scale in Europe, North America and Asia would see this work as standard now; in Argentina, it is all but revolutionary. \xe2\x80\x9cMost of the time, it is the head coach who recruits players, or the president, with the help of a few agents,\xe2\x80\x9d Huerta said. \xe2\x80\x9cThere is no process: Everything changes constantly. And there are times when crucial decisions are made by someone who does not know anything about football.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Racing, however, is determined to be \xe2\x80\x9canother type of club,\xe2\x80\x9d Weiner said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe have to be creative,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe have to have a network that means we can get players before bigger clubs because financially we cannot compete with River Plate and Boca Juniors.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The mastermind behind that plan for the future is one of the towering figures from Racing\xe2\x80\x99s past. His image hangs from not one poster, but two, in the hall at the academy.'
b'Diego Milito won two Argentine titles with Racing as a player, though most of his success came in Italy, where he was the attacking spearhead of Jos\xc3\xa9 Mourinho\xe2\x80\x99s treble-winning Inter Milan team. He returned to his boyhood team to see out his career in 2014. After retiring, in 2016, he was appointed Racing\xe2\x80\x99s technical secretary, an equivalent to a director of football role.'
b'Milito\xe2\x80\x99s goal, Huerta said, was to \xe2\x80\x9cmake Racing a champion again.\xe2\x80\x9d He is on the cusp of doing just that: Racing sits atop Argentina\xe2\x80\x99s Superleague, a first title since 2014 inching ever closer. Its journey, though, directed by Milito, has been unorthodox.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAll the time Milito was in Europe, he saw how they were working, and he tried to adapt some of the ideas he found,\xe2\x80\x9d Huerta said. '
b'Scouting was central to that. One of Milito\xe2\x80\x99s first appointments was Weiner, who had been working with his father, Gabriel, on his \xe2\x80\x9cmobile technical unit\xe2\x80\x9d: a freelance scouting operation, effectively, that carried out project work for European and North American clubs. \xe2\x80\x9cWe had been commissioned by Bayer Leverkusen, Udinese, Chicago Fire and a few others,\xe2\x80\x9d Javier Weiner said. A Racing fan, he leapt at the chance to sign up permanently when Milito asked. '
b'Huerta\xe2\x80\x99s route was a little different. A journalist by training, he spent four years working at Clar\xc3\xadn, Argentina\xe2\x80\x99s biggest news outlet, before starting to work with Mart\xc3\xad Perarnau, once an Olympian for Spain and now a prolific journalist, author and the biographer of Pep Guardiola.'
b'Huerta\xe2\x80\x99s connection with Perarnau allowed him to visit several of Europe\xe2\x80\x99s most progressive clubs. \xe2\x80\x9cI talked to people from Dortmund, Sevilla, Barcelona, Olympique Marseille,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI went to watch Zinedine Zidane while he was coaching Real Madrid\xe2\x80\x99s reserve team. I had read \xe2\x80\x98Soccernomics\xe2\x80\x99 and \xe2\x80\x98Moneyball.\xe2\x80\x99 I had some ideas on how to run a club.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He started doing video analysis and statistics work for Racing. When Milito arrived, he spotted Huerta\xe2\x80\x99s gift for languages and recruited him into his inner circle. He now acts as a bridge between the scouting operation, the first team and the academy. \xe2\x80\x9cWe did not have a structure before,\xe2\x80\x9d Huerta said. \xe2\x80\x9cNow we have a clear vision of what we want the club to be.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The best parallel he can find is with one of those clubs he visited on his tour of Europe: Sevilla, a team that has built sustained modern success among much bigger rivals by recruiting well and selling better.'
b'Racing has always had a reputation for youth development \xe2\x80\x94 the club is known, in Argentina, as La Academia \xe2\x80\x94 and that remains central to Milito\xe2\x80\x99s plan. In his office at the academy, Huerta keeps a map of all the areas of Argentina where he has searched for talent.'
b'There has never been any shortage of that, of course \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cSwitzerland knows how to make watches, and we make players,\xe2\x80\x9d the grizzled academy director Miguel Gomis said \xe2\x80\x94 but there is a belief, too, that it can be done more effectively, more reliably.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe do not see the mistakes we make because no matter how badly we do things, players come through,\xe2\x80\x9d Gomis said.'
b'There is a focus, now, not on \xe2\x80\x9ctraining talent\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 the endless slew of creative, attacking players that Argentina is famous for \xe2\x80\x94 but on \xe2\x80\x9cpositions of concept,\xe2\x80\x9d the more defensive, more cerebral roles. \xe2\x80\x9cWe want to create the players that Racing needs,\xe2\x80\x9d said Claudio \xc3\x9abeda, a coach at the academy. \xe2\x80\x9cBut also the players that Europe wants.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Racing is looking further afield than any of its rivals for that raw material. It is, Huerta said, often the only Argentine team that sends scouts to international youth tournaments. It has started to recruit players from Colombia, Peru and Venezuela.'
b'Just as significant, it has \xe2\x80\x9cformalized,\xe2\x80\x9d as Weiner put it, the other end of the process. \xe2\x80\x9cI remember seeing a couple of tall, blond guys in the crowd at one game,\xe2\x80\x9d Weiner said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt turned out they were scouts from F.C. Copenhagen, in Denmark. There was nobody to help them get tickets to watch a player, so they just ended up behind the goal. We have changed that now.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'So new that there remains some suspicion about it. The concept of scouting remains alien to some. Huerta is regularly asked by colleagues from other teams why he is bothering to watch lower tier games or follow players from Venezuela. There are skeptics within the club, too; Milito\xe2\x80\x99s revolution has not been entirely peaceful. Change does not come easily, even with such a potent figurehead. The team he has built, though, has the courage of its convictions. Racing can see the future; or its own, homemade version of it, at least.'
