b'In the Netherlands, thousands of fans turn up every year to watch IJsselmeervogels play S.V. Spakenburg. But can a local derby lose some of its spark when it earns a place on the soccer tourism circuit?'
b'By Rory Smith'
b'BUNSCHOTEN-SPAKENBURG, the Netherlands \xe2\x80\x94 Every seat, every perch, every conceivable inch of space is occupied. The two grandstands that run alongside the field at the Sportpark de Westmaat are full. The extra bleachers that have been put up for the occasion, no more than scaffold and gangplanks, are full.'
b'Fans hang over railings and cram into corners, standing four or five deep, straining on their toes to get a decent view. Once all the feasible vantage points are gone, one or two decide that there is no other option than to head for the roof. It feels as if everyone in this sleepy seaside village, an hour or so southeast of Amsterdam, has turned out for the occasion, and several more besides.'
b'Ronald Koeman, the coach of the Dutch national team, is here; so is Aad de Mos, the veteran former coach of Ajax. Fans, less illustrious, have traveled the length and breadth of the country to be here.'
b'It is not normally like this. IJsselmeervogels \xe2\x80\x94 the team that calls the Sportpark home \xe2\x80\x94 ordinarily attracts crowds of around 1,500, or maybe 2,000 for a big game, according to Theo Muijs, the club secretary. Its games are shown only on regional television. It competes, after all, in the Tweede Divisie, Dutch soccer\xe2\x80\x99s semiprofessional third tier.'
b'Today, though, is an 8,000-capacity sellout, and there are reporters and camera crews from Fox Sports posted around the field, too. For those who could not get a ticket, the game is being broadcast live on national television. Not bad for a third-division game in a village of scarcely more than 20,000 people. \xe2\x80\x9cWe will make as much money from today as we will from the rest of the season,\xe2\x80\x9d Muijs said.'
b'The reason for that is simple: The visitor today is S.V. Spakenburg, a rival so local that the two clubs\xe2\x80\x99 stadiums are all but contiguous. (They are both called the Sportpark de Westmaat, and share a parking lot; when the teams meet, Spakenburg\xe2\x80\x99s players walk from their own home ground to the changing rooms at IJsselmeervogels.)'
b'This game is widely regarded as the \xe2\x80\x9cbiggest amateur derby in Holland,\xe2\x80\x9d said Rob Commandeur, a fan who has made the trip from Heinkenszand, not far from the Belgian border, just to see it. Given the scale of the crowd, and the interest, there is a compelling case to be made that description undersells it a little.'
b'A Copa90 documentary in 2016 labeled IJsselmeervogels-Spakenburg the \xe2\x80\x9cworld\xe2\x80\x99s biggest amateur derby (probably).\xe2\x80\x9d In the village, they regard this game as fiercer than even Ajax and Feyenoord, the country\xe2\x80\x99s most famous rivalry. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is the derby of derbies,\xe2\x80\x9d Jan de Jong, an IJsselmeervogels fan, said.'
b'Spakenburg, a few hours before the game, does not quite give that impression. It is market day: Alongside the canal, stalls selling vast arrays of cheese and cold cuts do a steady trade. At the marina, beneath a forest of wooden masts, a couple of craftsmen whittle and plane away at their boat. Young men, wrapped up against the bitter cold, dangle fishing lines into the water.'
b'Aside from the occasional flash of color \xe2\x80\x94 a red IJsselmeervogels scarf, a hat adorned with Spakenburg\xe2\x80\x99s blue badge \xe2\x80\x94 most residents keep their affiliations hidden underneath thick jackets. One or two silken flags have been draped from balconies. Down the side streets, where each house boasts not just a number but a small plaque denoting the name of the family who call it home, a few more flutter from doorways. Often, red and blue sit side by side, in those places where loyalties are split.'
b'There is a reason for the peace. Bars in Spakenburg are forbidden from selling alcohol until 5 p.m. on derby day, the legacy of sporadic outbreaks of violence in years gone by. Some suggest the problems were related to hooligans from professional teams \xe2\x80\x94 Ajax and ADO Den Haag, in particular \xe2\x80\x94 who used the game as an excuse to settle their own scores; others look a little closer to home.'
b'Regardless, the effect of the alcohol ban has been pronounced. Rather than thronging the town, fans now tend to gather at house parties instead. \xe2\x80\x9cWe started at 11,\xe2\x80\x9d de Jong said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe ate fish. Also there was beer.\xe2\x80\x9d He is swaying, just a little, as he says it.'
b'Occasional bursts of boisterous chanting echo around the streets, though the big celebration \xe2\x80\x94 an official fan party thrown by IJsselmeervogels fans \xe2\x80\x94 was held on an industrial estate a 40-minute walk away. That, too, you sense, is deliberate: A brisk walk in freezing temperatures has a conveniently sobering effect.'
b'It is as kickoff approaches that the fans appear: dozens at first, then hundreds, a great tide walking toward the Sportpark, so many that it seems impossible that the village seemed empty just a few minutes earlier. Slowly, the stadium begins to fill. Finally, the show starts.'
b'Those who grew up with the game have always regarded it as special. \xe2\x80\x9cYou do not have a choice: You are either red or blue, from birth,\xe2\x80\x9d said Joran van Dierman, a red, here with his wife, Maureen, a blue. \xe2\x80\x9cEveryone remembers the first time they came to a derby.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In recent years, though, the game\xe2\x80\x99s reputation has grown, particularly among a certain type of soccer fan. It has become a destination game, a kind of hipster bucket-list item for anyone seeking a jolt of authenticity, something untainted by the sanitized, prepackaged corporate glamour of the world\xe2\x80\x99s elite leagues. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is quite a cool mix,\xe2\x80\x9d said Commandeur, here with a clutch of his teammates from their hometown club. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is an amateur game, but with a more professional vibe.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In the Netherlands, it is now what puts Spakenburg on the map. \xe2\x80\x9cI travel a lot for work, to Amsterdam, to Utrecht,\xe2\x80\x9d van Dierman said. \xe2\x80\x9cWhen people ask you where you are from, the first thing they say is: \xe2\x80\x98Oh, Spakenburg. Are you a red, or are you a blue?\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That fame, though, has spread well beyond the Dutch border. \xe2\x80\x9cWe have had requests from fans from Belgium, Germany, Austria, everywhere,\xe2\x80\x9d said Henk van de Groep, IJsselmeervogels\xe2\x80\x99s communications manager.'
b'Muijs, too, has been inundated with requests. \xe2\x80\x9cThere have been a lot of things on social media,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cA few years ago, there was a list of the top 20 derbies in the world. Boca Juniors against River Plate was first. We were 19th. It\xe2\x80\x99s not even a professional game!\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The game\xe2\x80\x99s appeal is not the standard of play, but the theater that surrounds it. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is a strong rivalry, but in a good way,\xe2\x80\x9d said Reinie van de Groep (no relation to Henk); she grew up here, but regards herself as a \xe2\x80\x9cpurple.\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x9cIt is very humorous, very creative,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'Fans of both clubs have, in the past, staged eye-catching stunts before the game. IJsselmeervogels fans released a live pig on Spakenburg\xe2\x80\x99s field, a nod to their rivals\xe2\x80\x99 reputation as the farmers\xe2\x80\x99 team; Spakenburg responded by hiring a plane to release hundreds of inflatable toilet brushes over enemy territory. There have been banners depicting warlike Smurfs, and enormous, inflatable Vikings.'
b'This edition\xe2\x80\x99s efforts center on \xe2\x80\x9cLa Casa de Papel,\xe2\x80\x9d a Spanish Netflix series about a heist at the Royal Mint in Madrid. Before the game, the home fans unveil a huge mural depicting several of their players in the show\xe2\x80\x99s red hoodies, above the slogan \xe2\x80\x9cLa Casa de los P\xc3\xa1jaros\xe2\x80\x9d: the Bird Cage. On the field, six men, their faces concealed by Guy Fawkes masks \xe2\x80\x94 another nod to the series \xe2\x80\x94 fire toy machine guns into the air. Fans are handed masks as they enter. Even the away section, clad in blue, has them, though nobody can quite explain the significance of the reference.'
b'There are streamers and glitter cannons and air dancers. The game kicks off 10 minutes late, in fact, because the display was so lavish that nobody seemed to have taken into account that all of the paraphernalia would have to be removed from the field. For much of the first half, players on one flank have to dodge not only opponents but the bright red streamers left littering the halfway line, too.'
b'The game, almost inevitably, feels something of an afterthought. IJsselmeervogels \xe2\x80\x94 historically the more successful of the two teams, and chasing a championship again this season \xe2\x80\x94 takes the lead. Spakenburg equalizes a few minutes later. Early in the second half, the host is reduced to 10 men, its midfielder Maikel de Harder sent off for lashing out at a Spakenburg player. It peters out into a feisty, full-blooded tie.'
b'By the end, the noise has abated a little. Fans start to filter out, clutching their masks as mementos. Perhaps the result has left everybody dissatisfied. Perhaps thoughts are drifting, now, to the lifting of the alcohol ban at 5 p.m.'
b'A few fans confide that this has been a more low-key affair than they had been expecting, that the previous encounter this season \xe2\x80\x94 also a tie \xe2\x80\x94 was a little more colorful, a little more of an occasion. They wonder if the novelty has worn off, or if the reputation now weighs too heavily, if the expectations are impossible to match.'
b'A few minutes after the game, the road out of Spakenburg is choked with traffic. Those who came from much further afield to watch the derby of derbies are starting to leave. They have had their weekend road trip, seen the world\xe2\x80\x99s biggest amateur derby, ticked another item off the bucket list, devoured another experience. The locals walk home, to the houses with their names etched outside and the flags hanging from balconies, to clear up the detritus of the parties they hosted. Spakenburg will be quiet again soon, the same as ever. The game that defines it, though, is changing, an occasion that used to be exclusively local irrevocably altered, somehow, by its contact with the global.'
b'Rory Smith is the chief soccer correspondent, based in Manchester, England. He covers all aspects of European soccer and has reported from three World Cups, the Olympics, and numerous European tournaments.  @RorySmith '

b'The competition\xe2\x80\x99s third round, when the Premier League\xe2\x80\x99s giants join the lower-level dreamers, has been devalued by disinterest. But there\xe2\x80\x99s still joy if you know where to look. '
b'By Rory Smith and Tariq Panja'
b'ACCRINGTON, England \xe2\x80\x94 Andy Holt is standing at the door to the bar, watching the celebrations unfold. On the field, Accrington Stanley\xe2\x80\x99s players are in the middle of an impromptu lap of honor, pumping their fists and beaming broad smiles. John Coleman, their manager, is conducting the crowd\xe2\x80\x99s chanting, soaking in their adulation.'
b'Holt, the club\xe2\x80\x99s owner, does not seek to join them, to bask in their reflected glory. But still, as fans start to leave, a steady stream heads toward him, hands outstretched, wanting to offer their congratulations, or share their glee.'
b'He greets each one like an old friend. \xe2\x80\x9cYou should come in here, it\xe2\x80\x99s only a pound a pint,\xe2\x80\x9d he tells one. Another is reassured that the prize money for the victory will be reinvested in the team. \xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s \xc2\xa3135,000, that is,\xe2\x80\x9d he says. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99ll go straight into the squad.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'On one level, that is what the F.A. Cup means to a club like Accrington Stanley, and to a chairman like Holt. Though Coleman\xe2\x80\x99s team is now thriving in League One \xe2\x80\x94 English soccer\xe2\x80\x99s third tier \xe2\x80\x94 it is doing so on a fourth-tier budget. By beating Ipswich Town, which competes a division higher, in the third round of the world\xe2\x80\x99s oldest cup competition, Accrington has earned around a tenth of its annual revenue in a single day.'
b'For Holt, the bigger thrill, though, is what may be to come. Should Accrington be drawn to face one of the Premier League\xe2\x80\x99s giants in the next round \xe2\x80\x94 Holt had hoped for Manchester United or Arsenal, though Monday night\xe2\x80\x99s draw would later pair those two titans together \xe2\x80\x94 and should the game be selected for television, the rewards could approach \xc2\xa31 million: life-changing, season-defining, horizon-expanding money. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere are not many chances for a club like us to get access to football\xe2\x80\x99s fortunes,\xe2\x80\x9d Holt said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe F.A. Cup is one of them. You could do a lot with a million pounds, around Accrington.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Accrington was not the only club imagining those possibilities over the last four days. That has always been the charm of the F.A. Cup\xe2\x80\x99s third-round weekend, traditionally the most romantic in England\xe2\x80\x99s soccer calendar. This is the point when the teams from the country\xe2\x80\x99s top two divisions, the Premier League and the second-tier Championship, enter the competition, alongside those from the lower tiers and any nonleague clubs that have survived an arduous campaign through the early rounds.'
b'That sense of opportunity has long made it fertile ground for surprises. It is in the F.A. Cup\xe2\x80\x99s third round that the lesser lights have the chance to bloody the noses of the great and the good, when the coddled elite come unstuck in airless, ramshackle stadiums and on haphazard, mud-ridden fields.'
b'When they do, their conquerors gain a form of immortality: Hereford beating Newcastle in 1972; Sutton United overcoming Coventry in 1989; Wrexham\xe2\x80\x99s win against Arsenal in 1992 \xe2\x80\x94 all of them now granted a place in the pantheon of giant-slayers, otherwise unremarkable names remembered in folklore by successive generations. If there is magic in the Cup, the spell is cast by third-round weekend.'
b'This year \xe2\x80\x94 as ever \xe2\x80\x94 a handful of teams maintained the tradition: Oldham, Newport County and Gillingham beat Premier League opposition. Barnet, of the fifth-tier Conference, overcame Sheffield United, a team in contention for promotion to the Premier League next season.'
b'By those standards, Accrington\xe2\x80\x99s win barely counted as a shock: Ipswich Town is currently last in the Championship, enduring a miserable season. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt will be F.A. Cup magic if we manage to win,\xe2\x80\x9d said Mark Pinkney, an Ipswich fan who had made the journey to Accrington with his father, Harold, and son, James. '
b'The three generations had come to the low hills of Lancashire from England\xe2\x80\x99s southeast coast because they hoped the Cup might provide a little \xe2\x80\x9cbreak\xe2\x80\x9d from the league.'
b'That, to many, is precisely the problem. For all that third-round weekend means in the hearts of many English soccer fans, for all the memories it conjures, it is now taken as a truism that it has lost some of its mystique, some of its appeal.'
b'Some fans, like Nick Mills, 43, a Grimsby Town supporter on his way to his team\xe2\x80\x99s meeting with Crystal Palace of the Premier League, blame those teams who prioritize survival in the top flight over a shot at glory.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTeams like Palace and Newcastle: they\xe2\x80\x99re the ones that have killed it, the teams where it is about Premier League survival,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cKnocking Palace out would be an upset, but you\xe2\x80\x99re expecting a reserve team.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Though the upsets still come, Mills is correct: those Premier League teams eliminated this year, as is now generally the case, were lacking most \xe2\x80\x94 if not all \xe2\x80\x94 of their first-choice players, many of them rested for what the club decided were more important games. Palace made it through, narrowly, in front of 6,000 traveling Grimsby fans, but it did so having made nine changes from its last Premier League game.'
b'Others cast the blame on the Football Association itself: for kick-starting the competition\xe2\x80\x99s demise by allowing Manchester United to opt out in 2000, in favor of playing in that year\xe2\x80\x99s Club World Cup in Brazil; for toying with various ideas \xe2\x80\x94 like abolishing replays of tied matches \xe2\x80\x94 to bow to the wishes of those Premier League clubs that see the Cup as an unwelcome distraction. This year, the F.A. was fiercely criticized for scheduling games at seemingly random times across the weekend to meet the demands of an international television deal, and using other matches as test runs for a video assistant referee system. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a wonderful thing, the F.A. Cup,\xe2\x80\x9d Holt said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt needs protecting.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Wherever the fault, the effects are obvious. At Burnley\xe2\x80\x99s meeting with Barnsley, the Premier League hosts had tried to encourage more fans to come by reducing ticket prices to \xc2\xa310 for adults and \xc2\xa35 for children. Though the visiting team had brought a healthy contingent, Turf Moor, Burnley\xe2\x80\x99s raucous stadium, was noticeably quieter than normal. Swaths of seats remained empty.'
b'Elsewhere, there were weakened teams named not only by the Premier League\xe2\x80\x99s giants and those battling to avoid relegation from the top flight, but by those, like Leicester City, caught in the middle, and with nothing much else to play for. The trend is now mainstream: Championship teams often name weakened sides, too; the prize money on offer even for winning the F.A. Cup pales in comparison to the king\xe2\x80\x99s ransom promotion to the Premier League would bring.'
b'Looked at from a distance, it is hard to see much magic left: teams of reserves contesting games they do not care about in front of half-empty stadiums, for the right to stay in a competition everyone involved sees as an afterthought.'
b'From close-up \xe2\x80\x94 at Burnley, at Accrington, at Crystal Palace \xe2\x80\x94 over the course of three games in eight hours on third-round Saturday, though, the picture changes. The Cup may not mean what it did; its halcyon days may be gone. But it still matters to some of those involved.'
b'Not just to the teams trying to win it, as proved by the sight of Sean Dyche, the Burnley manager, rendered apoplectic by V.A.R.\xe2\x80\x99s overturning a penalty given to his team just as his striker, Matej Vydra, started his run-up to take it.'
b'But to the fans, too. \xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99ll see a lot of kids today,\xe2\x80\x9d said Steve Wilkin, a program vendor sneaking glances at Grimsby-Palace at Selhurst Park. \xe2\x80\x9cMost of the ones you\xe2\x80\x99ll see won\xe2\x80\x99t be here at Premier League games.\xe2\x80\x9d '
b'Cup tickets are cheaper, more accessible; as at Burnley, the demographic inside Selhurst Park on Saturday skewed younger than the economics of English soccer ordinarily allow.'
b'For the Pinkney family and the rest of the 1,200 or so Ipswich fans who had made the 500-mile round trip to Accrington, north of Manchester, it was a chance to touch new territory. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99ve never played them before, ever,\xe2\x80\x9d Mark Pinkney said. \xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99ll be a lot of people here today who want to tick the stadium off the list.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The F.A. Cup may not have the prestige it once did; the annual discussion of how much better the Cup used to be may now be as much of a fixture of third-round weekend as the shocks and surprises. But it still provides opportunities: to visit new places, to see new teams, to welcome in new fans. It is still a place of possibilities.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s still a thrill for us,\xe2\x80\x9d said Holt, back in Accrington. '
b'Holt will have a little longer to cherish that feeling. Accrington will face the winner of a replay between the Southampton and Derby County in the fourth round. It is not quite the money-spinner he had hoped for, but there is more to the F.A. Cup than economics. There are memories to be made.'
b'Tariq Panja reported from London.'
b"An earlier version of this article misstated Coventry's status at the time of its loss to Sutton United in the 1989 F.A. Cup. Coventry won the Cup in 1987; it was not the holder at the time of its loss to Sutton United."

b'By Rory Smith'
b'DORTMUND, Germany \xe2\x80\x94 All told, Marcel Schmelzer must have spent hours scouring the video, searching for some sort of tell, some kind of clue.'
b'Schmelzer, Borussia Dortmund\xe2\x80\x99s long-serving left back, has performed the ritual 16 times over the last decade, building up an unparalleled expertise in the field. He has pored over countless clips. He was hoping to find something, anything that would give him a little advance warning, a bit of a head start.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI tried to find a pattern,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. Thus far, though, he has drawn a blank. Even after all these years, even after all those hours of study, even after all those games, the defender who knows Arjen Robben better than anyone else still cannot work out when, exactly, he is going to cut inside.'
b'From the outside, it can seem that there are few more predictable players in world soccer than Robben. He has performed his calling card so often since he first joined Bayern Munich 10 years ago that it now bears his name \xe2\x80\x94 not just in Germany, but also in France, where the act of cutting in from the right wing to shoot with the left foot is known as Le Robben. The player acknowledged last month that he was proud to have his \xe2\x80\x9cown move.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'What is most remarkable, though, is that his go-to maneuver has lost none of its power; the only surprise, now, is that he appears to retain his capacity to surprise.'
b'Robben is, after all, deep into what will be his final season in Munich. He may make his final appearance in the Champions League for the club this week, should Bayern prove unable to get past Liverpool in a delicately poised last 16 tie on Wednesday at Munich\xe2\x80\x99s Allianz Arena.'
b'His time in Germany has been impressively successful: He has won six straight Bundesliga titles and a slew of domestic cups, and he scored the winning goal in the 2013 Champions League final. But it has also been admirably long. Robben is 35. It is 15 years since Jos\xc3\xa9 Mourinho first signed him for Chelsea; 12 since he joined Real Madrid. '
b'He remains, though, an integral part of one of soccer\xe2\x80\x99s great powers, a winger of genuine menace, silken touch and searing speed. If Lionel Messi and Cristiano Ronaldo are this era\xe2\x80\x99s leading men, then Robben is among the most prominent members of the supporting cast: instantly recognizable, a fixture on the game\xe2\x80\x99s most exalted stage, his signature move a regular feature of the latter rounds of the Champions League.'
b'It is so familiar that it barely needs description. Robben sprints up the right wing, one arm outstretched for balance, head pulled back, legs whirring. Then, as he approaches the penalty area, he feints to his right and drops his shoulder, only to shift his weight and slip off to the left. The ball never leaves his control; his opponent is left grasping at shadows.'
b'Robben glances up, and curls a shot across the goalkeeper. It does not always go in, of course, but it does so frequently enough that Schmelzer is not the only one to have spent considerable time trying to work out how to stop it.'
b'Here, though, comes the puzzle. Robben has been cutting left for years. His intent is apparent to all. Defenders know exactly what is in his mind, precisely what is coming, and yet remain powerless to stop it.'
b'To Robben, two factors explain his continued success. Timing, he said in an interview with a handful of British newspapers last month, is one key: \xe2\x80\x9cIf you do it at the right time, it still surprises them.\xe2\x80\x9d Variation, he has previously suggested, is equally important. \xe2\x80\x9cDoing the same thing over and over again without variation will not work,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cIf you never pass or dribble or go on the outside, cutting inside will stop working.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'To Schmelzer \xe2\x80\x94 who has had to deal with Robben in direct, face-to-face competition more than any other opponent \xe2\x80\x94 there is something else, however. He has noticed that Robben has leaned more heavily on his favored move in recent years, using the wing as a decoy to \xe2\x80\x9copen the path to the center.\xe2\x80\x9d It still works, though, because he \xe2\x80\x9crecognizes it when you block his path, and then he reacts accordingly; that is what makes him special.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It is that ability to improvise that Ricardo Rodriguez identified, too. Rodriguez, a Swiss defender now with A.C. Milan, knows Robben almost as well as Schmelzer. According to Gracenote Sports, he has faced him 11 times during his career, in his time with Wolfsburg and F.C. Zurich.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe is very fast, especially with the ball,\xe2\x80\x9d Rodriguez said. \xe2\x80\x9cThat makes it very difficult to stop him. He is terribly fast when he cuts inside. The only way to try to stop him is to stay very close to him. If you don\xe2\x80\x99t, he can hurt you any time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'There is a reason for that. In 2010, a cognitive scientist named Shanti Ganesh, based at Radboud University in the Netherlands, conducted a study into Robben\xe2\x80\x99s movement. She determined that Robben moves \xe2\x80\x9ca little faster than conscious knowledge.\xe2\x80\x9d A defender\xe2\x80\x99s brain, Ganesh said, unconsciously follows Robben\xe2\x80\x99s feints, even if it knows, deep down, that they are only feints. In the time it takes to rectify the error, Robben \xe2\x80\x94 as he was always going to, as everyone involved knew he was going to \xe2\x80\x94 has cut inside and taken a shot. \xe2\x80\x9cThe player can still correct himself,\xe2\x80\x9d Ganesh said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut that will always be a fraction too late.\xe2\x80\x9d '
b'It is a theory that chimes with the empirical study conducted by Wendell, a Brazilian left back at Bayer Leverkusen. He has faced Robben 10 times since moving to Germany, behind only Schmelzer and Rodriguez.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNormally, it is the same move, but it is also the move we are tired of seeing, running after, and not getting the ball,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cThere must be something he does. Maybe he waits for the last moment, I don\xe2\x80\x99t know. Most of the time, I try to wait for his move, so I have a bigger chance of getting the ball back. If I don\xe2\x80\x99t take my time, I have no chance. He\xe2\x80\x99ll dribble past me.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Like Schmelzer, Wendell has spent more time than he might like watching clips of Robben. Like Schmelzer, he remembers training sessions in the days leading up to games against Bayern in which the team worked on how to defend him: His danger is such that it can only be dealt with collectively. '
b'Dortmund always had the same approach. \xe2\x80\x9cYou need your teammates to back you up,\xe2\x80\x9d Schmelzer said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe have to be honest: It is simply not possible to take him out of the match for the full 90 minutes. J\xc3\xbcrgen Klopp always taught us that the problem is not losing a duel, but not covering it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'When Schmelzer decided to go in for a tackle, he relied on his central defender, Mats Hummels, and his defensive midfielder, Sven Bender, to scurry across in support. It was not always enough: Robben, too, was not acting alone; he could always call on the threat of Philipp Lahm or, later, Joshua Kimmich streaking up the right wing to collect the ball on the overlap. Schmelzer had to be conscious of that, too.'
b'Working out when to use the cut inside, and when it was merely a decoy, was always the challenge. Even after all these years, his opponents cannot tell when the move is coming. They have seen it before, and yet somehow every time feels like the first time. They can study the tapes, they can stay close, they can call for backup.'
b'If none of that works, Wendell said, there is one last resort: \xe2\x80\x9cI try to get the ball back,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cIf I don\xe2\x80\x99t, then I have to commit a foul.\xe2\x80\x9d It is when that fails \xe2\x80\x94 as it so often has \xe2\x80\x94 when he skips away too quickly, when he disappears in a flash, that Arjen Robben does what he has been doing for 15 years, does what he always does, and cuts inside.'
b'An earlier version of this article misstated the gender of Shanti Ganesh. She is a woman, not a man.'
b'Rory Smith is the chief soccer correspondent, based in Manchester, England. He covers all aspects of European soccer and has reported from three World Cups, the Olympics, and numerous European tournaments.  @RorySmith '

b'By Rory Smith'
b'MANCHESTER, England \xe2\x80\x94 A few weeks ago, before Manchester City\xe2\x80\x99s serene season hit unexpected turbulence, David Silva ran into the parents of the club\xe2\x80\x99s bright midfield hope, Phil Foden, after yet another routine Premier League win.'
b'Silva is, both in private and in public, a quiet soul. He does not court the limelight \xe2\x80\x94 he consents to only one regular interview opportunity a year, a brief chat to promote tourism on the Canary Islands, where he grew up, in which he does his best to say nothing \xe2\x80\x94 or especially enjoy being the center of attention.'
b'With Foden\xe2\x80\x99s mother, Claire, though, he was effusive. He told her what a pleasure it was to train alongside her teenage son, and enthused at the prospect of just how good a player he thought Foden could become.'
b'Less than a year after Foden had made his debut for City, Silva said he was already convinced that the 18-year-old had the potential to go on to be one of the best players in the world. His only hope, he told her, was that she might ask her son to \xe2\x80\x9cwait a couple of years\xe2\x80\x9d before blossoming. \xe2\x80\x9cJust to give me a chance,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'There is a timeless quality to Silva. He turns 33 next week, but still seems the player he was when he first arrived in Manchester almost nine years ago. He is no less sharp, no less lively, no less fluent: \xe2\x80\x9calways in motion,\xe2\x80\x9d as his one time Spain teammate, Javi Martinez, once said. He still wears his brilliance lightly. He still sees no need to indulge in ornament or ostentation. His is a genius for simple things, done to perfection.'
b'To his coach, Pep Guardiola, Silva is a \xe2\x80\x9cjoy\xe2\x80\x9d to work with; to his teammates, as Kyle Walker put it, he is an \xe2\x80\x9cexample.\xe2\x80\x9d He has been a central figure at City ever since he arrived in 2010, but if anything he is even more integral now, charged with knitting together all of the complex passing patterns Guardiola has drummed into his players.'
b'It is no surprise that it was in his absence \xe2\x80\x94 as well as that of Fernandinho, another of City\xe2\x80\x99s old stagers \xe2\x80\x94 because of a leg injury that City lost to Crystal Palace and Leicester City, offering Liverpool daylight at the summit of the Premier League, and turning the two teams\xe2\x80\x99 meeting at the Etihad Stadium on Thursday into a game Silva and his teammates must win. \xe2\x80\x9cIf we drop points, it\xe2\x80\x99s over, almost impossible,\xe2\x80\x9d Guardiola said this week.'
b'Even City, with all its resources, lacks something in Silva\xe2\x80\x99s absence. \xe2\x80\x9cHe is one of the most incredible players in the world at playing in the pockets,\xe2\x80\x9d Guardiola said of his playmaker earlier this season. \xe2\x80\x9cHe is maybe the strongest in the world in those spaces. We try to attack those spaces: he is a master of it. Few players can do it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Silva\xe2\x80\x99s talent is not his only source of influence: around the same time he was greeting Foden\xe2\x80\x99s mother, Silva presented each of his teammates with a personalized Nintendo Switch console, inscribed with their initials, and two games. Silva is not much of a gamer himself, but he knew many of the younger players are; he felt the chance to play alongside and against each other might help the team bond on away trips.'
b'The gesture was not advertised or announced to the team: the gifts came as a surprise. Silva made it as he plays a pass: with delicacy and discretion, not for its own sake but toward a greater goal.'
b'Those are the traits on which he has built his career, that have led him to a World Cup title, two European Championships and three Premier League titles. But they are the characteristics, too, that may stop him from receiving the individual recognition he perhaps deserves.'
b'Roberto Mancini, one of Guardiola\xe2\x80\x99s predecessors at City and the manager who brought Silva to England from Valencia in 2010, always regarded his playmaker as the equal of Xavi and Andr\xc3\xa9s Iniesta. \xe2\x80\x9cIf he had gone to Barcelona\xe2\x80\x9d in 2008, Mancini said, \xe2\x80\x9ceveryone would be saying he is one of the best players in the world.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Silva has rarely \xe2\x80\x94 if ever \xe2\x80\x94 been mentioned in that conversation, even in dispatches. Indeed, remarkably, in nine years in England he has only once \xe2\x80\x94 back in September 2011 \xe2\x80\x94 managed to be voted the Premier League\xe2\x80\x99s player of the month. He has won that award as often as such luminaries as Nikica Jelavic, Adam Le Fondre and Connor Wickham. He has, needless to say, never been voted the country\xe2\x80\x99s player of the year.'
b'And yet there is a case to be made that Silva ranks not just among the finest players of this Premier League generation, but among the greatest-ever imports into English soccer.'
b'True, he cannot match the transformative effect Eric Cantona had on the game when he arrived \xe2\x80\x94 first at Leeds United, in 1992, and then at Manchester United \xe2\x80\x94 and true, he has not scored as frequently or played as explosively as the likes of Thierry Henry or Didier Drogba.'
b'He may not be as decorated as Peter Schmeichel \xe2\x80\x94 who picked up five Premier League titles at Manchester United \xe2\x80\x94 or produced as many moments of jaw-dropping wonder as Dennis Bergkamp. Unlike Cristiano Ronaldo, he has not led his team to the Champions League crown, or gone on to score more goals in that competition than anyone else.'
b'There are other ways, though, to gauge greatness. Never mind that Silva has won more Premier League titles than Henry, and as many as Ronaldo and Patrick Vieira.'
b'Much more significant is the fact that, over the last decade, nobody has created more goals in the Premier League than the elfin Spaniard; only two foreign players \xe2\x80\x94 Bergkamp and Cesc F\xc3\xa0bregas \xe2\x80\x94 have more assists in English history.'
b'Never mind that he has lasted longer in the tumult of English soccer than almost any of his rival candidates (only Vieira remains ahead of him, for now). Far more important is that he has done so despite being adjudged, in some quarters, as too lightweight for the fray when he first arrived. Silva has \xe2\x80\x94 not uniquely, but more than most \xe2\x80\x94 changed the way the Premier League sees itself; he has played a role in ending the tyranny of the powerhouse. He has not just helped to define and refine the playing style with which City is now synonymous, but proved that small, technical players can thrive in England.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou can see his quality from how long he has survived in the Premier League,\xe2\x80\x9d Guardiola said. \xe2\x80\x9cIf you survive, it is because you are a better player. When he moves, it is clever, more intelligent. When you see things like he does, it is because you are more intelligent than the others.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That he is so easily overlooked \xe2\x80\x94 when Alan Shearer nominated a player to enter that pantheon last year, he went for Silva\xe2\x80\x99s teammate Sergio Ag\xc3\xbcero \xe2\x80\x94 is in part because of the person Silva is: shy, private, not given to grand public declarations of his genius.'
b'But it is also because of the player he is. Silva does not pretend to be a great soloist; he does not play to the gallery or for his personal highlights reel. He is not especially quick or frighteningly strong or ruthlessly productive.'
b'He is, instead, an embodiment of that old Guardiola maxim: He takes the ball; he passes the ball. The better he plays, the brighter others shine. It has been easy to lose sight of him, a player who seeks nothing but to be a part of the collective, but he has always been at the heart of it.'
b'It is hard to tell, but he is slowly descending from the peak he has occupied for almost a decade. Even he thinks he has just a couple of years left before he is replaced. He may be right: Foden may go on to be one of the best in the world. Silva, though, will prove a tough act to follow.'

b'By Reuters'
b'(Reuters) - Manchester City skipper Vincent Kompany said diversity in club boardrooms and institutions of power could help in tackling racism in soccer more effectively, rather than just punishing individual offenders.'
b'"The upturn in racist abuse is worrying but at the same time it\'s something that is good to be discussed so much, to ask ourselves the right questions," Kompany told Sky Sports.'
b"Earlier this season, Kompany's team mate Raheem Sterling accused sections of the British media of fuelling the problem with a negative portrayal of young black players."
b"Sterling also encountered racist abuse during England's Euro 2020 qualifier in Montenegro in March, while there have been other cases in English soccer in recent months."
b'Arsenal launched an investigation into racist abuse suffered by Napoli defender Kalidou Koulibaly during their Europa League victory on Thursday.'
b"Three Chelsea fans were stopped from entering Slavia Prague's stadium for Thursday's Europa League game after a video of a racist chant about Liverpool's Egypt international Mohamed Salah circulated on social media."
b'However, Kompany said the focus should not lie only on individuals who directed abuse at players.'
b'"The issue is a little bit deeper. I look at boardrooms, I look at mechanisms of power... and I don\'t see a lot of diversity in that," the Belgian added.'
b'"When you ask for them to come up with policies to change the situation, you wonder whether the constitution of those boardrooms are capable of coming up with the appropriate solution.'
b'"I would like to see more people of a diverse background actually being the bosses, editors-in-chief, the people that actually decide on what the public agenda is.'
b'"I think that would make a big, big difference and would have a much bigger impact than just a punishment of individuals who probably carry a lot of their own problems on the table when they come to the stadiums."'
b' (Reporting by Shrivathsa Sridhar in Bengaluru; editing by Clare Fallon)'
